CODING APPENDIX.1

CA1.a Billig Diagram Plotter

Filename: billig_diagram.m


1 function [delta_H_fluid_vec,T_hot_fluid_vec, ...
2 T_cold_fluid_vec] = ...
3 billig_diagram(hot_fluid_str,P_hot_fluid, ...
4 cold_fluid_str,P_cold_fluid, ...
5 cold_fluid_scaling_factor, ...
6 delta_H_min,delta_H_max,num_delta_H, ...
7 plot_diagram, ...
8 give_condensation_ratio)
9 %
10 % This function takes, as input, the parameters describing two fluids (the
11 % hot fluid and the cold fluid) that are being fed into a counterflow heat
12 % exchanger. It then returns, as output, a Billig diagram, which plots
13 % the fluids' enthalpy changes on the x axis, and the fluids'
14 % temperatures on the y axis.
15 %
16 % In a physically realistic heat exchange system, the plot of the hot
17 % fluid's T(delta H) will always be above the cold fluid's T(delta H).
18 %
19 % The input terms are
20 %
21 % hot_fluid_str = ; P_hot_fluid = ;
22 % cold_fluid_str = ; P_cold_fluid = ;
23 % cold_fluid_scaling_factor = ;
24 % delta_H_min = ; delta_H_max= ; num_delta_H = ;
25 % plot_diagram = ;
26 %
27 % where
28 %
29 % hot_fluid_str = the string specifiying which fluid
30 % or mixture is to be used as the
31 % hot fluid in the subsequent
32 % calculations.
33 % NOTE:
34 % for this routine to work correctly,
35 % mixtures must be specified by a
36 % .mix
37 % ending, and pure fluids must
38 % be specified by a
39 % .fld
40 % ending;
41 %
42 % P_hot_fluid = the constant pressure (in kPa) the
43 % hot fluid is to be held at during
44 % its trip through the counterflow
45 % heat exchanger;

                                         487
46 %
47 % cold_fluid_str = the string specifiying which fluid
48 % or mixture is to be used as the
49 % cold fluid in the subsequent
50 % calculations.
51 % NOTE:
52 % for this routine to work correctly,
53 % mixtures must be specified by a
54 % .mix
55 % ending, and pure fluids must
56 % be specified by a
57 % .fld
58 % ending;
59 %
60 % P_cold_fluid = the constant pressure (in kPa) the
61 % cold fluid is to be held at during
62 % its trip through the counterflow
63 % heat exchanger;
64 %
65 % cold_fluid_scaling_factor = the factor by which the mass flux
66 % of cold fluid needs to be scaled up
67 % or down to properly absorb enthalpy
68 % from the hot fluid.
69 % EXAMPLE:
70 % Since 13.76 kilograms of air can be
71 % liquefied by 1 kilogram of
72 % parahydrogen, the cold fluid
73 % scaling factor will be
74 % 1/13.76
75 % whenever air is the hot fluid
76 % and parahydrogen is the cold fluid;
77 %
78 % delta_H_min = the minimum enthalpy change to be
79 % used during the calculation of the
80 % Billig diagram;
81 %
82 % delta_H_max = the maximum enthalpy change to be
83 % used during the calculation of the
84 % Billig diagram;
85 %
86 % num_delta_H = the number of enthalpy changes to
87 % be used during the calculation of
88 % the Billig diagram;
89 %
90 % plot_diagram = the truth value of whether or not
91 % the Billig diagram is to be plotted
92 % by the routine;
93 %
94 % and
95 %
96 % give_condensation_ratio = the truth value of whether or not
97 % the condensation ratio (i.e. the
98 % reciprocal of the cold fluid
99 % scaling factor) is to be plotted
100 % by the routine;
101 %
102 % Usage:
103 %
                                       488

CA1.b Cool Down Air to Vapor Stagnation Temperature Enthalpy Change

integrate_precooled_air_Cp.m



                                       493
1 function [T_air_sat_vapor_vec,delta_H_air_vec,Cp_air_mat] =
integrate_precooled_air_Cp
(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec,T_offset)
2 % This function is meant to answer the following question:
3 %
4 % Consider 1 kilogram of precooled air entering a cryogenic heat
5 % exchanger at some pressure. It is then cooled down to the vapor
6 % saturation temperature of air, while being held at that initial
7 % pressure. What enthalpy change is needed to make this happen?
8 %
9 % Usage:
10 %
11 % [T_air_sat_vapor_vec,delta_H_air_vec,Cp_air_mat]...
12 % = integrate_precooled_air_Cp(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec,T_offset) ;
13
14 % Perform an inital validation check of the input vectors.
15
16 if max(size(T_air_init_vec))~=max(size(P_air_init_vec))
17 error( 'The air temperature and air pressure vectors must have the same
length.' )
18 else
19 end
20
21 % Make a note of the current directory, then move to the REFPROP directory
22 % for the following calculations.
23
24 WD = pwd ;
25
26 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
27
28 % Perform an initial validation check of the pressure vector.
29
30 P_critical_air = refpropm( 'P','C',0,' ',0,'nitrogen'
,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557,
0.012700,0.2316]) ;
31
32 if max(P_air_init_vec) >= P_critical_air
33 error( 'The maximum pressure of the air must be below its critical pressure.' )
34 else
35 end
36
37 % Initialize the data output vectors.
38
39 T_air_sat_vapor_vec = zeros(1,max(size(P_air_init_vec))) ;
40
41 delta_H_air_vec = zeros(1,max(size(P_air_init_vec))) ;
42
43 % Break the integration range for each run down into a constant number of
44 % temperature divisions.
45
46 num_divisions = 100 ;
47
48 Cp_air_mat = zeros(max(size(P_air_init_vec)),num_divisions) ;
49
50 start_inspection_at_num = 1857 ;
51
52 % Initialize the figure that will be used to provide graphical output of
53 % the Cp values for air.
                                       494
54
55 figure
56 hold on
57 grid
58 xlabel( 'Integration Range Temperature (K)' )
59 ylabel( 'Cp (J/(kg K))' )
60
61 % For each air pressure...
62 for P_air_itr = 1:1:max(size(P_air_init_vec))
63
64 if mod(P_air_itr,100)==0
65 formatSpec = 'iteration number %0.0f' ;
66 disp( ' ')
67 disp( ' ')
68 fprintf(formatSpec,P_air_itr) ;
69 else
70 end
71
72 % ...Determine what the corresponding saturated air vapor temperature
73 % would be.
74
75 T_air_sat_vapor = refpropm( 'T','P',P_air_init_vec(1,P_air_itr), 'Q',
1,'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
76
77 T_air_sat_vapor_vec(1,P_air_itr) = T_air_sat_vapor_vec(1,P_air_itr) +
T_air_sat_vapor ;
78
79 % Use the initial air temperature, and the saturated vapor temperature, to
80 % construct the vector of air temperature values that the Cp of air needs
81 % to be integrated over.
82
83 %T_offset = 1 ;
84
85 T_air_final = T_air_sat_vapor + T_offset ;
86
87 T_air_init = T_air_init_vec(1,P_air_itr) ;
88
89 T_air_integral_vec = T_air_init : ( T_air_final - T_air_init ) / (
num_divisions - 1 ) :
T_air_final ;
90
91 % For each one of these temperatures, return the Cp of air.
92
93 Cp_air_vec = zeros(1,num_divisions) ;
94
95 for Cp_itr = 1:1:num_divisions
96
97 Q_current = refpropm( 'Q','T',T_air_integral_vec(1,Cp_itr),
'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
P_air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
98
99 % The next if-else-end statement is to return internal results for
100 % validation. Comment this section out if it is not needed.
101
102 if P_air_itr>=start_inspection_at_num
103 %formatSpec1 = 'Pressure iteration number %0.0f' ;
104 %disp(' ')
105 %fprintf(formatSpec1,P_air_itr) ;
                                       495
106
107 %formatSpec2 = 'Cp iteration number %0.0f' ;
108 %disp(' ')
109 %fprintf(formatSpec2,Cp_itr) ;
110
111 %Q_current =
refpropm('Q','T',T_air_integral_vec(1,Cp_itr),'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
P_air_itr),'nitrogen','argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
112
113 %formatSpec3 = ' The current temperature is %3.4f K.' ;

115 %fprintf(formatSpec3,T_air_integral_vec(1,Cp_itr)) ;

P_air_init_vec(1,P_air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557,
0.012700,0.2316]) ;

144 disp( ' ')

146 end

148 else
149 end
150
151 if Q_current > 1
152 Cp_new = refpropm( 'C','T',T_air_integral_vec(1,Cp_itr), 'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
P_air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]);
153 else
154 Cp_new = refpropm( 'C','T',(T_air_integral_vec(1,Cp_itr)+T_offset), 'P',
P_air_init_vec(1,P_air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557,
0.012700,0.2316]);
155 %error('A phase transition is occurring; Cp cannot be calculated.')
156 end
                                       496
157
158 Cp_air_vec(1,Cp_itr) = Cp_air_vec(1,Cp_itr) + Cp_new ;
159
160 %delta_Cp = Cp_new - Cp_old ;
161
162 %Cp_old = Cp_new ;
163
164 % The next if-else-end statement is to return internal results for
165 % validation. Comment this section out if it is not needed.
166
167 if P_air_itr>=start_inspection_at_num
168 formatSpec4 = ' The current Cp is is %4.4f J/(kg K).' ;
169 fprintf(formatSpec4,Cp_air_vec(1,Cp_itr)) ;
170 disp( ' ')
171 else
172 end
173
174 end
175
176 Cp_air_mat(P_air_itr,:) = Cp_air_mat(P_air_itr,:) + Cp_air_vec ;
177
178 plot(T_air_integral_vec,Cp_air_vec)
179
180 % Integrate the Cp values over the specified temperature range. This
181 % will yield the change in enthalpy.
182
183 delta_H_air_vec(1,P_air_itr) = delta_H_air_vec(1,P_air_itr) +
trapz(T_air_integral_vec,
Cp_air_vec) ;
184
185 end
186
187 disp( ' ')
188 disp( ' ')

CA1.c Find Temperature for Given Enthalpies and Pressures

Filename: find_T_given_P_for_H.m


1 function [H_vec,P_vec,T_mat] ...
2 = find_T_given_P_for_H(H_min,H_max,num_H, ...
3 P_min,P_max,num_P)
4 %
5 % This function takes, as input, a series of enthalpies and pressures
6 % of dry air.
7 % It will then return, as output, the temperatures that
8 % correspond to each combination of enthalpy and pressure.
                                       497
9 %
10 % The input terms are
11 % H_min = ; H_max = ; num_H = ;
12 % P_min = ; P_max = ; num_P = ;
13 % where
14 %
15 % H_min = the minimum enthalpy (in J/kg) that the dry air will
16 % experience;
17 %
18 % H_max = the maximum enthalpy (in J/kg) that the dry air will
19 % experience;
20 %
21 % num_H = the number of enthalpy values that will be examined for
22 % dry air, over the range from H_min to H_max;
23 %
24 % P_min = the minimum pressure (in kPa) that the dry air will
25 % experience;
26 %
27 % P_max = the maximum pressure (in kPa) that the dry air will
28 % experience;
29 %
30 % num_P = the number of pressure values that will be examined for
31 % dry air, over the range from P_min to P_max.
32 %
33 % The output terms are
34 % [H_vec,P_vec,T_mat]
35 % where
36 %
37 % H_vec = a column vector containing the specified enthalpy values;
38 %
39 % P_vec = a row vector containing the specified pressure values;
40 %
41 % T_mat = a matrix where each row represents an enthalpy value,
42 % each column represents a pressure value, and each
43 % (row,column) entry represents the corresponding
44 % absolute temperature of dry air in K.
45 %
46 % Usage:
47 %
48 % [H_vec,P_vec,T_mat] ...
49 % = find_T_given_P_for_H(H_min,H_max,num_H,...
50 % P_min,P_max,num_P);
51
52 H_vec = H_min:(H_max - H_min)/(num_H-1):H_max ;
53
54 H_vec = H_vec' ;
55
56 P_vec = P_min:(P_max - P_min)/(num_P-1):P_max ;
57
58 T_mat = zeros(num_H,num_P) ;
59
60 % For each enthalpy...
61 for H_itr = 1:1:num_H
62 % ...iterate across the range of pressures.
63 for P_itr = 1:1:num_P
64 % Find the temperature that corresponds to the current enthalpy at
65 % the current pressure. Enter that value into the temperature
66 % matrix.
                                       498
67
68 T_mat(H_itr,P_itr) = T_mat(H_itr,P_itr) + refpropm( 'T','H',H_vec(H_itr,1),
'P',P_vec(1,
P_itr),'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
69
70 end
71 end
72
73 end

CA1.d Mach Number at Altitude Finder

Filename: MachCalc2.m


1 function [ Machvec ] = MachCalc2( vvec,Altvec )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ Machvec ] = MachCalc2( vvec,Altvec )
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to take a series of velocities
8 % in (m/s) over a corresponding range of altitudes in m, and return the
9 % Mach numbers corresponding to these values.
10 %
11 % This routine calls the non-Matlab subroutines refpropm and TempAltCS6.
12 %
13 % The subroutine TempAltCS6 requires calculation of
14 % atmospheric properties using tabular data, generated using the
15 % parameters of US Standard Atmosphere 1976.
16
17 % Hand Altvec's values off to an internal variable.
18
19 Altvec2=[];
20 Altvec2=Altvec;
21
22 %Find size of vectors
23 numval = max(size(Altvec2));
24
25 %Set up speed of sound vector
26 C=ones(1,numval);
27
28 for i = 1:1:numval
29 C(1,i)=C(1,i).*refpropm( 'A','T',TempAltCS6(Altvec2(1,i)), 'P',
101.325,'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]);
30 end
31
32 Machvec=vvec./C;
33 end
34




                                       499
CA1.e Intake Heat Flux Calculator

Filename: HFcalc2.m


1 function [ heatflux ] = HFcalc2( A,altvec,vvec,Tcool )
2 % Usage:
3 %
4 % [ heatflux ] = HFcalc2( A,altvec,vvec,Tcool )
5 %
6 % Consider the case of an aircraft, with a constant intake area A, flying
7 % through Earth's atmosphere at an altitude h, and at a velocity v. This
8 % aircraft takes all air going through its intake, at a stagnation
9 % temperature Tstag, and cools it down to a temperature Tcool, all at the
10 % constant stagnation pressure Pstag.
11 % The question then becomes--what amount of heat energy must be
12 % rejected every second, under these circumstances, to accomplish such
13 % cooling?
14 % The purpose of this function is to answer the preceding question.
15 % This function assumes that all intake air is completely dry, and also
16 % assumes that no phase changes are encountered as the air is cooled.
17 %
18 % The input terms are
19 % A=;altvec=;vvec=;Tcool=;
20 % where
21 % A=the fixed intake area in m^2;
22 % altvec=the vector of altitude values, in m, over which the aircraft
23 % flies;
24 % vvec=the vector of velocities, in m/s, corresponding to those same
25 % altitudes in altvec
26 % Tcool=the temperature to which the incoming air is to be cooled.
27 %
28 % This program calls the non-Matlab subroutines TempAltCS6, BarForm2,
29 % MachCalc2, refpropm, StagTemp, and StagPress.
30 %
31 % The subroutines TempAltCS6, BarForm2, and MachCalc2 all make reference
32 % to external data tables. Generation of these tables requires
33 % calculation of atmospheric properties using US Standard Atmosphere 1976.
34
35 % Hand off the values in altvec to an internal variable.
36 altvec2=[];
37 altvec2=altvec;
38
39 % Calculate the atmospheric temperature at the specified altitude.
40
41 tempvec=TempAltCS6( altvec2 );
42
43 %load alttemp
44
45 %tempvec=spline(alttemp(:,1)',alttemp(:,2)',altvec);
46
47 % Calculate the atmospheric pressure at the specified altitude.
48
49 pressvec= BarForm2( altvec2 );
50
51 %load altpress
52
                                       500
53 %pressvec=spline(altpress(:,1)',altpress(:,2)',altvec);
54
55 % Calculate the effective mach number using the information on velocity,
56 % pressure and temperature.
57
58 machvec = MachCalc2( vvec,altvec2 );
59
60 % Generate the vector of gamma values corresponding to the temperature and
61 % pressure values previously obtained.
62
63 gammavec=zeros(1,max(size(tempvec)));
64
65 for gammait=1:max(size(tempvec))
66 gammavec(1,gammait)=gammavec(1,gammait)+refpropm( 'K','T',tempvec(1,gammait),
'P',pressvec
(1,gammait), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]);
67 end
68
69 % Calculate the stagnation temperature at the specified atmospheric
70 % temperature, atmospheric pressure and velocity.
71
72 Tstagvec=StagTemp( tempvec,gammavec,machvec );
73
74 % Calculate the stagnation pressure at the specified atmospheric
75 % temperature, atmospheric pressure and velocity.
76
77 Pstagvec= StagPress(pressvec,gammavec,machvec);
78
79 % Calculate the density of the gas corresponding to each stagnation temperature
and
80 % pressure combination.
81
82 mMair=0.0289644;
83 R=8.314472; % units of m^3?Pa?K^?1?mol^?1
84
85 rhovec = (mMair.*Pstagvec)./(R.*Tstagvec);
86
87 % Integrate numerically across the differential heat fluxes from Tstag to
88 % Tcool. This will be done using Simpson's quadrature.
89
90 areaflux=zeros(1,max(size(Pstagvec)));
91
92 for iter=1:max(size(Pstagvec))
93 areaflux(1,iter)=areaflux(1,iter) + quad(@(T)HFntgrnd(
T,Pstagvec(1,iter),rhovec(1,iter),
vvec(1,iter)),Tstagvec(1,iter),Tcool);
94 end
95
96 % Multiply this integral by the intake area.
97
98 heatflux=areaflux.*A;
99
100 end
101




                                       501
CA1.f Differential Heat Flux Per Unit Area

Filename: HFntgrnd.m


1 function [ dheatfluxvec ] = HFntgrnd( Tvec,Pstag,rhostag,vvec )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ dheatfluxvec ] = HFntgrnd( Tvec,Pstag,rhostag,vvec )
6 %
7 % This function will give the differential heat flux per unit area per
8 % temperature unit(in W/(m^2 * K)) for an aircraft that is flying through
9 % Earth's atmosphere, collecting air through an intake of fixed size, and
10 % cooling that air to a specified temperature in a constant-pressure
11 % process.
12 %
13 % Input terms:
14 % Tvec=;Pvec=;rhovec=;vvec=;
15 % where
16 % Tvec=a vector of temperature values. In the integration, these will
17 % extend from the stagnation temperature to the cooled-air temperature;
18 % Pstag=the stagnation pressure;
19 % rhovec=the density value corresponding to Pstag;
20 % and
21 % v=the absolute velocity (in m/s) at which the stagnation
22 % temperature and pressure are observed.
23
24 dheatfluxvec=zeros(1,max(size(Tvec)));
25 %
26 for i=1:max(size(Tvec))
27 Cp=refpropm( 'C','T',Tvec(1,i), 'P',Pstag,'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557,
0.012700,0.2316]);
28 dheatfluxvec(1,i)= dheatfluxvec(1,i)+(Cp.*rhostag.*vvec);
29 end
30
31 end
32
33




                                       502
CA1.g Keep Range Only Function

Filename: kro.m


1 function [ newvec ] = kro( oldvec,lowend,equallow,highend,equalhigh )
2 %
3 % Usage: [ newvec ] = kro( oldvec,lowend,equallow,highend,equalhigh )
4 %
5 % The purpose of this kro (Keep Range Only) function is to take a vector,
6 % return a new
7 % vector the same size as the old one. This is done in a manner such that
8 % only the values of the old vector that are within a specified range
9 % will be preserved. These values will be have the same indices in the
10 % new vector that they had in the old vector. All other parts of the new
11 % vector will be set to zero.
12 %
13 % Input terms:
14 % oldvec = the vector with the input values;
15 % lowend = the lowest allowable end of the desired range;
16 % equallow = 1 if the values to be kept may equal the low end of the desired
range,
17 % =0 if the values to be kept may NOT equal the low end of the
18 % desired range;
19 % highend = the highest allowable end of the desired range;
20 % equalhigh = 1 if the values to be kept may equal the high end of the desired
range,
21 % =0 if the values to be kept may NOT equal the high end of the
22 % desired range;
23
24 %Start by finding everything in oldvec above or at the specified low end.
25
26 if equallow==1
27 aboveind=find(oldvec>=lowend);
28 else
29 aboveind=find(oldvec>lowend);
30 end
31
32 %Create a vector of zeros the same size as oldvec. The preserved values
33 %will ultimately be entered into this vector.
34
35 valvec1=zeros(1,max(size(oldvec)));
36
37 %Enter the values that are above (or at) the specified lower limit.
38 for i=1:1:max(size(aboveind))
39 valvec1(1,aboveind(i)) = valvec1(1,aboveind(i))+oldvec(1,aboveind(i));
40 end
41
42 %valvec1
43
44 %Now, find everything in valvec that is below or at the specified high end.
45
46 if equalhigh==1
47 belowind=find(oldvec<=highend);
48 else
49 belowind=find(oldvec<highend);
50 end
                                       503
51
52 %Create a vector of zeros the same size as oldvec. The preserved values
53 %from valvec1 will ultimately be entered into this vector.
54
55 valvec2=zeros(1,max(size(oldvec)));
56
57 %valvec1(1,belowind)
58
59 %Enter the values that are above (or at) the specified lower limit.
60 for j=1:1:max(size(belowind))
61 valvec2(1,belowind(j)) = valvec2(1,belowind(j))+valvec1(1,belowind(j));
62 end
63
64 %valvec2
65
66 % The surviving values are now entered into newvec.
67 newvec=valvec2;
68
69 end
70




CA1.h Condensation Ratio Performance Calculator

Filename: lace_cr_calc_2.m


1 function [v_vehicle_vec,Mach_num_vec, ...
2 P_stag_vec,T_stag_vec, ...
3 condensation_ratio_vec] = lace_cr_calc_2(alt_vec,intake_area,air_mass_flux)
4 %
5 % This function is meant to calculate the performance of an air
6 % collection and enrichment (ACES) system, within a flight vehicle, over
7 % a series of altitudes and speeds.
8 %
9 % An ACES system functions in the following manner:
10 % 1) Intake air flows through a first heat exchanger, where it is
11 % precooled by nitrogen gas.
12 % 2) This precooled air flows into a second heat exchanger, where it
13 % is further cooled and liquefied by parahydrogen.
14 % 3) The liquefied air is separated into its nitrogen and oxygen
15 % components.
16 % 4) The oxygen component of the air, along with the parahydrogen
17 % from step 2), is sent to a rocket engine and burned.
18 % 5) The nitrogen component of the air is sent through the first
19 % heat exchanger, then dumped overboard.
20 %
21 % The input terms are
22 % alt_vec = ; intake_area = ; air_mass_flux = ;
23 %
24 % where
25 %
26 % alt_vec = the vector of altitudes, in m, that the flight
27 % vehicle is to traverse:
28 %
29 % intake_area = the fixed intake area, in m^2, that the flight
                                       504
30 % vehicle has overall;
31 %
32 % and
33 %
34 % air_mass_flux = the fixed rate of air intake, in kg / s, that
35 % the flight vehicle is to sustain.
36 %
37 % The output terms are
38 %
39 % v_vehicle_vec = the vector of absolute vehicle speeds,
40 % in meters per second, required to
41 % maintain a constant mass flux of intake
42 % air across the specified altitudes;
43 %
44 % Mach_num_vec = the vector of corresponding Mach
45 % numbers experienced by the vehicle;
46 %
47 % P_stag_vec = the vector of stagnation pressures, in
48 % Pa, experienced by the vehicle during
49 % its flight;
50 %
51 % T_stag_vec = the vector of stagnation temperatures,
52 % in Kelvin, experienced by the vehicle
53 % during its flight;
54 %
55 % T_intermediate_vec = the vector of "intermediate"
56 % temperatures, in Kelvin, the intake air
57 % will have after being passed through
58 % the first, air-to-nitrogen counterflow
59 % heat exchanger;
60 %
61 % and
62 %
63 % condensation_ratio_vec = the vector of condensation ratios
64 % for each set of flight conditions.
65 % NOTE: condensation ratio is defined as
66 % the kilograms of air liquefied, over
67 % the kilograms of parahydrogen used to
68 % liquefy that air,
69 %
70 %
71 % Usage:
72 %
73 % [v_vehicle_vec,Mach_num_vec,...
74 % P_stag_vec,T_stag_vec,...
75 % condensation_ratio_vec] = lace_cr_calc_2(alt_vec,intake_area,air_mass_flux)
76
77 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
78 %
79 % This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines directly:
80 % const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2
81 % MachCalc3
82 % StagTemp
83 % StagPress
84 % liquefy_air
85 % integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_2
86 %
87 % In addition, the subroutine refpropm is called indirectly, as the above
                                       505
88 % subroutines make calls to REFPROP.
89
90 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
91 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
92 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
93 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
94 %
95 % Calculate Properties of Intake Air
96 %
97 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
98 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
99 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
100 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
101
102 % Start by entering phyical properties for air.
103 % Note: for dry air...
104 % Mass Fractions
105 % nitrogen = 0.7557
106 % argon = 0.012700
107 % oxygen = 0.2316
108 %
109 % Mole Fractions
110 % nitrogen = 0.7812
111 % argon = 0.0092065
112 % oxygen = 0.2096
113
114 gamma = 1.4 ; %air
115
116 % For each altitude the vehicle is to fly within, calculate the absolute
117 % velocity needed to ensure the correct mass flux, along with the
118 % freestream air opressures and temperatures that correspond to these
119 % altitudes.
120
121 [T_inf_vec,P_inf_vec,v_vehicle_vec] =
const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2(alt_vec,intake_area,
air_mass_flux) ;
122
123 disp( ' ')
124 disp( 'Flight profile calculations done' )
125
126 % Calculate the corresponding Mach numbers.
127
128 [ Mach_num_vec ] = MachCalc3( v_vehicle_vec,alt_vec ) ;
129
130 disp( ' ')
131 disp( 'Mach Number calculations done' )
132
133 % Calculate the corresponding stagnation temperatures and pressures.
134
135 [ T_stag_vec ] = StagTemp( T_inf_vec,gamma,Mach_num_vec ) ;
136
137 T_air_init_vec = T_stag_vec ;
138
139 [ P_stag_vec ] = StagPress( P_inf_vec,gamma,Mach_num_vec) ;
140
141 disp( ' ')
142 disp( 'Stagnation calculations done' )
143
                                       506
144 % Since the pressures from the previous routines are returned in terms of
145 % Pa, they need to be converted to kPa to work in the following routines
146 % (since they will call REFPROP via refpropm, which needs pressures to be
147 % in units of kPa).
148
149 P_air_init_vec = P_stag_vec / 1000 ;
150
151 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
152 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
153 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
154 %
155 % Precool and Liquefy Air
156 %
157 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
158 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
159 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
160
161 % For 1 kg of air at stagnation pressure and temperature, calculate how
162 % much enthalpy change will be required to further cool that air to its
163 % saturated vapor temperature, then liquefy it.
164
165 [delta_H_to_liquefy_intake_air_vec] =
liquefy_air(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec) ;
166
167 disp( ' ')
168 disp( 'Air liquefaction calculations done' )
169
170 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
171 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
172 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
173 % 2222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222
174 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
175 %
176 % Calculate Para-H2 Requirements
177 %
178 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
179 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
180 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
181 % 2222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222
182 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
183
184 % Calculate how many kilograms of parahydrogen, at its critical pressure,
185 % would be required to absorb that change in enthalpy.
186 % NOTE: since the Cp of parahydrogen varies widely over its temperature
187 % range, a numerical integration is required to get this number.
188
189 % First, calculate the change in the enthalpy of 1 kg of parahydrogen at
190 % its critical pressure, as the parahydrogen is warmed from its critical
191 % temperature to the temperature of the stagnated intake air.
192
193 T_offset = 1 ;
194
195 [delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec] =
integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_2(T_air_init_vec,T_offset) ;
196
197 disp( ' ')
198 disp( 'Integration of para-H2 Cp over air T range done' )
199
                                       507
200 % To find how many kilograms of parahydrogen will actually be needed, take
201 % the absolute value of the enthalpy change 1 kg of precooled air has to
202 % undergo to get liquefied in the air heat exchanger, then divide that by
203 % the absolute value of the enthalpy change 1 kg of the parahydrogen will
204 % experience over the temperature range of the heat exchanger.
205 %
206 % EXAMPLE: if 1 kg of air needs to lose 40,000 J of enthalpy to get
207 % liquefied within the air-parahydrogen heat exchanger, and 1 kg of para-
208 % hydrogen will absorb 200,000 J of enthalpy over the temperature range of
209 % that same heat exchanger, it follows that
210 %
211 % 40,000 / 200,000 = 0.20000
212 %
213 % kg of parahydrogen would be needed to accomplish this process.
214
215 mass_paraH2_vec = abs(delta_H_to_liquefy_intake_air_vec) ./
abs(delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec) ;
216
217 % Calculate the corresponding condensation ratio.
218
219 condensation_ratio_vec = 1./mass_paraH2_vec ;
220
221 end
222




CA1.i Animated Billig Plotter

billig_anim_3.m


1 function [delta_H_fluid_vec,T_hot_fluid_vec, ...
2 T_cold_fluid_mat] = ...
3 billig_anim_3(hot_fluid_str,P_hot_fluid, ...
4 cold_fluid_str,P_cold_fluid, ...
5 condensation_ratio_vec, ...
6 delta_H_min,delta_H_max,num_delta_H, ...
7 animate_diagram, ...
8 condensation_ratio_in_legend)
9
10 % This function takes, as input, the parameters describing two fluids (the
11 % hot fluid and the cold fluid) that are being fed into a counterflow heat
12 % exchanger. It then returns, as output, a Billig diagram, which plots
13 % the fluids' enthalpy changes on the x axis, and the fluids'
14 % temperatures on the y axis.
15 %
16 % In a physically realistic heat exchange system, the plot of the hot
17 % fluid's T(delta H) will always be above the cold fluid's T(delta H).
18 %
19 % The input terms are
20 %
21 % hot_fluid_str = ; P_hot_fluid = ;
22 % cold_fluid_str = ; P_cold_fluid = ;
23 % condensation_ratio_vec = ;
24 % delta_H_min = ; delta_H_max= ; num_delta_H = ;
25 % plot_diagram = ;
                                       508
26 % condensation_ratio_in_legend = ;
27 %
28 % where
29 %
30 % hot_fluid_str = the string specifiying which fluid
31 % or mixture is to be used as the
32 % hot fluid in the subsequent
33 % calculations.
34 % NOTE:
35 % for this routine to work correctly,
36 % mixtures must be specified by a
37 % .mix
38 % ending, and pure fluids must
39 % be specified by a
40 % .fld
41 % ending;
42 %
43 % P_hot_fluid = the constant pressure (in kPa) the
44 % hot fluid is to be held at during
45 % its trip through the counterflow
46 % heat exchanger;
47 %
48 % cold_fluid_str = the string specifiying which fluid
49 % or mixture is to be used as the
50 % cold fluid in the subsequent
51 % calculations.
52 % NOTE:
53 % for this routine to work correctly,
54 % mixtures must be specified by a
55 % .mix
56 % ending, and pure fluids must
57 % be specified by a
58 % .fld
59 % ending;
60 %
61 % P_cold_fluid = the constant pressure (in kPa) the
62 % cold fluid is to be held at during
63 % its trip through the counterflow
64 % heat exchanger;
65 %
66 % condensation_ratio = the factor by which the mass flux
67 % of cold fluid needs to be scaled up
68 % or down to properly absorb enthalpy
69 % from the hot fluid.
70 % EXAMPLE:
71 % Since 13.76 kilograms of air can be
72 % liquefied by 1 kilogram of
73 % parahydrogen, the condensation
74 % ratio will be
75 % 13.76
76 % whenever air is the hot fluid
77 % and parahydrogen is the cold fluid;
78 %
79 % delta_H_min = the minimum enthalpy change to be
80 % used during the calculation of the
81 % Billig diagram;
82 %
83 % delta_H_max = the maximum enthalpy change to be
                                       509
84 % used during the calculation of the
85 % Billig diagram;
86 %
87 % num_delta_H = the number of enthalpy changes to
88 % be used during the calculation of
89 % the Billig diagram;
90 %
91 % plot_diagram = the truth value of whether or not
92 % the Billig diagram is to be plotted
93 % by the routine;
94 %
95 % and
96 %
97 % condensation_ratio_in_legend= the truth value of whether or not
98 % the condensation ratio (i.e. the
99 % reciprocal of the cold fluid
100 % scaling factor) is to be plotted
101 % by the routine;
102 %
103 % Usage:
104 %
105 % [delta_H_fluid_vec,T_hot_fluid_vec,...
106 % T_cold_fluid_mat] = ...
107 % billig_anim_3(hot_fluid_str,P_hot_fluid,...
108 % cold_fluid_str,P_cold_fluid,...
109 % condensation_ratio_vec,...
110 % delta_H_min,delta_H_max,num_delta_H,...
111 % animate_diagram,...
112 % condensation_ratio_in_legend);
113
114 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
115 %
116 % This routine calls the non-MATLAB subroutine refpropm.
117
118 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
119 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
120 %
121 % Validate Input
122 %
123 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
124 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
125
126 % Do basic validation on the data input before proceeding.
127
128 % First, confirm if the fluids' identity strings are indeed strings.
129
130 if ischar(hot_fluid_str) == 1
131 if ischar(cold_fluid_str) == 1
132 else
133 error( 'The name of the cold fluid fluid must be a string of characters.' )
134 end
135 else
136 error( 'The name of the hot fluid must be a string of characters.' )
137 end
138
139 % Second, confirm that the hot fluid's string is correctly identified as a
140 % pure fluid or mixture.
141
                                       510
142 % If the hot fluid is *NOT* ID'd as a pure fluid...
143 if ~contains(hot_fluid_str, '.fld')
144 % ...check to see that it is identified as a mixture.
145
146 % If the hot fluid is *NOT* ID'd as a mixture...
147 if ~contains(hot_fluid_str, '.mix')
148 error( 'The hot fluid must be either a pure fluid (.fld) or a mixture (.mix).'
)
149 else
150 end
151
152 else
153 end
154
155 % If the cold fluid is *NOT* ID'd as a pure fluid...
156 if ~contains(cold_fluid_str, '.fld')
157 % ...check to see that it is identified as a mixture.
158
159 % If the cold fluid is also *NOT* ID'd as a mixture...
160 if ~contains(cold_fluid_str, '.mix')
161 error( 'The cold fluid must be either a pure fluid (.fld) or a mixture
(.mix).' )
162 else
163 end
164
165 else
166 end
167

:
delta_H_max ;

                                       511

'T','H',
delta_H_fluid_vec(1,delta_H_itr), 'P',P_hot_fluid,hot_fluid_str) ;

('T','H',delta_H_fluid_vec(1,delta_H_itr), 'P',P_hot_fluid,hot_fluid_str) ;

)

refpropm( 'T','H',delta_H_fluid_vec(1,delta_H_itr)*condensation_ratio,
'P',P_cold_fluid,
cold_fluid_str) ;

refpropm( 'T','H',delta_H_fluid_vec(1,delta_H_itr)*condensation_ratio,
'P',P_cold_fluid,
cold_fluid_str) ;

mix).')

CA1.j ACES Code Overview

aces_cr_calc_5.m (Coding Appendix CA1.k)


This is the front end for doing all the calculations we are interested in for ACES.

   1) Its first step is to calculate the basic parameters of the flight path the vehicle will

       take. This is done via calls to the subroutines…

       const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m (Coding Appendix CA1.l)


               This subroutine calculates the actual flight profile an air-breathing vehicle

               must take to ingest a constant mass flux of air, as it flies through Earth’s

               atmosphere.

               const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m makes calls to the non-

               MATLAB subroutines…

       TempAltCS6.m (Coding Appendix CA1.m)


               This subroutine does tabular lookup of atmospheric temperature data using

               U.S. Standard Atmosphere 1976 parameters, then performs splining to

               generate any unavailable values. TempAltCS6.m makes calls to the

               following MATLAB data file:

                                       alttemp2.mat

       BarForm2.m (Coding Appendix CA1.n)


               This subroutine tabular lookup of atmospheric pressure data using U.S.

               Standard Atmosphere 1976 parameters, then performs splining to generate

                                             518
      any unavailable values. BarForm2.m makes calls to the following

      MATLAB data file:

                            altpress2.mat

MachCalc3.m (Coding Appendix CA1.o)




      This subroutine calculates the Mach numbers that correspond to the flight

      conditions (freestream temperatures & pressure, velocities) calculated by

      const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m


             MachCalc3.m makes calls to the following non-MATLAB

             subroutines:

             refpropm.m (Brown, et al. 2011) and TempAltCS6.m




StagTemp.m (Coding Appendix CA1.p)


      This subroutine generates the stagnation temperatures that correspond to

      the freestream temperatures and Mach numbers generated by

             const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m and MachCalc3.m

      respectively.

      StagTemp.m does not make calls to any additional non-

             MATLAB subroutines.

                                  519
       StagPress.m (Coding Appendix CA1.q)


               This subroutine generates the stagnation temperatures that correspond to

the            freestream pressures and Mach numbers generated by

                       const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m and MachCalc3.m

               respectively.

               StagPress.m does not make calls to any additional non-MATLAB

               subroutines.




2) The second part of this routine involves calculating the enthalpy change that has to

happen in the stagnated intake air, on a per-kilogram basis, for it to be liquefied by the

ACES system. Since this will involve two stages (precooling by the air/N 2 heat

exchanger, followed by cooling to liquefaction at the air/para-H2 heat exchanger, recall

Figure 1.25 from Chapter 1), two non-MATLAB subroutines are called…

       T_intermediate_calc_4.m (Coding Appendix CA1.r)


               This subroutine determines what the “intermediate” temperature of the

               precooled air will be after it leaves the first, air/N2 heat exchanger. In this

               heat exchanger, the 0.7557 kg of N2 extracted from liquid air are used to

               absorb heat from 1.0000 kg of stagnated intake air.

               T_intermediate_calc_4.m makes calls to the following non-

               MATLAB subroutine…

                       refpropm.m (Brown, et al. 2011)


                                             520
                               See above.

       liquefy_air.m (Coding Appendix CA1.s)


               This subroutine calculates how much enthalpy needs to be removed from

               dry air, at an initial temperature and a constant pressure, to turn it into

               saturated vapor, then liquefy it.

               liquefy_air.m makes calls to the following non-MATLAB

subroutine…

                       refpropm.m (Brown, et al. 2011)




3) The third part of this routine involves determining how much enthalpy 1 kilogram of

parahydrogen can absorb, at its critical pressure, over the temperature range of the

second, air/para-H2 heat exchanger. Once this is known, the ratio of

                         enthalpy lost by 1 kg of liquefying air
                      enthalpy absorbed by 1 kg of parahydrogen

gives the quantity of para-H2 that is actually required to liquefy air at the second heat

exchanger. Finally, the reciprocal of that parahydrogen mass gives the corresponding

condensation ratio.


                                             521
To find the enthalpy absorbed by the parahydrogen at the second heat exchanger, the

following non-MATLAB subroutine is called…

       integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_3.m (Coding Appendix CA1.t)


              This subroutine integrates the constant-pressure heat capacity of

              parahydrogen, from its “starting temperature” (i.e. a temperature that is

              offset just above the critical temperature of para-H2), to some final

              temperature (i.e. the temperature of the incoming, precooled air).

              integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_3.m makes calls to the following non

              MATLAB subroutine…

              refpropm.m (Brown, et al. 2011)




                                           522
CA1.k Frontend ACES Function

Filename: aces_cr_calc_5.m


1 function [v_vehicle_vec,Mach_num_vec, ...
2 P_stag_vec,T_stag_vec, ...
3 T_intermediate_vec, ...
4 condensation_ratio_vec] = aces_cr_calc_5(alt_vec,intake_area,air_mass_flux)
5 % This function is meant to calculate the performance of an air
6 % collection and enrichment (ACES) system, within a flight vehicle, over
7 % a series of altitudes and speeds. Results can be viewed in Chapter 1 of
8 % Ram Accelerator Design Considerations for Aerospace Engineers.
9 %
10 % An ACES system functions in the following manner:
11 % 1) Intake air flows through a first heat exchanger, where it is
12 % precooled by nitrogen gas.
13 % 2) This precooled air flows into a second heat exchanger, where it
14 % is further cooled and liquefied by parahydrogen.
15 % 3) The liquefied air is separated into its nitrogen and oxygen
16 % components.
17 % 4) The oxygen component of the air, along with the parahydrogen
18 % from step 2), is sent to a rocket engine and burned.
19 % 5) The nitrogen component of the air is sent through the first
20 % heat exchanger, then dumped overboard.
21 %
22 % The input terms are
23 % alt_vec = ; intake_area = ; air_mass_flux = ;
24 %
25 % where
26 %
27 % alt_vec = the vector of altitudes, in m, that the flight
28 % vehicle is to traverse:
29 %
30 % intake_area = the fixed intake area, in m^2, that the flight
31 % vehicle has overall;
32 %
33 % and
34 %
35 % air_mass_flux = the fixed rate of air intake, in kg / s, that
36 % the flight vehicle is to sustain.
37 %
38 % The output terms are
39 %
40 % v_vehicle_vec = the vector of absolute vehicle speeds,
41 % in meters per second, required to
42 % maintain a constant mass flux of intake
43 % air across the specified altitudes;
44 %
45 % Mach_num_vec = the vector of corresponding Mach
46 % numbers experienced by the vehicle;
47 %
48 % P_stag_vec = the vector of stagnation pressures, in
49 % Pa, experienced by the vehicle during
50 % its flight;
51 %
52 % T_stag_vec = the vector of stagnation temperatures,
                                       523
53 % in Kelvin, experienced by the vehicle
54 % during its flight;
55 %
56 % T_intermediate_vec = the vector of "intermediate"
57 % temperatures, in Kelvin, the intake air
58 % will have after being passed through
59 % the first, air-to-nitrogen counterflow
60 % heat exchanger;
61 %
62 % and
63 %
64 % condensation_ratio_vec = the vector of condensation ratios
65 % for each set of flight conditions.
66 % NOTE: condensation ratio is defined as
67 % the kilograms of air liquefied, over
68 % the kilograms of parahydrogen used to
69 % liquefy that air,
70 %
71 %
72 % Usage:
73 %
74 % [v_vehicle_vec,Mach_num_vec,...
75 % Pstag_vec,Tstag_vec,...
76 % T_intermediate_vec,...
77 % condensation_ratio_vec] = ...
78 % aces_cr_calc_5(alt_vec,intake_area,air_mass_flux) ;
79
80 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
81 %
82 % This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines directly:
83 % const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2
84 % MachCalc3
85 % StagTemp
86 % StagPress
87 % T_intermediate_calc_4
88 % liquefy_air
89 % integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_2
90 %
91 % In addition, the subroutine refpropm is called indirectly, as the above
92 % subroutines make calls to REFPROP.
93
94 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
95 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
96 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
97 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
98 %
99 % Calculate Properties of Intake Air
100 %
101 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
102 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
103 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
104 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
105
106 % Start by entering phyical properties for air.
107 % Note: for dry air...
108 % Mass Fractions
109 % nitrogen = 0.7557
110 % argon = 0.012700
                                       524
111 % oxygen = 0.2316
112 %
113 % Mole Fractions
114 % nitrogen = 0.7812
115 % argon = 0.0092065
116 % oxygen = 0.2096
117
118 gamma = 1.4 ; %AIR
119
120 % For each altitude the vehicle is to fly within, calculate the absolute
121 % velocity needed to ensure the correct mass flux, along with the
122 % freestream air opressures and temperatures that correspond to these
123 % altitudes.
124
125 [T_inf_vec,P_inf_vec,v_vehicle_vec] =
const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2(alt_vec,intake_area,
air_mass_flux) ;
126
127 disp( ' ')
128 disp( 'Flight profile calculations done' )
129
130 % Calculate the corresponding Mach numbers.
131
132 [ Mach_num_vec ] = MachCalc3( v_vehicle_vec,alt_vec ) ;
133
134 disp( ' ')
135 disp( 'Mach Number calculations done' )
136
137 % Calculate the corresponding stagnation temperatures and pressures.
138
139 [ T_stag_vec ] = StagTemp( T_inf_vec,gamma,Mach_num_vec ) ;
140
141 T_air_init_vec = T_stag_vec ;
142
143 [ P_stag_vec ] = StagPress( P_inf_vec,gamma,Mach_num_vec) ;
144
145 disp( ' ')
146 disp( 'Stagnation calculations done' )
147
148 % Since the pressures from the previous routines are returned in terms of
149 % Pa, they need to be converted to kPa to work in the following routines
150 % (since they will call REFPROP via refpropm, which needs pressures to be
151 % in units of kPa).
152
153 P_air_init_vec = P_stag_vec / 1000 ;
154
155 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
156 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
157 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
158 %
159 % Precool and Liquefy Air
160 %
161 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
162 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
163 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
164
165 % For 1 kg of air at each combination of stagnation pressure and
166 % temperature, calculate what its temperature (T_intermediate) will be when
                                       525
167 % it transfers enthalpy to 0.7557 kg of N2 in a counterflow heat exchange
168 % precooler.
169
170 [~,...
171 ~,~, ...
172 T_intermediate_vec,~] = ...
173 T_intermediate_calc_4(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec) ;
174
175 disp( ' ')
176 disp( 'Precooler calculations done' )
177
178 % For 1 kg of air at stagnation pressure and T_intermediate, calculate how
179 % much enthalpy change will be required to further cool that air to its
180 % saturated vapor temperature, then liquefy it.
181
182 [delta_H_to_liquefy_precooled_air_vec] =
liquefy_air(T_intermediate_vec,P_air_init_vec) ;
183
184 disp( ' ')
185 disp( 'Air liquefaction calculations done' )
186
187 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
188 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
189 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
190 % 2222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222
191 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
192 %
193 % Calculate Para-H2 Requirements
194 %
195 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
196 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
197 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
198 % 2222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222222
199 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
200
201 % Calculate how many kilograms of parahydrogen, at its critical pressure,
202 % would be required to absorb that change in enthalpy.
203 % NOTE: since the Cp of parahydrogen varies widely over its temperature
204 % range, a numerical integration is required to get this number.
205
206 % First, calculate the change in the enthalpy of 1 kg of parahydrogen at
207 % its critical pressure, as the parahydrogen is warmed from its critical
208 % temperature to the temperature of the incoming (precooled) air.
209
210 T_offset = 1 ;
211
212 [delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec] =
integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_2(T_intermediate_vec,T_offset) ;
213
214 disp( ' ')
215 disp( 'Integration of para-H2 Cp over air liquefaction T range done' )
216
217 % To find how many kilograms of parahydrogen will actually be needed, take
218 % the absolute value of the enthalpy change 1 kg of precooled air has to
219 % undergo to get liquefied in the air heat exchanger, then divide that by
220 % the absolute value of the enthalpy change 1 kg of the parahydrogen will
221 % experience over the temperature range of the heat exchanger.
222 %
                                       526
223 % EXAMPLE: if 1 kg of air needs to lose 40,000 J of enthalpy to get
224 % liquefied within the air-parahydrogen heat exchanger, and 1 kg of para-
225 % hydrogen will absorb 200,000 J of enthalpy over the temperature range of
226 % that same heat exchanger, it follows that
227 %
228 % 40,000 / 200,000 = 0.20000
229 %
230 % kg of parahydrogen would be needed to accomplish this process.
231
232 mass_paraH2_vec = abs(delta_H_to_liquefy_precooled_air_vec) ./
abs(delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec)
;
233
234 % Calculate the corresponding condensation ratio.
235
236 condensation_ratio_vec = 1./mass_paraH2_vec ;
237
238 end
239



CA1.l Air-Breathing Vehicle's Flight Profile

Filename: const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2.m


1 function [T_inf_vec,P_inf_vec,v_vehicle_vec] =
const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2(alt_vec,
intake_area,air_mass_flux)
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to calculate an air-breathing vehicle's
4 % speeds as a function of altitude, as the vehicle climbs hhigher and
5 % higher.
6 %
7 % Consider the case of an air-breathing vehicle ascending through Earth's
8 % atmosphere. The vehicle is adjusting its speed, as it ascends, so that
9 % the inlets of the vehicle's jet engines--which are assumed to have a
10 % constant, unvarying area--will ingest an unchanging mass of air each
11 % second.
12 %
13 % In other words, as the vehicle reaches higher altitudes, where the air
14 % density becomes lower, the vehicle will have to fly at a higher
15 % absolute speed to endure that the mass flux of air at the inlet remains
16 % constant.
17 %
18 % The input terms are
19 % alt_vec = ; intake_area = ; air_mass_flux = ;
20 %
21 % where
22 %
23 % alt_vec = the vector of altitudes, in m, that the flight
24 % vehicle is to traverse:
25 %
26 % intake_area = the fixed intake area, in m^2, that the flight
27 % vehicle has overall;
28 %

                                        527
29 % and
30 %
31 % air_mass_flux = the fixed rate of air intake, in kg / s, that
32 % the flight vehicle is to sustain.
33 %
34 % Usage:
35 %
36 % [T_inf_vec,P_inf_vec,v_vehicle_vec] = ...
37 % const_mass_flux_flight_profile_2(alt_vec,intake_area,air_mass_flux) ;
38
39
40 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
41 %
42 % This function calls the non-MATLAB subroutines
43 % TempAltCS6
44 % BarForm2
45
46 % Generate the vector of temperature values for freestream air, at all the
47 % altitudes being traversed by the flight vehicle.
48
49 T_inf_vec = TempAltCS6( alt_vec );
50
51 % Generate the vector of pressure values for freestream air, at all the
52 % altitudes being traversed by the flight vehicle.
53
54 P_inf_vec = BarForm2( alt_vec );
55
56 % Using these values, generate the freestream air densities at all of the
57 % altitudes the vehicle flies at. This will be done using an ideal gas
58 % approximation.
59
60 mM_air = 0.0289644 ;
61 R = 8.314472 ; % units of ( m^3 * Pa ) / ( K * mol )
62
63 rho_inf_vec = (mM_air.*P_inf_vec)./(R.*T_inf_vec) ;
64
65 % Using these densities as a function of altitude, calculate the
66 % corresponding vehicle speeds.
67
68 v_vehicle_vec = air_mass_flux ./ (rho_inf_vec * intake_area) ;
69
70 end
71

CA1.m Atmospheric Temperature Data Lookup

Filename: TempAltCS6.m
1 function [ Tempvec ] = TempAltCS6( altvec )
2 %
3 % Usage: [ Tempvec ] = TempAltCS6( altvec )
4 %
5 % The purpose of this function is to generate a series of temperatures
6 % for the Earth's atmosphere over a series of given altitudes, using the
7 % US Standard Atmosphere 1976 parameters. This series can then be used to
8 % construct a table of temperatures as a function of altitude. This table
9 % may then be saved as a .mat file, and used by other routines that
10 % require such data.
11 %
12 % Input terms:
13 %
14 % altvec = the vector of all altitudes above sea level, in meters,
15 % for which the temperature is to be calculated.
16 %
17 % Output terms:
18 %
19 % Tempvec = the vector of absolute temperatures, in Kelvin,
20 % corresponding to the input vector of altitudes.
21
22 %size_altvec=size(altvec)
23
24 altvec2=altvec;
25
26 % Load the external data table alttemp2.
27 load alttemp2;
28
29 %size_altvec2=size(altvec2)
30
31 tabalt=[];
32 tabalt=alttemp2(1,:);
33 size(tabalt);
34
35 tabtemp=[];
36 tabtemp=alttemp2(2,:);
37 size(tabtemp);
38
39 % Interpolate the input data with the table, generating Tempvec.
40 Tempvec=[];
41 Tempvec=spline(tabalt,tabtemp,altvec2);
42
43 end
44

CA1.n Atmospheric Pressure Data Lookup

Filename: BarForm2.m


1 function [ pressvec ] = BarForm2( altvec )
2 %
3 % Usage: [ pressvec ] = BarForm2( altvec )
4 %
5 % The purpose of this function is to find the barometric pressures
6 % (in Pascals) of Earth's atmosphere, for a range of given altitudes
7 % (in m). This is done by interpolating tables generated from the
8 % parameters specified for the US Standard Atmosphere
9 % 1976.
10 %
11 % Input terms:
12 %
13 % altvec = vector of altitudes (in m) for which the barometric pressure
14 % is to be evaluated
15 %
16 % Output terms:
17 %
18 % pressvec = the barometric pressures (in Pa) at those altitudes
19
20 % Hand off the input variable to a local variable.
21
22 %size_altvec=size(altvec) ;
23
24 altvec2=[];
25
26 altvec2=altvec;
27
28 %size_altvec2=size(altvec2) ;
29
30 % Load the table of altitudes and pressures used to interpolate the values.
31
32 load altpress2 ;
33
34 % Load the altitude and pressure data into input vectors for the spline
routine.
35
36 tabalt=altpress2(1,:);
37
38 tabpress=altpress2(2,:);
39
40 % Use a spline to interpolate the table values, to get the corresponding
41 % pressure values for the altitude input vector.
42
43 pressvec=spline(tabalt,tabpress,altvec2);
44
45 end
46

Filename: MachCalc3.m


1 function [ Machvec ] = MachCalc3( vvec,Altvec )
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to take a series of velocities
4 % in (m/s) over a corresponding range of altitudes in m, and return the
5 % Mach numbers corresponding to these values.
6 %
7 % Usage:
8 % [ Machvec ] = MachCalc3( vvec,Altvec ) ;

10 % PROGRAMMING NOTES

12 %
13 % This routine calls the non-Matlab subroutines refpropm and TempAltCS6.
14 %
15 % The subroutine TempAltCS6 requires calculation of
16 % atmospheric properties using tabular data, generated using the
17 % parameters of US Standard Atmosphere 1976.
18

20
21 Altvec2=[];

23
24 temp_vec = TempAltCS6(Altvec2);
25

27 numval = max(size(Altvec2));
28

30 C=ones(1,numval);
31

33 % for the following calculations.
34 WD = pwd ;
35
36 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
37
38 for i = 1:1:numval

,'argon','oxygen',
[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]);
40 end

45
46 cd(WD) ;

CA1.p Calculate Stagnation Temperatures

Filename: StagTemp.m


1 function [ stagnationT ] = StagTemp( temp,gamma,mach )
2 %
3 % StagTemp Function for calculating stagnation temperature
4 %
5 % Usage:
6 %
7 % [ stagnationT ] = StagTemp( temp,gamma,mach )
8
9 stagterm = 1 + (((gamma-1)/2) * (mach.^2));
10 stagnationT = temp .* stagterm;
11
12 end
13
14




CA1.q Calculate Stagnation Pressures

Filename: StagPress.m


1 function [ stagnationP ] = StagPress(pressure,gamma,mach)
2 %
3 % StagPress Function for calculating stagnation pressure
4 %
5 % Usage: [ stagnationP ] = StagPress(pressure,gamma,mach)
6
7 stagPquant = 1+((gamma-1)/2)*(mach.^2);
8 stagPexp = gamma / (gamma-1);
9 stagPterm = stagPquant .^ stagPexp;
10 stagnationP = pressure .* stagPterm;
11
12 end
13
14




                                       532
CA1.r Temperature of the Precooled Air After air/N2 Heat Exchanger

Filename: T_intermediate_calc_4.m


1 function [H_air_init_vec, ...
2 H_N2_init_vec,T_N2_init_vec, ...
3 T_intermediate_vec,delta_H_air_precooled_vec] = ...
4 T_intermediate_calc_4(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec)
5 %
6 % This function is meant to answer the following question, which is a key
7 % to the understanding of air-collection and enrichment (ACES) propulsion
8 % systems in flight vehicles:
9 %
10 % Suppose I have 1 kilogram of gaseous air at some combination of
11 % pressure and temperature. I then transfer enthalpy from it to 0.7557 kg
12 % of nitrogen at that same pressure, using a counterflow heat exchanger.
13 % (NOTE: 1 kilogram of air contains 0.7557 kg of N2, which is the origin
14 % of this number.)
15 %
16 % The nitrogen starts out at its vapor saturation temperature, and ends
17 % up at the air's initial temperature (again, all without the pressure
18 % changing).
19 %
20 % Under these circumstances, what is the final temperature of the 1 kg of
21 % air?
22 %
23 % The input terms are
24 % T_air_init_vec = ; P_air_init_vec = ;
25 %
26 % where
27 %
28 % T_air_init_vec = the vector of initial temperatures, in Kelvin,
29 % for the 1 kilogram of air as it enters the
30 % counterflow heat exchanger;
31 %
32 % and
33 %
34 % P_air_init_vec = the vector of initial pressures, in kPa,
35 % for the 1 kilogram of air as it enters the
36 % counterflow heat exchanger.
37 %
38 % The output terms are
39 % delta_H_air_precooled_vec,T_intermediate_vec
40 %
41 % where
42 %
43 % delta_H_air_precooled_vec = the vector of the enthalpy changes,
44 % in J, experienced by 1 kilogram of
45 % air as it is sent through the
46 % counterflow heat exchanger;
47 %
48 % and
49 %
50 % T_intermediate_vec = the vector of final temperatures,
51 % in Kelvin, 1 kilogram of air will
52 % have after being passed through the
                                       533
53 % counterflow heat exchanger.
54 %
55 % Usage:
56 %
57 % [H_air_init_vec,...
58 % H_N2_init_vec,T_N2_init_vec,...
59 % T_intermediate_vec,delta_H_air_precooled_vec] = ...
60 % T_intermediate_calc_4(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec) ;
61
62 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
63 %
64 % ------------------------Development History------------------------------
65 % This code is designed to remove subcooled (negative enthalpy) values for
66 % gaseous nitrogen, but ONLY at subcritical pressures. For pressures at or
67 % above critical, negative enthalpy values for supercritical fluid nitrogen
68 % are considered valid, and are retained.
69 %
70 % -------------------------Subroutines Called------------------------------
71 % This function calls the following non-MATLAB subroutine:
72 % refpropm
73 % Make sure to set your REFPROP directory at line 97.
74
75 % Validate the input vector sizes before proceeding further.
76
77 if max(size(T_air_init_vec))~=max(size(P_air_init_vec))
78 error( 'The air temperature and air pressure vectors must have the same
length.' )
79 else
80 end
81
82 T_N2_init_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
83
84 H_N2_init_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
85
86 T_intermediate_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
87
88 H_air_init_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
89
90 delta_H_air_precooled_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
91
92 % Make a note of the current directory, then move to the REFPROP directory
93 % for the following calculations.
94
95 WD = pwd ;
96
97 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
98
99 is_pressure_subcritical = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
100
101 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
102 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
103 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
104 %
105 % Get Initial Enthalpies
106 %
107 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
108 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
109 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
                                       534
110
111 % For each (T_air_init,P_air_init) combination...
112
113 for air_itr = 1:1:max(size(T_air_init_vec))
114
115 %air_itr = air_itr
116
117 % Determine the inital enthalpic content of the 1 kg of air.
118
119 H_air_init = refpropm( 'H','T',T_air_init_vec(1,air_itr),
'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
120
121 H_air_init_vec(1,air_itr) = H_air_init_vec(1,air_itr) + H_air_init ;
122 % Checks out to this point
123
124 % Determine the enthalpic content of 1 kg of N2 at P_air_init, whether
125 % it is subcritical gas or a supercritical fluid.
126
127 P_critical_N2 = refpropm( 'P','C',0,' ',0,'nitrogen' );
128
129 % If the pressure is below the critical pressure of nitrogen...
130
131 if P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr) < P_critical_N2
132
133 is_pressure_subcritical(1,air_itr) = is_pressure_subcritical(1,air_itr) + 1 ;
134
135 % ...use a quality = 1 call to REFPROP to determine the temperature of
136 % the saturated nitrogen vapor.
137 T_N2_fluid = refpropm( 'T','P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'Q',1,'nitrogen' ) ;
138 % Otherwise...
139 else
140 % ...make a C = 0 call to REFPROP to determine the temperature of the
141 % supercritical fluid nitrogen.
142 % NOTE: we assume that this temperature is the critical-point
143 % temperature of nitrogen; this is the lowest temperature that will
144 % still prevent liquid formation at pressures above Pcritical.
145
146 %T_N2_fluid = refpropm('T','P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr),'nitrogen') ;
147 T_N2_fluid = refpropm( 'T','C',0,'P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'nitrogen' ) ;
148
149 end
150
151 T_N2_init_vec(1,air_itr) = T_N2_init_vec(1,air_itr) + T_N2_fluid ;
152 % Checks out to this point
153
154 % Perform data validation on the temperature before proceeding.
155
156 if T_air_init_vec(1,air_itr) <= T_N2_fluid
157 cd(WD) ;
158 error( 'All air temperatures must be greater than the saturated vapor
temperature for
nitrogen.' )
159 else
160 end
161
162 H_N2_init = refpropm( 'H','T',T_N2_fluid, 'P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr),
'nitrogen' ) ;
                                       535
163
164 H_N2_init_vec(1,air_itr) = H_N2_init_vec(1,air_itr) + H_N2_init ;
165
166 end
167
168 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
169 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
170 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
171 %
172 % Reject Subcooled Enthalpies
173 %
174 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
175 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
176 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
177
178 % Remove subcooled enthalpy values for nitrogen gas entering the
179 % precooler, if--and only if--its pressure is subcritical.
180
181 % First, extract all the indices for the subcritical nitrogen values...
182
183 subcritical_ind_vec = find( is_pressure_subcritical > 0 ) ;
184
185 % ...then, extract all the indices for the supercritical nitrogen values.
186
187 supercritical_ind_vec = find( is_pressure_subcritical < 1 ) ;
188
189 % Process the subcritical nitrogen values to retain only the superheated
190 % enthalpy values.
191
192 H_N2_init_subcritical_vec = H_N2_init_vec(subcritical_ind_vec) ;
193
194 [~,pos_ind_vec] = find(H_N2_init_subcritical_vec > 0) ;
195
196 H_N2_init_superheated_subcritical_vec =
H_N2_init_subcritical_vec(1,pos_ind_vec) ;
197
198 % Perform a pchip spline on these subcritical nitrogen values, to fill in
199 % the gaps that have been created by throwing out the subcooled nitrogen
200 % enthalpies.
201
202 H_N2_init_subcritical_vec =
pchip(pos_ind_vec,H_N2_init_superheated_subcritical_vec,
subcritical_ind_vec) ;
203
204 % Extract all supercritical nitrogen enthalpies.
205
206 H_N2_init_supercritical_vec = H_N2_init_vec(supercritical_ind_vec) ;
207
208 % Merge the subcritical and supercritical enthalpies to make the corrected
209 % vector of initial enthalpies for the nitrogen entering the precooler.
210
211 H_N2_init_vec = horzcat(H_N2_init_subcritical_vec,H_N2_init_supercritical_vec)
;
212
213 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
214 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
215 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
216 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
                                       536
217 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
218 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
219 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
220 %
221 % Find Enthalpy Changes And Final Air Temperature
222 %
223 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
224 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
225 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
226 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
227 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
228 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
229 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
230
231 for air_itr = 1:1:max(size(T_air_init_vec))
232
233 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
234 % Nitrogen Enthalpy Changes
235 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
236
237 % Determine the enthalpic content of 1 kg of N2 at
238 % (T_air_init,P_air_init).
239
240 H_N2_final = refpropm( 'H','T',T_air_init_vec(1,air_itr),
'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
air_itr), 'nitrogen' ) ;
241
242 % Find the difference between these two enthalpic contents of 1 kg of
243 % N2...
244
245 H_N2_init = H_N2_init_vec(1,air_itr) ;
246
247 delta_H_per_kg_N2 = H_N2_final - H_N2_init ;
248
249 % ...then rescale this by a factor of 0.7557 to get the enthalpic
250 % change of the amount of nitrogen that was actually used.
251
252 delta_H_for_N2_in_air = delta_H_per_kg_N2 * 0.7557 ;
253
254 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
255 % Air Enthalpy Change and Overall Enthalpies
256 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
257
258 % This last enthalpic change for nitrogen must be equal in size, but
259 % opposite in sign, to the change in enthalpy of the 1 kg of air, given
260 % a completely efficient heat exchanger.
261
262 delta_H_for_air = delta_H_air_precooled_vec(1,air_itr) - delta_H_for_N2_in_air
;
263
264 delta_H_air_precooled_vec(1,air_itr) = delta_H_air_precooled_vec(1,air_itr) +
delta_H_for_air ;
265
266 % Calculate the final enthalpy of the 1 kg of air...
267
268 H_air_init = H_air_init_vec(1,air_itr) ;
269
270 H_air_final = H_air_init + delta_H_for_air ;
                                       537
271
272 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
273 % Final Air Temperature
274 % ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
275
276 % ...and use this to calculate the corresponding T_intermediate of the air.
277
278 T_intermediate_vec(1,air_itr) = T_intermediate_vec(1,air_itr) + refpropm(
'T','H',
H_air_final, 'P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557,
0.012700,0.2316])
;
279
280 end
281
282 % Return to the original directory.
283
284 cd(WD) ;
285
286 end
287




CA1.s Amount of Enthalpy Needs to be Removed from Air to Liquefy It

Filename: liquefy_air.m


1 function [delta_H_air_total_vec] = liquefy_air(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec)
2 % The purpose of this routine is to answer the following question:
3 %
4 % Consider gaseous, dry air at some initial temperature and pressure.
5 % This air is then cooled, with its pressure held constant, until it
6 % liquefies completely. What enthalpy change must occur to make this
7 % happen?
8 %
9 % Usage:
10 % [delta_H_air_total_vec] = liquefy_air(T_air_init_vec,P_air_init_vec);
11
12 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
13 %
14 % This routine makes calls to the following non-MATLAB routine:
15 % refpropm
16 % Make sure to set your REFPROP directory at line 30.
17
18 % Validate the input before proceeding further.
19
20 if max(size(T_air_init_vec))~=max(size(P_air_init_vec))
21 error( 'The air temperature and air pressure vectors must have the same
length.' )
22 else
23 end
24
25 % Make a note of the current directory, then move to the REFPROP directory
26 % for the following calculations.
27
                                       538
28 WD = pwd ;
29
30 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
31
32 delta_H_air_total_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_air_init_vec))) ;
33
34 for air_itr = 1:1:max(size(T_air_init_vec))
35
36 % Calculate the enthalpy change involved in going from the initial
37 % temperature of the gaseous air to its saturated vapor temperature.
38 % NOTES;
39 % 1) Enthalpy is given in units of J/kg.
40 % 2) Temperature is given in units of K.
41
42 H_air_init = refpropm( 'H','T',T_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
43
44 T_air_vapor_sat = refpropm( 'T','P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'Q',
1,'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
45
46 H_air_vapor_sat = refpropm( 'H','T',T_air_vapor_sat, 'P',P_air_init_vec(1,
air_itr), 'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
47
48 delta_H_cool_to_T_cond = H_air_vapor_sat - H_air_init ;
49
50 % Calculate the enthalpy change involved in going from air as saturated
51 % vapor to air that is 100% liquid.
52
53 H_air_liquid = refpropm( 'H','P',P_air_init_vec(1,air_itr), 'Q',
0,'nitrogen' ,'argon','oxygen',[0.7557, 0.012700,0.2316]) ;
54
55 delta_H_liquefaction = H_air_liquid - H_air_vapor_sat ;
56
57 % Using these figures, calculate the overall enthalpy change.
58
59 delta_H_air_total_vec(1,air_itr) = delta_H_air_total_vec(1,air_itr) + (
delta_H_cool_to_T_cond + delta_H_liquefaction ) ;
60
61 end
62
63 % Return to the original directory.
64
65 cd(WD) ;
66
67 end
68




                                       539
CA1.t Integrate the Constant-Pressure Heat Capacity of Parahydrogen

Filename: integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_3.m


1 function [Cp_paraH2_vec,delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec] =
integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_3(T_higher_vec,
T_offset)
2 %
3 % This routine is meant to answer the following question:
4 % 1 kilogram of parahydrogen is initially at its critical temperature and
5 % pressure. It is then warmed up to some higher temperature, while being
6 % maintained at its critical pressure. How much enthalpy does it absorb
7 % during this process?
8 %
9 % The input terms are
10 % T_higher_vec = ; T_offset = ;
11 %
12 % where
13 %
14 % T_higher_vec = the vector of "final" temperatures, in Kelvin,
15 % the critical parahydrogen will be warmed up to.
16 %
17 % The output terms are
18 %
19 % Cp_paraH2_vec = the vector of Cp values the
20 % critical parahydrogen takes, as it
21 % is warmed up from its initial
22 % (critical) temperature to its final
23 % temperature.
24 %
25 % delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec = the vector of Cp values the
26 % critical parahydrogen takes, as it
27 % is warmed up from its initial
28 % (critical) temperature to its final
29 % temperature.
30 %
31 % Usage:
32 % [Cp_paraH2_vec,delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec] =
integrate_paraH2_Pcrit_Cp_3(T_higher_vec,
T_offset) ;
33 %
34 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
35 %
36 % This routine makes calls to the following non-MATLAB routine:
37 % refpropm
38
39 % Make a note of the current directory, then move to the REFPROP directory
40 % for the following calculations.
41
42 WD = pwd ;
43
44 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
45
46 % Break the integration range for each run down into a constant number of
47 % temperature divisions.
48
                                       540
49 num_divisions = 100 ;
50
51 % Retrieve the critical temperature and pressure for parahydrogen.
52
53 %T_offset = 0 ;
54
55 T_critical = refpropm( 'T','C',0,' ',0,'parahyd' ) + T_offset ;
56
57 P_critical = refpropm( 'P','C',0,' ',0,'parahyd' ) ;
58
59 % Perform data validation on the temperatures.
60
61 for T_itr = 1:1:max(size(T_higher_vec))
62 if T_higher_vec(1,T_itr) <= T_critical
63 cd(WD) ;
64 error( 'All input temperatures must be greater than T_critical for
parahydrogen.' )
65 else
66 end
67 end
68
69 delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec = zeros(1,max(size(T_higher_vec))) ;
70
71 %figure
72 %hold on
73 %grid
74 %xlabel('Integration Range Temperature (K)')
75 %ylabel('Cp (J/(kg K))')
76
77 % For each "higher" temperature being investigated...
78 for T_itr = 1:1:max(size(T_higher_vec))
79
80 % Generate a vector of temperatures from T_critical to T_higher.
81
82 %T_critical = T_critical + 1 ;
83
84 T_higher = T_higher_vec(1,T_itr) ;
85 T_integral_vec = T_critical: (T_higher - T_critical)/(num_divisions - 1) :
T_higher ;
86
87 % For each one of these temperatures, return the Cp of parahydrogen.
88
89 Cp_paraH2_vec = zeros(1,num_divisions) ;
90
91 for Cp_itr = 1:1:num_divisions
92 Cp_paraH2_vec(1,Cp_itr) = Cp_paraH2_vec(1,Cp_itr) + refpropm(
'C','T',T_integral_vec
(1,Cp_itr), 'P',P_critical, 'parahyd' );
93 end
94
95 %plot(T_integral_vec,Cp_paraH2_vec)
96
97 % Integrate the Cp values over the specified temperature range. This
98 % will yield the change in enthalpy.
99
100 delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec(1,T_itr) = delta_H_paraH2_Pcrit_vec(1,T_itr) + trapz
(T_integral_vec,Cp_paraH2_vec) ;
101
                                       541
102 end
103
104 %hold off
105
106 % Return to the original directory.
107
108 cd(WD) ;
109
110 end
111
