CODING APPENDIX.2 Coding Appendix Chapter 2

This is a collection of all the MATLAB code used in Chapter 2.

CA2.a Model General Gun Behavior for Nitroglycerin

Filename: gun_calc_SC_ideal.m


1 function [time_vec, ...
2 static_pressure_vec,dynamic_pressure_vec, ...
3 temperature_vec, ...
4 force_vec, ...
5 acceleration_vec,velocity_vec,displacement_vec, ...
6 volume_vec, ...
7 gas_internal_energy_vec,shell_kinetic_energy_vec] = ...
8 gun_calc_SC_ideal(shell_mass,shell_diameter, ...
9 initial_vol,initial_temp,initial_nitro_mass, ...
10 initial_velocity,initial_displacement, ...
11 max_num_timesteps,max_time, ...
12 plot_static_pressure,plot_dynamic_pressure,plot_dynamic_over_static_pressure,
...
13 plot_temperature, ...
14 plot_force, ...
15 plot_acceleration,plot_velocity,plot_displacement, ...
16 plot_gas_internal_energy,plot_shell_kinetic_energy)
17 %
18 % Consider the case of a gun, which fires a shell from a cylindrical
19 % bore. Given the mass and base-plate area of the shell, along with the
20 % initial properties of the propellant gas generated by the powder
21 % charge, how does the shell move during subsequent points in time?
22 %
23 % This routine is meant to answer the preceding question, given the
24 % following assumptions:
25 %
26 % 0) This routine will only run within a range that is above the critical
27 % pressure of the explosive decomposition gas mixture (hence, the "SC" in
28 % the routine's name, for SuperCritical).
29 %
30 % 1) The behavior of the gas behind the shell may be described by the
31 % ideal gas law equations, PV = nRT and U = (3/2)nRT.
32 %
33 % 2) The pressure exerted by the propellant gas on the base of the
34 % projectile IS weighted by Maxwell-Boltzmann considerations, i.e.
35 % by what fraction of gas molecules in the propellant gas are moving with
36 % speeds greater than or equal to that of the projectile.
37 %
38 % 3) Joule-Thomson isenthalpic effects ARE NOT fully accounted for
39 % during the expansion of the propellant gas. More specifically, the
40 % routine is set up to terminate when the critical pressure is reached.
41 %
42 % 4) The projectile starts out motionless, with zero displacement, at
43 % t = 0.
44 %

                                         545
45 % 5) The explosive decomposition products of the propellant used for the
46 % shell are stoichiometrically equivalent to those of nitroglycerin.
47 % This assumption imposes a stoichiometry of
48 % 4 C_3 H_5 N_3 O_9 --> 6 N_2 + 10 H_2 O + 12 C O_2 + 1 O_2
49 %
50 %
51 % Input terms:
52 %
53 % shell_mass = ; shell_diameter = ;
54 % initial_vol = ; initial_temp = ; initial_nitro_mass = ;
55 % max_num_timesteps = ; max_time = ;
56 % plot_static_pressure = ; plot_dynamic_pressure = ;
plot_dynamic_over_static_pressure = ;
57 % plot_temperature = ;
58 % plot_force = ;
59 % plot_acceleration = ; plot_velocity = ; plot_displacement = ;
60 % plot_gas_internal_energy = ; plot_shell_kinetic_energy = ;
61 %
62 %
63 % Usage:
64 %
65 % [time_vec,...
66 % static_pressure_vec,dynamic_pressure_vec,...
67 % temperature_vec,...
68 % force_vec,...
69 % acceleration_vec,velocity_vec,displacement_vec,...
70 % volume_vec,...
71 % gas_internal_energy_vec,shell_kinetic_energy_vec] = ...
72 % gun_calc_SC_ideal(shell_mass,shell_diameter,...
73 % initial_vol,initial_temp,initial_nitro_mass,...
74 % initial_velocity,initial_displacement,...
75 % max_num_timesteps,max_time,...
76 %
plot_static_pressure,plot_dynamic_pressure,plot_dynamic_over_static_pressure,...
77 % plot_temperature,...
78 % plot_force,...
79 % plot_acceleration,plot_velocity,plot_displacement,...
80 % plot_gas_internal_energy,plot_shell_kinetic_energy) ;
81
82 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
83 %
84 % This code explicitly incorporates user inputs for the initial
85 % displacement and velocity of the shell.
86 %
87 % Note that this function has REFPROP dependencies.
88 %
89 % Assign your REFPROP directory at line 226.
90 %
91
92 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
93 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
94 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
95 %
96 % Validate and Initialize
97 %
98 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
99 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
100 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
                                       546
101
102 % Validate the input.
103
104 if shell_mass<=0
105 error( 'The shell mass must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
106 else
107 end
108
109
110
111 if shell_diameter<=0
112 error( 'The shell diameter must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
113 else
114 end
115
116
117
118 if initial_vol<=0
119 error( 'The initial volume must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
120 else
121 end
122
123
124
125 if initial_temp<=0
126 error( 'The initial temperature must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
127 else
128 end
129
130 if initial_nitro_mass<=0
131 error( 'The initial mass of nitroglycerin must be a positive, nonzero number.'
)
132 else
133 end
134
135 if max_num_timesteps<=0
136 error( 'The number of timesteps must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
137 else
138 end
139
140 if max_time<=0
141 error( 'The maximum elapsed time must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
142 else
143 end
144
145 % Use the stoichiometry of nitroglycerin's explosive decomposition to find
146 % the inital moles of propellant gas. In the balanced equation, 29 mol of
147 % gas go out for every 4 mol of nitroglycerin that go in.
148
149 mol_nitro = initial_nitro_mass * (1000/1) * (1/288.088) ;
150
151 % Detremine the moles and average molar mass of the decomposition products
152 % of nitroglycerin.
153
154 number_of_moles_of_gas = mol_nitro * (29/4) ;
155
156 avg_NG_prod_molar_mass_kg_per_mol =
(1/29)*(1/1000)*((6*28.014)+(10*18.0153)+(12*44.009)+31.
                                       547
9988) ;
157
158 % Use the shell's diameter to find the shell's base plate area.
159
160 shell_area = pi * ((shell_diameter/2)^2) ;
161
162 % Initialize the vectors.
163
164 prelim_time_vec = 0: max_time / (max_num_timesteps-1): max_time ;
165
166 static_pressure_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
167
168 dynamic_pressure_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
169
170 temperature_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
171
172 force_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
173
174 acceleration_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
175
176 velocity_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
177
178 velocity_vec(1,1) = initial_velocity ;
179
180 displacement_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
181
182 displacement_vec(1,1) = initial_displacement ;
183
184 volume_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
185
186 % Set the first values of the volume and temperature vectors.
187
188 volume_vec(1,1) = initial_vol ;
189
190 temperature_vec(1,1) = initial_temp ;
191
192 % Set the gas constant.
193
194 gas_constant = 8.31447 ; % m^3 Pa mol^-1 K^-1
195
196 % Determine the starting internal energy of the gas.
197
198 gas_internal_energy_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
199
200 gas_internal_energy_vec(1,1) =
(3/2)*number_of_moles_of_gas*gas_constant*initial_temp ;
201
202 % Initialize the kinetic energy of the shell.
203
204 shell_kinetic_energy_vec = nan(1,max_num_timesteps) ;
205
206 shell_kinetic_energy_vec(1,1) = 0 ;
207
208 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
209 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
210 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
211 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
212 %
                                       548
213 % Iterate Through Firing Process
214 %
215 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
216 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
217 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
218 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
219
220 % Make a note of the current directory, then move to the REFPROP directory
221 % for the following calculations.
222
223 WD = pwd ;
224
225 %%%% User, use your REFPROP directory here!!!!!!
226 cd('C:\Program Files (x86)\REFPROP' ) ;
227
228 P_critical = refpropm( 'P','C',0,' ',0,'nitrogen' ,'water','co2','oxygen',
[0.185043,0.198330,0.58140,0.0352270]) ;
229 % Critical pressure
230
231 keep_iterating = 1 ;
232
233 % For each point in time:
234
235 time_itr = 0 ;
236
237 time_vec = [] ;
238
239 while keep_iterating == 1
240 %for time_itr = 1:1: max(size(time_vec))-1
241
242 time_itr = time_itr + 1
243
244 time_vec = horzcat(time_vec,prelim_time_vec(1,time_itr))
245
246 % Calculate the pressure of gas in the bore.
247
248 static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) = number_of_moles_of_gas * gas_constant *
temperature_vec(1,time_itr) ./ volume_vec(1,time_itr) ;
249
250 static_pressure_vec_at_time_itr = static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr)
251
252 % Calculate the pressure on the base plate of the projectile.
253
254 dynamic_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) = static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) ...
255 *
integral(@(vx_vec)Maxwell_Boltzmann_1D_corr(avg_NG_prod_molar_mass_kg_per_mol,
temperature_vec(1,time_itr),vx_vec), velocity_vec(1,time_itr),1e6) ;
256
257 % Calculate the force acting on the projectile.
258
259 force_vec(1,time_itr) = dynamic_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) * shell_area ;
260
261 % Calculate the acceleration of the projectile.
262
263 acceleration_vec(1,time_itr) = force_vec(1,time_itr) / shell_mass ;
264
265 % Calculate the new velocity of the projectile.
266
                                       549
267 velocity_vec(1,time_itr+1) = velocity_vec(1,time_itr) + (
acceleration_vec(1,time_itr)
* (prelim_time_vec(1,time_itr+1)-prelim_time_vec(time_itr)) ) ;
268
269 % Calculate the new kinetic energy of the projectile.
270
271 shell_kinetic_energy_vec(1,time_itr+1) = 0.5 * shell_mass * ( (velocity_vec(1,
time_itr+1)) ^ 2 ) ;
272
273 delta_E = shell_kinetic_energy_vec(1,time_itr+1) -
shell_kinetic_energy_vec(1,time_itr) ;
274
275 % Calculate the new internal energy and temperature of the propellant
276 % gas.
277
278 gas_internal_energy_vec(1,time_itr+1) = gas_internal_energy_vec(1,time_itr) -
delta_E ;
279
280 temperature_vec(1,time_itr+1) = gas_internal_energy_vec(1,time_itr+1) / ((3/2)
*number_of_moles_of_gas*gas_constant) ;
281
282 % Further update the temperature if Joule-Thomson effects are
283 % determined to be important. This will be done on the basis of the
284 % pressure, via a call to REFPROP.
285
286 static_pressure_vec_at_time_itr = static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr)
287
288 if static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) >= P_critical*1e3
289 if time_itr == max_num_timesteps
290 keep_iterating = 0 ;
291 else
292 end
293 else
294 disp( ' ')
295 disp( 'Pressure has fallen below critical level.' )
296 disp( 'Halting execution....' )
297 disp( ' ')
298 keep_iterating = 0 ;
299 end
300
301 % Calculate the new displacement of the projectile.
302
303 displacement_vec(1,time_itr+1) = displacement_vec(1,time_itr) + (
velocity_vec(1,
time_itr) * (prelim_time_vec(1,time_itr+1)-prelim_time_vec(time_itr)) ) ;
304
305 % Calculate the new volume of gas behind the projectile.
306
307 volume_vec(1,time_itr+1) = initial_vol + (
shell_area.*displacement_vec(1,time_itr+1) ) ;
308
309 end
310
311 time_vec = horzcat(time_vec,prelim_time_vec(1,time_itr+1)) ;
312
313 shell_kinetic_energy_vec = rmmissing(shell_kinetic_energy_vec) ;
314
315 gas_internal_energy_vec = rmmissing(gas_internal_energy_vec) ;
                                       550
316
317 temperature_vec = rmmissing(temperature_vec) ;
318
319 displacement_vec = rmmissing(displacement_vec) ;
320
321 volume_vec = rmmissing(volume_vec) ;
322
323 % Calculate the final pressure on the base plate of the projectile.
324
325 size_temperature_vec = size(temperature_vec)
326
327 size_volume_vec = size(volume_vec)
328
329 static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr+1) = number_of_moles_of_gas * gas_constant *
temperature_vec
(1,time_itr) ./ volume_vec(1,time_itr) ;
330
331 static_pressure_vec = rmmissing(static_pressure_vec) ;
332
333 dynamic_pressure_vec(1,time_itr+1) = static_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) ...
334
*integral(@(vx_vec)Maxwell_Boltzmann_1D(avg_NG_prod_molar_mass_kg_per_mol,temperat
ure_vec
(1,time_itr+1),vx_vec),velocity_vec(1,time_itr+1),1e6) ;
335
336 dynamic_pressure_vec = rmmissing(dynamic_pressure_vec) ;
337
338 % Calculate the final force acting on the projectile.
339
340 force_vec(1,time_itr+1) = dynamic_pressure_vec(1,time_itr) * shell_area ;
341
342 force_vec = rmmissing(force_vec) ;
343
344 % Calculate the final acceleration of the projectile.
345
346 acceleration_vec(1,time_itr+1) = force_vec(1,time_itr) / shell_mass ;
347
348 acceleration_vec = rmmissing(acceleration_vec) ;
349
350 % Calculate the ratio of the dynamic pressure over the static pressure.
351
352 dynamic_over_static_pressure_vec = dynamic_pressure_vec ./ static_pressure_vec
;
353
354 dynamic_over_static_pressure_vec = rmmissing(dynamic_over_static_pressure_vec)
;
355
356 velocity_vec = rmmissing(velocity_vec) ;
357
358 displacement_vec = rmmissing(displacement_vec) ;
359
360 % Return to the original working directory.
361
362 cd(WD) ;

                                       551

CA2.b Maxwell Boltzmann Probability Distributions

Filename: Maxwell_Boltzmann_1D_molar_mass_abs_temp_vx_vec.m


1 function [prob_vx_vec] =
Maxwell_Boltzmann_1D_molar_mass_abs_temp_vx_vec(molar_mass,abs_temp,
vx_vec)
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to calculate, for a gas with a given
4 % molar mass and Kelvin temperature, the probability distribution of a
5 % given range of x-direction-velocities of its particles. Note that the
6 % gas_constant is at like 33.
7 %
8 % Input terms:
9 %
10 % molar_mass,abs_temp,vx_vec
11 %
12 % where
13 %
14 % molar_mass = the average molar mass of the gas, in kg/mol ;
15 %
16 % abs_temp = the absolute temperature of the gas, in Kelvin ;
17 %
18 % and
19 %
20 % vx_vec = the vector of velocities of the gas particles, in
21 % m/s.
22 %
23 % Usage:
24 %
25 % [prob_vx_vec] = Maxwell_Boltzmann_1D_corr(molar_mass,abs_temp,vx_vec) ;
26
27 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
28 %
29 % Changing the inputs of this function to match the fuel-oxidizer-diluent
30 % mixtures in different sections of a ram accelerator will demonstrate how
31 % the projectile velocity will increase as it moves down the bore.
32
33 gas_constant = 8.31447 ; % m^3 Pa mol^-1 K^-1
34
35 factor = ( molar_mass / (2*pi*gas_constant*abs_temp) )^(3/2) ;
36
37 exp_power_vec = -( molar_mass .* (vx_vec.^2) ) / ( 2* gas_constant * abs_temp )
;
38
39 prob_vx_vec = 4 * pi * factor .* (vx_vec.^2) .* exp(exp_power_vec) ;
40
41 end
42
43




                                       558
CA2.c Calculate Length of Barrel of Prelauncher Stage of a Ram Accelerator

Filename: PPIG_gun_barrel_length.m


1 function [length_of_barrel] = ...
2 PPIG_gun_barrel_length(projectile_mass,projectile_velocity,projectile_area, ...
3 pressure,speed_of_sound,gamma)
4 %
5 % This routine solves the preburned-propellant-ideal-gas-gun barrel
6 % length equation (12-1) in Arnold E. Seigel, _The Theory of High-Speed
7 % Guns_: AGARD / NATO, May 1965, p. 21. This is how we calculate the
8 % length of the prelauncher in ram accelerator.
9 %
10 % Usage:
11 %
12 % [length_of_barrel] = ...
13 %
PPIG_gun_barrel_length(projectile_mass,projectile_velocity,projectile_area,...
14 % pressure,speed_of_sound, gamma)
15
16 pressure = pressure
17
18 speed_of_sound = speed_of_sound
19
20 gamma = gamma
21
22 term_1 = ( projectile_mass * (speed_of_sound^2) ) / ( pressure *
projectile_area ) ;
23
24 term_2 = 2 / (gamma + 1) ;
25
26 term_3_num = (2 / (gamma - 1) ) - (((gamma+1)/(gamma-1))*( 1 -
((projectile_velocity*
(gamma-1))/(2*speed_of_sound)) ) ) ;
27
28 term_3_den = ( 1 - ((projectile_velocity*(gamma-1))/(2*speed_of_sound)) ) ^ (
(gamma+1) /
(gamma-1) ) ;
29
30 term_3 = ( term_3_num / term_3_den ) + 1 ;
31
32 length_of_barrel = term_1 * term_2 * term_3;
33
34 end




                                       559
CA2.d Calculate Section Lengths A Ram Accelerator in Thermally Choked Mode

and Oblique Detonation Mode

Filename: shell_w_linearly_varying_P.m


1 function [u_proj_vec] = shell_w_linearly_varying_P(pressure_1,velocity_1, ...
2 pressure_2,velocity_2, ...
3 shell_mass,shell_area, ...
4 t_vec)
5 % Usage:
6 %
7 % [u_proj_vec] = shell_w_linearly_varying_P(pressure_1,velocity_1,...
8 % pressure_2,velocity_2,...
9 % shell_mass,shell_area,...
10 % t_vec)
11 %
12 % This is how we calculate the section lengths of the barrels
13 % of a ram accelerator in thermally choked mode and
14 % oblique detonation mode.
15 %
16
17 m_slope = (pressure_2-pressure_1) / (velocity_2-velocity_1) ;
18
19 b = pressure_1 - ( m_slope * velocity_1 ) ;
20
21 constant = velocity_1 + ( b / m_slope ) ;
22
23 area_over_mass = shell_area / shell_mass ;
24
25 u_proj_vec = -( b / m_slope ) + ( constant .*
exp(area_over_mass*m_slope.*t_vec) ) ;
26
27 end

CODING APPENDIX.3 Coding Appendix Chapter 3

This is a collection of all the MATLAB code used in Chapter 3.

CA3.a Stagnation temperature function for when M = V2 / c2

Filename: StagTempExpanded.m


1 function [ stagnationTExpanded ] = StagTempExpanded(
v,freestream_temp,gamma,R,molar_mass )
2 %
3 %StagTempExpanded Function for calculating stagnation temperature, where
4 %Mach is equal to v^2 / c^2. And v is the velocity of the projectile, c is
5 %the speed of sound in the gas (local speed of sound).
6 % Usage:
7 % [ stagnationTExpanded ] = StagTempExpanded(
v,freestream_temp,gamma,R,molar_mass )
8
9 stagterm0 = ((gamma-1)/2);
10 stagterm1 = v.^2;
11 stagterm2 = molar_mass/(gamma * R);
12 stagnationTExpanded = freestream_temp + (stagterm0.*stagterm1.*stagterm2);
13
14 end
15

);

);
10
11 precent_of_original_t_stag = (stagnationTExpanded2./stagnationTExpanded1)*100;

CA3.c Adiabatic Flame Temperature Calculator

Filename: adiabatic_flame_temperature_calc_O2_CH4_Ludwig.m



1 %adiabatic_flame_temperature_calc
2
3 % Step 1: Balance equation for products and reactants.
4
5 % Step 2: Hess's Law (rule of thumb)
6 % kJ/mol
7 deltaH_CO = -110.5233 ;
8 deltaH_CO2 = -393.509 ;
9 deltaH_H2O = -285.8 ;
10 deltaH_CH4 = -74.9 ;
11 deltaH_O2 = 0 ;
12 deltaH_H2 = 0 ;
13 deltaH_N2 = 0 ;
14
15 % Step 2: Apply Hess's Law.
16
17 deltaH_reaction_p = deltaH_CO2 + (2*deltaH_H2O)
18
19 deltaH_reaction_r = deltaH_CH4 + (2*deltaH_O2)
20
21 deltaH_reaction = deltaH_reaction_p - deltaH_reaction_r
22
23 % Step 3: Empirical constants for molar heat capacities of gases at constant
pressure
24 % C_p = A + BT + CT^2 +DT^3 + ET^4, where T where T is in degrees Kelvin;
kJ/(mole * K)
(specify temp range)
25 % from Ludwig
26
27 % Heat of Vaporization of Water kJ/mole
28
29 Vape_H2O = 43.988 ;
30
31 % cal_to_kJ = (4.184/1000) ;
32 %
33 %
34 % a_CO = 6.350;
35 % b_CO = 1.811*(10^-3);
36 % c_CO = -0.2675*(10^-6);
37 %
38 % a_CO = a_CO * cal_to_kJ ;
39 % b_CO = b_CO * cal_to_kJ ;
40 % c_CO = c_CO * cal_to_kJ ;
41 %
42 %
                                       562
43 %
44 % a_CO2 = 6.339;
45 % b_CO2 = 10.14*(10^-3);
46 % c_CO2 = -3.415*(10^-6);
47 %
48 % a_CO2 = a_CO2 * cal_to_kJ ;
49 % b_CO2 = b_CO2 * cal_to_kJ ;
50 % c_CO2 = c_CO2 * cal_to_kJ ;
51
52 % a_H2O = 7.136;
53 % b_H2O = 2.640*(10^-3);
54 % c_H2O = 0.0459*(10^-6);
55 %
56 % a_H2O = a_H2O * cal_to_kJ ;
57 % b_H2O = b_H2O * cal_to_kJ ;
58 % c_H2O = c_H2O * cal_to_kJ ;
59
60 % a_CH4 = 3.204;
61 % b_CH4 = 18.41*(10^-3);
62 % c_CH4 = -4.48*(10^-6);
63 %
64 % a_CH4 = a_CH4 * cal_to_kJ ;
65 % b_CH4 = b_CH4 * cal_to_kJ ;
66 % c_CH4 = c_CH4 * cal_to_kJ ;
67
68 a_CH4 = 34.942e-3 ;
69 b_CH4 = -3.9957e-5 ;
70 c_CH4 = 1.9184e-7 ;
71 d_CH4 = -1.5303e-10 ;
72 e_CH4 = 3.9321e-14 ;
73
74 a_CO2 = 27.437e-3 ;
75 b_CO2 = 4.2315e-5 ;
76 c_CO2 = -1.9555e-8 ;
77 d_CO2 = 3.9968e-12 ;
78 e_CO2 = -2.9872e-16 ;
79
80 a_H2O = 33.933e-3 ;
81 b_H2O = -8.4186e-6 ;
82 c_H2O = 2.9906e-8 ;
83 d_H2O = -1.7825e-11 ;
84 e_H2O = 3.6934e-15 ;
85
86 % a_O2 = 6.117;
87 % b_O2 = 3.167*(10^-3) ;
88 % c_O2 = -1.005*(10^-6) ;
89 %
90 % a_O2 = a_O2 * cal_to_kJ ;
91 % b_O2 = b_O2 * cal_to_kJ ;
92 % c_O2 = c_O2 * cal_to_kJ ;
93
94 % a_H2 = 6.946;
95 % b_H2 = -0.196*(10^-3);
96 % c_H2 = 0.4757*(10^-6);
97 %
98 % a_H2 = a_H2 * cal_to_kJ ;
99 % b_H2 = b_H2 * cal_to_kJ ;
100 % c_H2 = c_H2 * cal_to_kJ ;
                                   563
101
102 n_CO2 = 1 ;
103 n_H2O = 2 ;
104 n_CH4 = 0.4 ;
105
106 T0 = 298 ;
107 n_moles = n_CO2 + n_H2O + n_CH4 ;
108
109 a = ((n_CO2/n_moles)*a_CO2) + ((n_H2O/n_moles)*a_H2O) +
((n_CH4/n_moles)*a_CH4) ;
110 b = ((n_CO2/n_moles)*b_CO2) + ((n_H2O/n_moles)*b_H2O) +
((n_CH4/n_moles)*b_CH4) ;
111 c = ((n_CO2/n_moles)*c_CO2) + ((n_H2O/n_moles)*c_H2O) +
((n_CH4/n_moles)*c_CH4) ;
112 d = ((n_CO2/n_moles)*d_CO2) + ((n_H2O/n_moles)*d_H2O) +
((n_CH4/n_moles)*d_CH4) ;
113 e = ((n_CO2/n_moles)*e_CO2) + ((n_H2O/n_moles)*e_H2O) +
((n_CH4/n_moles)*e_CH4) ;
114
115 Ta = 1000:10:5000;
116
117 size_Ta = size(Ta)
118
119 aterm = a.*(Ta - T0);
120 bterm = (b/2).*((Ta.^2) - (T0^2));
121 cterm = (c/3).*((Ta.^3) - (T0^3));
122 dterm = (d/4).*((Ta.^4) - (T0^4));
123 eterm = (e/5).*((Ta.^5) - (T0^5));
124
125 % negative_deltaH_reaction = -deltaH_reaction
126
127 H2O_term = (n_H2O*Vape_H2O)
128
129 A_term = -abs( deltaH_reaction + (n_H2O*Vape_H2O) )
130
131 %size_f_Ta = size(f_Ta)
132
133 f_Ta = -abs( deltaH_reaction + (n_H2O*Vape_H2O) ) + (n_moles.*(aterm + bterm +
cterm + dterm
+ eterm)) ;
134
135 % fun_MAT(:,1) = Ta';
136 % fun_MAT(:,2) = f_Ta';
137
138 % fun_MAT = horzcat(Ta',f_Ta')
139
140 %figure
141 hold on
142 grid
143
144 ax = gca ;
145
146 ax.XLabel.String = 'Temperature (K)'
147
148 ax.YLabel.String = 'f_{Ta} (kJ)'
149
150 plot(Ta, f_Ta, '-ob')

                                       564
CODING APPENDIX.4 Coding Appendix Chapter 4

There is no MATLAB code in Chapter 4.

CODING APPENDIX.5 Coding Appendix Chapter 5

This is a collection of all the MATLAB code used in Chapter 5.

CA5.a Kantrowitz Area Ratio Calculator

Filename: Kantrowitz5.m


1 function [ area_ratio ] = Kantrowitz5( Mach_num,gamma )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ area_ratio ] = Kantrowitz5( Mach_num,gamma )
6 % The purpose of this function is to calculate the Kantrowitz area ratio,
7 % of (area at cowl lip / area at inlet throat), required for a
8 % self-starting scramjet inlet.
9 % From Van Wie et al., "Starting characteristics of supersonic inlets,"
10 % p. 2.
11 %
12
13 term_0 = (Mach_num);
14
15 term_1_num = (gamma+1).*(Mach_num.^2);
16 term_1_den = ((gamma-1).*(Mach_num.^2))+2;
17 term_1_power = (-gamma)./(gamma-1);
18 term_1 = (term_1_num./term_1_den).^term_1_power;
19
20 term_2_num = (gamma+1);
21 term_2_den = (2*gamma.*(Mach_num.^2))-(gamma-1);
22 term_2_power = -1./(gamma-1);
23 term_2 = (term_2_num./term_2_den).^term_2_power;
24
25 term_3_num = 1+(((gamma-1)/2).*(Mach_num.^2));
26 term_3_den = (gamma+1)/2;
27 term_3_power = -((gamma+1)./(2*(gamma-1)));
28 term_3_p1 = term_3_num./term_3_den;
29 term_3 = term_3_p1.^term_3_power;
30
31 area_ratio_a4_over_a0 = term_0.* term_1.* term_2.* term_3;
32 % note this is now in the form of r_inlet/r_throat

                                         565
33 area_ratio = 1./area_ratio_a4_over_a0;
34
35 end
36




CA5.b Isentropic Area Ratio Calculator

Filename: Isentropic_Area_Ratio_calc.m


1 function [ isentropic_area_ratio ] = Isentropic_Area_Ratio_calc( Mach_num,gamma
)
2 % Isentropic Area Ratio
3 %
4 % Usage:
5 % [ isentropic_area_ratio ] = Isentropic_Area_Ratio_calc( Mach_num,gamma )
6 % From Van Wie, “Scramjet Inlets,” in
7 % Scramjet Propulsion, E.T Curran and S.N.B. Murthy (eds), Chapter 7,
8 % p. 463 EQ. 33
9 %
10
11 term_0 = (Mach_num);
12
13 term_1_num = (gamma+1);
14 term_1_den = 2;
15 term_1_power = (gamma+1)./(2*(gamma-1));
16 term_1 = (term_1_num./term_1_den).^term_1_power;
17
18 term_2_par = 1 + (((gamma-1)/2).*Mach_num.^2);
19 term_2_power = (gamma+1)./(2*(gamma-1));
20 term_2 = (term_2_par).^((-1)*term_2_power);
21
22 isentropic_area_ratio = term_0 .* term_1 .* term_2 ;
23
24 end
25
26
27




CA5.c Ram Accelerator Projectile Throat to Bore Area Ratio Calculator

Filename: Ram_Area_Ratio_calc.m


1 function [ ram_area_ratio ] = Ram_Area_Ratio_calc( Mach_num,gamma )
2 % Isentropic Area Ratio
3 %
4 % Usage:
5 % [ Ram_area_ratio ] = Ram_Area_Ratio_calc( Mach_num,gamma )
6 % From "The Subdetonative Ram Accelerator Starting Process"
7 % By Eric Schultz

                                         566
8 % p. 10 EQ. 2.1
9 %
10
11 term_0 = (1/(Mach_num^2));
12
13 term_1_num = 2;
14 term_1_den = (gamma+1);
15 term_1_power = (gamma+1)./(gamma-1);
16
17 term_2_par = 1 + (((gamma-1)/2).*Mach_num.^2);
18
19 term_1_2 = ((term_1_num./term_1_den).*(term_2_par)).^term_1_power;
20
21 % in the form A_tube/A_throat
22 ram_area_ratio = sqrt(term_0 .* term_1_2) ;
23
24 end
25

CA5.e Throat Radius Calculator

Filename: r_throat_calc.m


1 function [ r_throat_c ] = r_throat_calc(r_inlet,area_ratio)
2 % This calculates the radius of the throat of the Busemann toroid using the
3 % Kantrowitz ratio, since the bore size is known.
4
5 r_throat_c = sqrt((r_inlet.^2)./area_ratio);
6
7 end

CA5.g Given θshock find θcone

Filename: given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4.m


1 function [theta_cone] = given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4(
theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to find the angle of a cone that
4 % supports a specified shock wave, given a particular Mach number of
5 % flight, and a known gamma for the atmosphere it is flying through.
6 %
7 % This is done by carrying out a restricted version of steps 1-4 in Anderson's
8 % procedure for the numerical solution of the Taylor-MacColl equations
9 % (Modern Compressible Flow, 3rd ed, pp. 371-372).
10 %
11 % We use Piecewise Cubic Hermite Interpolating Polynomial (PCHIP)interpolation
to find
theta_cone.
12 %
13 % Usage:
14 % [theta_cone] = given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
15 %
16 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
17 %
18 % This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
19 %
20 % delta_m2_behind_cone_shock
21 % V_prime_r_theta
22 % find_v_primes_behind_shock_6
23 % Set theta_num at line 69
24
25 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
26 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
27 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
28 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
29 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
30 %
                                       570
31 % Initial Taylor-MacColl Steps
32 %
33 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
34 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
35 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
36 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
37 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
38
39 % First, calculate the deflection angle and Mach number for the slowed-down
40 % flow immediately behind the shock.
41
42 [ delta,Mach_2 ] = delta_m2_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma );
43
44 % Second, using this information, find the normal and radial components of
45 % the flow velocity immediately behind the shock.
46
47 [ ~,V_prime_r,V_prime_theta ] = V_prime_r_theta( theta_s,delta,Mach_2,gamma ) ;
48
49 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
50 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
51 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
52 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
53 %
54 % Iterative V_prime Solver
55 %
56 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
57 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
58 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
59 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
60
61 % Third, use this information to calculate the flowfield behind the shock,
62 % by working inward from the shock toward the cone. The angle at which the
63 % V_prime_theta = 0 must be the angle of the cone. (Anderson, p. 371)
64
65 theta_max = theta_s;
66
67 theta_min = 0.01*(pi/180) ;
68
69 theta_num = 10000 ;
70
71 V_prime_r_at_theta_max = V_prime_r ;
72
73 V_prime_theta_at_theta_max = V_prime_theta ;
74
75 for num_itr = 1:1:10
76
77 disp( ' ')
78 sprintf( 'This is iteration number %d.' ,num_itr)
79 disp( ' ')
80
81 [ V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec,theta_vec ] = ...
82 find_v_primes_behind_shock_6( theta_max,theta_min,theta_num, ...
83 V_prime_r_at_theta_max,V_prime_theta_at_theta_max, ...
84 gamma )
85
86 % Find the center of the negative V_prime_theta_values.
87
88 neg_V_prime_theta_ind_vec = find(V_prime_theta_vec<0)
                                       571
89
90 max_neg_V_prime_theta_ind = max(neg_V_prime_theta_ind_vec)
91
92 ind_middle_neg_V_prime_theta = floor(max_neg_V_prime_theta_ind/2)
93
94 % Reset theta_min to the angle that occurs at the center of the
95 % negative V_prime_theta range.
96
97 theta_min = theta_vec(ind_middle_neg_V_prime_theta,1) ;
98
99 % Find the center of the positive V_prime_theta values.
100
101 ind_middle_pos_V_prime_theta = ceil( (max_neg_V_prime_theta_ind + 1 + max(size
(theta_vec))) / 2 )
102
103 % Reset theta_max to the angle that occurs at the center of the
104 % positive V_prime_theta range.
105
106 theta_max = theta_vec(ind_middle_pos_V_prime_theta,1) ;
107
108 % Reset the initial conditions of V_prime_r and V_prime_theta to those
109 % that hold at the center of the positive V_prime_theta range.
110
111 V_prime_r_at_theta_max = V_prime_r_vec(ind_middle_pos_V_prime_theta,1) ;
112
113 V_prime_theta_at_theta_max = V_prime_theta_vec(ind_middle_pos_V_prime_theta,1)
;
114
115 end
116
117 disp( ' ')
118 disp( 'Leaving iterative step.' )
119 disp( ' ')
120
121 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
122 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
123 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
124 %
125 % Generate Theta_Cone
126 %
127 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
128 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
129 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
130
131 % Using interpolation, estimate the theta and V_prime_r values at the
132 % surface of the cone. (The V_prime_theta value at the surface of the cone
133 % must, by definition, be zero; see Anderson, p. 371.)
134
135 % Do interpolation to find theta_cone.
136 % Piecewise Cubic Hermite Interpolating Polynomial (PCHIP)
137
138 theta_cone = pchip(V_prime_theta_vec,theta_vec,0);
139
140 end
141




                                       572
CA5.h Given θcone find θshock

Filename: given_supersonic_cone_find_shock_4.m


1 function [shock_half_angle, ...
2 theta_vec,V_prime_vec,Mach_vec, ...
3 partially_stagnated_P_vec,partially_stagnated_T_vec] = ...
4 given_supersonic_cone_find_shock_4(cone_half_angle,num_theta, ...
5 Mach_inf,P_inf,T_inf,gamma)
6 %
7 % This function takes, as input, the Mach number and angle of a
8 % supersonic cone flying through an atmosphere with zero angle of attack,
9 % along with the properties of that atmosphere. It returns, as output,
10 % the resulting shock wave angle created by that cone, along with the
11 % flow velocities, partially stagnated pressures, and partially stagnated
12 % temperatures created by that shock.
13 % This is done by using the Taylor-MacColl codes to find the cones that
14 % support various conical shocks, then implementing a root-finding
15 % algorithm to home in on the shock supported by the specified cone.
16 %
17 % Input terms:
18 %
19 % cone_half_angle = ; num_theta = ;
20 % Mach_inf = ; P_inf = ; T_inf = ; gamma = ;
21 %
22 % where
23 %
24 % cone_half_angle = the angular distance, in radians, from the central
25 % axis of the cone to its outer surface;
26 %
27 % num_theta = the number of theta values, from the shock wave
28 % to the cone, that flowfield calculations should be
29 % done at;
30 %
31 % Mach_inf = the freestream Mach number of the atmospheric gas
32 % the cone is flying through;
33 %
34 % P_inf = the freestream pressure of the atmospheric gas the
35 % cone is flying through;
36 %
37 %
38 % T_inf = the freestream temperature of the atmospheric gas
39 % the cone is flying through;
40 %
41 % and
42 %
43 % gamma = the heat capacity ratio of the atmospheric gas the
44 % cone is flying through.
45 %
46 % Usage:
47 %
48 % [shock_half_angle,...
49 % theta_vec,V_prime_vec,Mach_prime_vec...
50 % partially_stagnated_P_vec,partially_stagnated_T_vec] = ...
51 % given_supersonic_cone_find_shock_4(cone_half_angle,num_theta,...
52 % Mach_inf,P_inf,T_inf,gamma)
                                       573
53
54 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
55 %
56 % This routine directly calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
57 %
58 % m2_behind_cone_shock
59 % delta_behind_cone_shock
60 % given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4
61 % delta_m2_behind_cone_shock
62 % V_prime_r_theta
63 % find_v_primes_behind_shock_6
64 % StagPress
65 % StagTemp
66 %
67 %
68 % This routine indirectly calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
69 %
70 % taylor_maccoll_3 (via: given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4,
71 % find_v_primes_behind_shock_6)
72
73 tic
74
75 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
76 %
77 % Validation
78 %
79 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
80
81 % Validate the data input.
82
83 if cone_half_angle < 0
84 error( 'The half-angle of the cone must be no lower than zero.' )
85 else
86 if isreal(cone_half_angle)==0
87 error( 'The half-angle of the cone must be a real number.' )
88 else
89 if cone_half_angle > pi/2
90 error( 'The half-angle of the cone must be no larger than pi/2.' )
91 else
92 end
93 end
94 end
95
96 if Mach_inf < 1
97 error( 'The freestream Mach number must be no lower than one.' )
98 else
99 if isreal(Mach_inf)==0
100 error( 'The freestream Mach number must be a real number.' )
101 else
102 end
103 end
104
105 if T_inf < 0
106 error( 'The freestream temperature must be no lower than zero.' )
107 else
108 if isreal(T_inf)==0
109 error( 'The freestream temperature must be a real number.' )
110 else
                                       574
111 end
112 end
113
114 if P_inf < 0
115 error( 'The freestream pressure must be no lower than zero.' )
116 else
117 if isreal(P_inf)==0
118 error( 'The freestream pressure must be a real number.' )
119 else
120 end
121 end
122
123 if num_theta <= 0
124 error( 'The number of angular locations within the flowfield must be at least
one.' )
125 else
126 if isreal(num_theta)==0
127 error( 'The number of angular locations within the flowfield must be a real
number.' )
128 else
129 if mod(num_theta,1) >= 1e-12
130 error( 'The number of angular locations within the flowfield must be a whole
number.')
131 else
132 end
133 end
134 end
135
136 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
137 % UUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUU
138 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
139 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
140 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
141 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
142 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
143 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
144 %
145 % Find Upper and Lower Limits of Shock Angle
146 %
147 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
148 % UUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUU
149 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
150 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
151 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
152 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
153 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
154 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
155
156 % Before a rootfinding search for the correct shock angle / cone angle
157 % combo can be performed, the upper and lower limits of acceptable shock
158 % angle values must be determined for the given freestream Mach number and
159 % atmospheric gamma value.
160
161 % The lowest acceptable shock angle will be the one that gives a Mach
162 % number behind the shock which is exactly equal to the freestream Mach
163 % number. Spuriously low shock angles may be identified by the following
164 % characteristics:
165 % 1) negative delta values;
                                       575
166 % 2) imaginary values of M2; and / or
167 % 3) values of M2 in excess of the freestream Mach number.
168
169 fun1 = @(theta_s) abs(Mach_inf - real(m2_behind_cone_shock(
theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma ))) ;
170
171 theta_s_lower = fminbnd(fun1,0,pi/2)
172
173 % The highest acceptable shock angle will be the one that gives the largest
174 % possible value of delta. Spuriously high shock angles will result in
175 % decreases in the angle of flow deflection, corresponding to the detached,
176 % bow-shock / strong-shock solution.
177
178 fun2 = @(theta_s) abs(delta_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma ) -
delta_behind_cone_shock( (theta_s+0.001),Mach_inf,gamma )) ;
179
180 theta_s_upper = fminbnd(fun2,theta_s_lower,pi/2) + 0.0005
181
182 % Once the range of valid shock wave angles is known, these can be used, in
183 % conjunction with a cone-angle-finding subroutine, to determine the
184 % shock wave angle that corresponds to the actual cone being used.
185
186 fun3 = @(theta_s) abs(cone_half_angle - given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4(
theta_s,
Mach_inf,gamma )) ;
187
188 shock_half_angle = fminbnd(fun3,theta_s_lower,theta_s_upper) ;
189
190 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
191 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
192 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
193 %
194 % Taylor-MacColl
195 %
196 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
197 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
198 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
199
200 % Given the true value of theta_s, back out all the other terms associated
201 % with this supersonic cone by running through the Taylor-MacColl relations
202 % one more time.
203
204 % First, calculate the deflection angle and Mach number for the slowed-down
205 % flow immediately behind the shock.
206
207 [ delta,Mach_2 ] = delta_m2_behind_cone_shock( shock_half_angle,Mach_inf,gamma
) ;
208
209 % Second, using this information, find the normal and radial components of
210 % the flow velocity immediately behind the shock.
211
212 [ ~,V_prime_r_at_theta_max,V_prime_theta_at_theta_max ] = V_prime_r_theta(
shock_half_angle,
delta,Mach_2,gamma ) ;
213
214 % Third, use this information to calculate the flowfield behind the shock,
215 % by working inward from the shock toward the cone. The angle at which the
216 % V_prime_theta = 0 must be the angle of the cone. (Anderson, p. 371)
                                       576
217
218 [ V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec,theta_vec ] = ...
219 find_v_primes_behind_shock_6( shock_half_angle,cone_half_angle,num_theta, ...
220 V_prime_r_at_theta_max,V_prime_theta_at_theta_max, ...
221 gamma ) ;
222
223 % Once their two orthogonal velocity components are known, the V_primes for
224 % all theta values can be computed.
225
226 V_prime_vec = sqrt( (V_prime_r_vec.^2) + (V_prime_theta_vec.^2) ) ;
227
228 % The associated Mach numbers can now be computed, using eq. 10.16 from
229 % Anderson (p. 371).
230
231 rad_den_vec = ( ( (V_prime_vec.^-2) - 1 ) * ( gamma - 1 ) ) ;
232
233 Mach_vec = sqrt( 2 ./ rad_den_vec ) ;
234
235 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
236 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
237 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
238 %
239 % Partial Stagnation Relationships
240 %
241 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
242 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
243 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
244
245 % Standard "calorically perfect," ideal-gas relationships can then be used
246 % to determine the stagnated pressures and temperatures behind the shock.
247
248 delta_Mach_vec = Mach_inf - Mach_vec ;
249
250 [ partially_stagnated_P_vec ] = StagPress(P_inf,gamma,delta_Mach_vec) ;
251
252 [ partially_stagnated_T_vec ] = StagTemp(T_inf,gamma,delta_Mach_vec) ;
253
254 toc
255
256 end
257




                                       577
CA5.i Find Delta and M2 Behind Cone Shock

Filename: delta_m2_behind_cone_shock.m


1 function [ delta,Mach_2 ] = delta_m2_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
2 %Usage:
3 % [ delta,Mach_2 ] = delta_m2_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
4 % The purpose of this function is to return values for the Mach number
5 % and deflection angle directly behind an oblique shockwave on a
6 % supersonic cone at zero angle of attack, given an initial shockwave
7 % angle, a freestream Mach number, and the gamma value for the gas the
8 % cone is travelling through.
9 %
10 % Input terms:
11 % theta_s=; Mach_inf=; gamma=;
12 % where
13 % theta_s = the angle of the shockwave (in radians);
14 % Mach_inf = the freestream Mach number; and
15 % gamma = the ratio of specific heats of the gas (unitless).
16 %
17 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
18 %
19 % This subroutine corresponds to step 1 of 5 in the algorithm for numerical
20 % flowfield calculations, as given by Anderson (Modern Compressible Flow,
21 % Ch. 10.4, pp. 371-2).
22 %
23 % The velocity component of the freestream Mach number orthogonal to the
24 % shockwave is calculated first, using eqn (4.7) from Anderson.
25
26 Mach_n_inf = Mach_inf * sin(theta_s) ;
27
28 % The deflection angle behind the shock is then computed using the
29 % theta-beta-M relationship, where the assumed shock wave angle theta_s
30 % stands in for beta. Also, the deflection angle behind the shock is termed
31 % delta rather than theta. (These substitutions follow Anderson's
32 % convention in Ch. 10 of Modern Compressible Flow.)
33
34 tbm_num = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (sin(theta_s)^2) ) - 1 ;
35
36 tbm_den = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (gamma+cos(2*theta_s)) ) + 2 ;
37
38 delta = atan( 2 * cot(theta_s) * (tbm_num/tbm_den) ) ;
39
40 % Using this information, the Mach number component of the shocked flow
41 % normal to, and immediately behind, the shockwave can be calculated, using
42 % eqn (4.10) from Anderson.
43
44 Mn2_num = (2/(gamma-1)) + (Mach_n_inf^2);
45
46 Mn2_den = ( (2*gamma/(gamma-1)) * (Mach_n_inf^2) ) - 1 ;
47
48 Mach_n_2 = sqrt( Mn2_num / Mn2_den ) ;
49
50 % Using this information, the absolute magnitude of the Mach number of the
51 % shocked flow immediately behind the shockwave can be calculated, using
52 % eqn (4.12) from Anderson.
                                         578
53
54 Mach_2 = Mach_n_2 / sin (theta_s - delta) ;
55
56 end


CA5.j Find the Nondimensional Velocity of Flow Immediately Behind an Oblique

Shock

Filename: V_prime_r_theta.m


1 function [ V_prime,V_prime_r,V_prime_theta ] = V_prime_r_theta(
theta_s,delta,Mach_2,gamma )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ V_prime,V_prime_r,V_prime_theta ] = V_prime_r_theta(
theta_s,delta,Mach_2,gamma )
6 % The purpose of this function is to find the nondimensional velocity of
7 % flow immediately behind an oblique shock, generated by a cone flying
8 % at zero angle of attack. It also generates the corresponding angular
9 % and radial components of this nondimensional velocity.
10 %
11 % Input terms:
12 % theta_s=; delta=; Mach_2=; gamma=;
13 % where
14 % theta_s = the shockwave angle of the oblique shock generated by
15 % the cone;
16 % delta = the angle of deflection of the incoming flow, created
17 % by the shockwave;
18 % Mach_2 = the Mach number of the flow immediately behind the
19 % shock;
20 % and
21 % gamma = the heat capacity ratio of the gas the cone is flying
22 % through.
23
24 % This subroutine corresponds to step 2 of 5 in the algorithm for numerical
25 % flowfield calculations, as given by Anderson (Modern Compressible Flow,
26 % Ch. 10.4, pp. 371-2).
27
28 % Find the nondimensional velocity, V_prime, of the flow directly behind
29 % the shock.
30
31 V_prime = ( ( 2 / ((gamma-1)*(Mach_2^2)) ) + 1 ) ^ (-1/2) ;
32
33 % Find the internal angle, theta_int, of the triangle defined by V_prime_r
34 % and V_prime_theta.
35
36 theta_int = theta_s - delta ;
37
38 % Find the radial component of the nondimensional velocity, V_prime_r.
39
40 V_prime_r = cos(theta_int) * V_prime ;
41
42 % Find the angular component of the nondimensional velocity, V_prime_theta.
                                       579
43
44 V_prime_theta = sin(theta_int) * V_prime ;
45
46 end
47




CA5.k Determine The Velocity Components of The Supersonic Flow Over a Quasi-

Infinite Cone

Filename: find_v_primes_behind_shock_6.m


1 function [ V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec,theta_vec ] = ...
2 find_v_primes_behind_shock_6( theta_max,theta_min,num_theta, ...
3 V_prime_r_at_theta_max,V_prime_theta_at_theta_max, ...
4 gamma )
5 %
6 % The purpose of this function is to determine the velocity components of
7 % the supersonic flow over a quasi-infinite cone, in the region behind
8 % the cone's shock wave. This is done by solving the Taylor-MacColl
9 % equation numerically, with the shock-wave angle and nondimensionalized
10 % velocity behind the shock being used as boundary values.
11 %_
12 % Usage:
13 %
14 % [ V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec,theta_vec ] = ...
15 % find_v_primes_behind_shock_6( theta_max,theta_min,num_theta,...
16 % V_prime_r_at_theta_max,V_prime_theta_at_theta_max,...
17 % gamma )
18
19 % This subroutine corresponds to steps 3-4 of 5 in the algorithm for numerical
20 % flowfield calculations, as given by Anderson (Modern Compressible Flow,
21 % Ch. 10.4, pp. 371-2).
22
23 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
24 %
25 %
26 % 1) This routine differs from its predecessor,
27 % find_v_primes_behind_shock_5, in that all code for conditioning the
28 % output has been removed. This ensures that both physically valid,
29 % positive V_prime_theta values, and unphysical, negative
30 % V_prime_theta values, will be returned by this routine.
31 %
32 % Returning both types of V_prime_theta values facilitates this
33 % routine's use in the iterative stage of
34 % given_theta_shock_find_theta_cone_4, as the latter routine uses
35 % progressively-narrower integration ranges with ode113 to home in
36 % on the correct value of theta_cone.
37 %
38 %
39 % 2) This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
40 %
41 % taylor_maccoll_3

                                       580
42
43 theta_vec = theta_max:-(theta_max - theta_min)/(num_theta-1):theta_min;
44
45 % A second row vector is set up to specify the initial conditions, in terms
46 % of nondimensionalized flow velocities directly behind the shock.
47
48 V_prime_ic_vec = [V_prime_r_at_theta_max,-V_prime_theta_at_theta_max];
49
50 %MATLAB CORE Create or modify options structure for ODE and PDE solvers
51 options = odeset( 'RelTol',1e-5,'AbsTol',1e-8);
52
53 %[theta_vec,V_prime_vec] = ode113(@(theta_vec,V_prime_vec)taylor_maccoll_3(
theta_vec,
V_prime_vec,gamma ),theta_vec,V_prime_ic_vec,options);
54
55 %Solve stiff differential equations and DAEs — variable order method %say
56 %somthing about tolerances %%ERROR
57
58 [theta_vec,V_prime_vec] = ode15s(@(theta_vec,V_prime_vec)taylor_maccoll_3(
theta_vec,
V_prime_vec,gamma ),theta_vec,V_prime_ic_vec,options);
59
60 % Condition the output results so that the velocities returned are listed
61 % in order of ascending theta values.
62
63 theta_vec = flipud(theta_vec);
64
65 V_prime_r_vec = flipud(V_prime_vec(:,1)) ;
66
67 V_prime_theta_vec = -flipud(V_prime_vec(:,2)) ;
68
69 end
70




                                       581
CA5.l Expression of the Taylor-Maccoll Equation

Filename: taylor_maccoll_3.m


1 function [ V_prime_deriv_vec ] = taylor_maccoll_3( theta,V_prime_vec,gamma )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ V_prime_deriv_vec ] = taylor_maccoll_3( theta,V_prime_vec,gamma )
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to provide an expression of the
8 % Taylor-MacColl equation, as given via eqn. 10.15 in Anderson's
9 % Modern Compressible Flow, 3rd ed. More specifically, it is meant to
10 % solve for the first and second derivative of the nondimensionalized
11 % radial velocity of supersonic flow over a quasi-infinite cone, with
12 % respect to the theta variable. The numerical solutions to the equation
13 % are then determined using a solver such as ode23.
14 %
15 % This routine is based on the function "taymaceqn" written by Sercome
16 % and Buttsworth ("Transverse Injection From A Hypersonic Cone", 2004;
17 % p. 110), with corrections being made for an apparent sign
18 % error in the original code.
19 %
20 % Input terms:
21 % theta=; V_prime_vec=; gamma=;
22 % where
23 % theta = the angle between the axis of the cone and the
24 % flow direction of interest;
25 % V_prime_vec = [ V_prime_r, V_prime_theta ]
26 % where
27 % V_prime_r = nondimensionalized radial
28 % velocity of supersonic flow
29 % over the cone;
30 % and
31 % V_prime_theta = dV_prime_r_over_dtheta
32 % (eqn. 10.14, Anderson)
33 % = nondimensionalized angular
34 % velocity of supersonic flow
35 % over the cone;
36 % and
37 % gamma = the ratio of specific heats for the gas through
38 % which the cone is flying.
39 %
40 % Output terms:
41 % [ V_prime_theta
42 % dV_prime_theta_over_dtheta ]
43 %
44 % = [ dV_prime_r_over_dtheta
45 % dV_prime_theta_over_dtheta ]
46 %
47 % = [ dV_prime_r_over_dtheta
48 % d2V_prime_r_over_dtheta2 ]
49
50 theta = theta;
51
52 V_prime_deriv_prelim_vec = zeros(2,1);
                                       582
53
54 % Set dV_prime_r_over_dtheta = V_prime_theta, as in equation 10.14 by
55 % Anderson.
56
57 dV_prime_r_over_dtheta = V_prime_vec(2);
58
59 V_prime_deriv_prelim_vec(1,1) = dV_prime_r_over_dtheta;
60
61 % Set V_prime_r.
62
63 V_prime_r = V_prime_vec(1);
64
65 a = (gamma-1)/2;
66
67 % Define the B term. This term is equal to the
68 % [1 - V_prime_r^2 + (dV_prime_r/dtheta)^2]
69 % term in eqn. (10.15).
70
71 B_term = 1 - ( (V_prime_r) .^ 2 ) - ( (dV_prime_r_over_dtheta) .^ 2 ) ;
72
73 c_term_1 = ( -a .* B_term .* ( (2.*V_prime_r) +
(dV_prime_r_over_dtheta.*cot(theta))
) ) ;
74
75 c_term_2 = ((dV_prime_r_over_dtheta).^2) .* (V_prime_r) ;
76
77 c = c_term_1 + c_term_2 ;
78
79 d_term_1 = a.*B_term;
80
81 d_term_2 = ( -( (dV_prime_r_over_dtheta) .^ 2 ) ) ;
82
83 d = d_term_1 + d_term_2;
84
85 %V_prime_deriv_prelim_vec(2,1) = c./d;
86
87 d2V_prime_r_over_dtheta2 = c./d;
88
89 V_prime_deriv_prelim_vec(2,1) = d2V_prime_r_over_dtheta2;
90
91 V_prime_deriv_vec = V_prime_deriv_prelim_vec;
92
93 end
94




                                       583
CA5.m Find M2 Behind an Oblique Shock

Filename: m2_behind_cone_shock.m


1 function [ Mach_2 ] = m2_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ Mach_2 ] = m2_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
6 % The purpose of this function is to return values for the Mach number
7 % behind an oblique shockwave on a
8 % supersonic cone at zero angle of attack, given an initial shockwave
9 % angle, a freestream Mach number, and the gamma value for the gas the
10 % cone is travelling through.
11 %
12 % Input terms:
13 % theta_s=; Mach_inf=; gamma=;
14 % where
15 % theta_s = the angle of the shockwave (in radians);
16 % Mach_inf = the freestream Mach number; and
17 % gamma = the ratio of specific heats of the gas (unitless).
18
19 % This subroutine corresponds to step 1 of 5 in the algorithm for numerical
20 % flowfield calculations, as given by Anderson (Modern Compressible Flow,
21 % Ch. 10.4, pp. 371-2).
22
23 % The velocity component of the freestream Mach number orthogonal to the
24 % shockwave is calculated first, using eqn (4.7) from Anderson.
25
26 Mach_n_inf = Mach_inf * sin(theta_s) ;
27
28 % The deflection angle behind the shock is then computed using the
29 % theta-beta-M relationship, where the assumed shock wave angle theta_s
30 % stands in for beta. Also, the deflection angle behind the shock is termed
31 % delta rather than theta. (These substitutions follow Anderson's
32 % convention in Ch. 10 of Modern Compressible Flow.)
33
34 tbm_num = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (sin(theta_s)^2) ) - 1 ;
35
36 tbm_den = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (gamma+cos(2*theta_s)) ) + 2 ;
37
38 delta = atan( 2 * cot(theta_s) * (tbm_num/tbm_den) ) ;
39
40 % Using this information, the Mach number component of the shocked flow
41 % normal to, and immediately behind, the shockwave can be calculated, using
42 % eqn (4.10) from Anderson.
43
44 Mn2_num = (2/(gamma-1)) + (Mach_n_inf^2);
45
46 Mn2_den = ( (2*gamma/(gamma-1)) * (Mach_n_inf^2) ) - 1 ;
47
48 Mach_n_2 = sqrt( Mn2_num / Mn2_den ) ;
49
50 % Using this information, the absolute magnitude of the Mach number of the
51 % shocked flow immediately behind the shockwave can be calculated, using
52 % eqn (4.12) from Anderson.
                                       584
53
54 Mach_2 = Mach_n_2 / sin (theta_s - delta) ;
55
56 end
57




CA5.n Find The M2 Deflection Angle Behind an Oblique Shockwave

Filename: delta_behind_cone_shock.m


1 function [ delta ] = delta_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ delta ] = delta_behind_cone_shock( theta_s,Mach_inf,gamma )
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to return values for the Mach number
8 % and deflection angle directly behind an oblique shockwave on a
9 % supersonic cone at zero angle of attack, given an initial shockwave
10 % angle, a freestream Mach number, and the gamma value for the gas the
11 % cone is travelling through.
12 %
13 % Input terms:
14 % theta_s=; Mach_inf=; gamma=;
15 % where
16 % theta_s = the angle of the shockwave (in radians);
17 % Mach_inf = the freestream Mach number; and
18 % gamma = the ratio of specific heats of the gas (unitless).
19
20 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
21 %
22 % 1) This subroutine corresponds to step 1 of 5 in the algorithm for numerical
23 % flowfield calculations, as given by Anderson (Modern Compressible Flow,
24 % Ch. 10.4, pp. 371-2).
25
26 % The deflection angle behind the shock is then computed using the
27 % theta-beta-M relationship, where the assumed shock wave angle theta_s
28 % stands in for beta. Also, the deflection angle behind the shock is termed
29 % delta rather than theta. (These substitutions follow Anderson's
30 % convention in Ch. 10 of Modern Compressible Flow.)
31
32 tbm_num = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (sin(theta_s)^2) ) - 1 ;
33
34 tbm_den = ( (Mach_inf^2) * (gamma+cos(2*theta_s)) ) + 2 ;
35
36 delta = atan( 2 * cot(theta_s) * (tbm_num/tbm_den) ) ;
37
38 end
39

CA5.o Stagnation Temperature Calculator

Filename: StagTemp.m


1 function [ stagnationT ] = StagTemp( temp,gamma,mach )
2 %
3 % StagTemp Function for calculating stagnation temperature
4 %
5 % Usage:
6 %
7 % [ stagnationT ] = StagTemp( temp,gamma,mach )
8 %
9 % freestream temperature
10 % temperature of the gas in the bore of the ram accelerator
11
12 stagterm = 1 + (((gamma-1)/2) * (mach.^2));
13 stagnationT = temp .* stagterm;
14
15 end
16




CA5.p Stagnation Pressure Calculator

Filename: StagPress.m


1 function [ stagnationP ] = StagPress(pressure,gamma,mach)
2 %
3 % StagPress Function for calculating stagnation pressure
4 %
5 % Usage:
6 %
7 % [ stagnationP ] = StagPress(pressure,gamma,mach)
8 %
9 % freestream pressure
10 % pressure of the gas in the bore of the ram accelerator
11 %
12 stagPquant = 1+((gamma-1)/2)*(mach.^2);
13 stagPexp = gamma / (gamma-1);
14 stagPterm = stagPquant .^ stagPexp;
15 stagnationP = pressure .* stagPterm;
16
17 end

35 Sound_Speed = 299.60; %Units m/s
36 temp = 298; % Units Kelvin %Freestream Temperature

50 T_inf = temp;

CA5.r V Prime Function

Filename: V_prime_sys.m


1 function [ V_prime_c ] = V_prime_sys(V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec)
2 %
3 %
4 % Use;
5 % [ V_prime_c ] = V_prime_sys(V_prime_r_vec,V_prime_theta_vec)
6 %
                                       613
7
8 V_prime_c = sqrt((V_prime_r_vec.^2)+(V_prime_theta_vec.^2));
9
10 end
11




CA5.s Find Mach Numbers in System

Filename: Mach_sys.m


1 function [ mach ] = Mach_sys(gamma,V_prime_c)
2 %From page 371 in Anderson MCF.
3 % From equation 10.16, rearranged to solve for Mach
4 %
5 % Use:
6 % [ mach ] = Mach_sys(gamma,V_prime_c)
7 %
8 term0 = sqrt(2).*V_prime_c;
9 term1 = sqrt(gamma-1-((V_prime_c.^2)*gamma)+(V_prime_c.^2));
10
11 mach = term0./term1;
12 end
CA5.t Find System Temperatures

Filename: actual_temp_relationship.m


1
2 function actual_temp = actual_temp_relationship(Mach_inf,mach,gamma,temp)
3 %
4 %page 80 MCF by anderson (3.28)
5 %
6 % Use:
7 %
8 % actual_temp = actual_temp_relationship(Mach_inf,mach,gamma,temp)
9 %
10
11 delta_M = Mach_inf - mach;
12 delta_M_squared = delta_M.^2;
13 term0 = 1;
14 term1 = ((gamma-1)/2).*delta_M_squared;
15
16 actual_temp = (term0 + term1).*temp;
17
18 end
19




                                       614
CA5.u Aid for Finding Points in First Ray After Shockwave

Filename: y_delta.m


1 function y_delta1 = y_delta(l_toroid,x_shock,delta)
2
3 %this function is used to help find the intersection points in the first
4 %ray after the shock wave
5
6 y_delta1 = ((l_toroid/2)-x_shock)*tan(delta);
7
8 end




CA5.v M2 Calculator

Filename: Mach_2_2nd_shock.m


1
2 function M_2_2nd_shock = Mach_2_2nd_shock(mach,beta_old,gamma,theta_M_1_cart)
3
4 %page 135 MCF by anderson
5 %
6
7 %first we need to find Mn1
8
9 Mn1 = mach.*sin(beta_old); %4.7
10
11 term0l = Mn1.^2;
12 term0r = 2/(gamma-1);
13 term1l = ((2*gamma)/(gamma-1)).*(Mn1.^2);
14 term1r = 1;
15
16 %4.10 Anderson Page 135
17
18 top = term0l+term0r;
19 bottom = term1l-term1r;
20 Mn2 = sqrt(top./bottom);
21
22 M_2_2nd_shock = Mn2./sin(beta_old-theta_M_1_cart);
23
24 end




                                       615
CA5.w βnew Calculator

Filename: beta_new_calc.m


1 function [ beta_new ] = beta_new_calc(mach,gamma,theta_oblique)
2 %lambda-kai-theta-beta-theta relation page 143 Modern Compressable Flow
3 % Note that theta_oblique comes from the theat in the oblique shock
4 % geometry diagram in Anderson on page 134, figure 4.7
5
6 term0lam = ((mach.^2)-1).^2;
7 term1lam = 1+((gamma-1)./2).*(mach.^2);
8 term2lam = 1+((gamma+1)./2).*(mach.^2);
9 term3lam = tan(theta_oblique).^2;
10
11 lambda = (term0lam-(3*(term1lam .* term2lam .* term3lam))).^.5;
12
13 term0kai = ((mach.^2)-1).^3;
14 term1kai = 1+(((gamma-1)./2).*(mach.^2));
15 term2kai_1 = 1;
16 term2kai_2 = ((gamma-1)./2).*(mach.^2);
17 term2kai_3 = ((gamma+1)./4).*(mach.^4);
18 term2kai = term2kai_1 + term2kai_2 + term2kai_3;
19 term3kai = tan(theta_oblique).^2;
20
21 kai = (term0kai - (9.*(term1kai.*( term2kai ).*term3kai)))./(lambda.^3);
22
23 %delta = 1 for weak shock solution
24 delta = 1;
25
26 term0beta = (mach.^2)-1;
27 term0cfun = (4.*pi.*delta)+acos(kai);
28 term1beta = 2.*lambda.*cos(term0cfun./3);
29
30 term2beta = 1+(((gamma-1)./2).*(mach.^2));
31
32 tbeta = (term0beta + term1beta)./(3.*term2beta.*tan(theta_oblique));
33
34 beta_new = atan(tbeta);
35
36 end




                                       616
CA5.x Taylor-Maccoll Oblique Shock Relations Busemann Dimensions

Filename: TM_Busemann_Dimensions.m


1 function [ x_intersect_inlet_bottom , y_intersect_inlet_bottom ,
x_intersect_inlet_top ,
y_intersect_inlet_top , throat_size , l_toroid , xsi , ysi] =
TM_Busemann_Dimensions(
cone_half_angle_input , inlet_input , gamma_input , temp_input , pressure_input ,
Mach_input )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ x_intersect_inlet_bottom , y_intersect_inlet_bottom , x_intersect_inlet_top
,
y_intersect_inlet_top , throat_size , l_toroid , xsi , ysi] =
TM_Busemann_Dimensions(
cone_half_angle , inlet_input , gamma_input , temp_input , pressure_input ,
Mach_input )
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to return values needed for
8 % constructing a Busemann toroid based on calculating the shock angle for
9 % a specified cone using Taylor-Maccoll.
10
11 %%%%% Model Settings %%%%%%%%
12
13 inlet_size = inlet_input;
14 cone_half_angle = deg2rad(cone_half_angle_input);
15 theta_cone = cone_half_angle;
16
17 %Ram Tube
18 %Mach_inf = 4; %look at 2,
19
20 %Ignition tube
21 Mach_inf = Mach_input;
22
23 %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
24 %Hiroshima University Ram tube
25 %Page 107, Ram Accelerators, K. Takayama, A. Sasoh
26 %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
27 %Propellant = '1.4CH_4 + 2O_2 + 4.3CO_2';
28 gamma = gamma_input;
29 %freestream_enthalpy = 481.97*1000; % Units J/kg
30 %Sound_Speed = 299.60; %Units m/s
31 temp = temp_input; % Units Kelvin %Freestream Temperature
32 pressure = pressure_input; %Units Mpa %Freestream Pressure
33
34 %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
35 %Hiroshima University Ignition tube
36 %Page 107, Ram Accelerators, K. Takayama, A. Sasoh
37 %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
38 % Propellant = '1.4CH_4 + 2O_2 + 2CO_2';
39 % gamma = 1.3344;
40 % freestream_enthalpy = 470.60*1000; % Units J/kg
41 % Sound_Speed = 317.92; %Units m/s
42 % temp = 298; % Units Kelvin
                                       617
43 % pressure = 0.3; %Units Mpa
44
45 T_inf = temp;
46 P_inf = pressure;
47
48 %set the spead of rays in the system, the actual number of rays is less
49 %because we remove rays that go through the Busemann toroid
50 ray_spread = 200; %60
51 theta_num = ray_spread;
52
53 % %these values help with visibility of the flowfield arrows
54 % flowfield_linewidth = 3;
55 % flowfield_MaxHeadSize = 2; %2
56
57 theta_min = 0.01*(pi/180) ;
58 num_theta = theta_num;
59
60 %%%%%% Taylor Maccoll %%%%%%%%
61
62 [shock_half_angle, ...
63 theta_vec,V_prime_vec,Mach_prime_vec ...
64 partially_stagnated_P_vec,partially_stagnated_T_vec] = ...
65 given_supersonic_cone_find_shock_4(cone_half_angle,num_theta, ...
66 Mach_inf,P_inf,T_inf,gamma)
67
68 %for cone method %%%%%%%
69 theta_s = shock_half_angle;
70 theta_max = theta_s;
71
72 %%%%%% Shock Intersection %%%%%%%
73
74 xsi = (inlet_size/2)/tan(theta_s);
75 ysi = (inlet_size/2);
76
77 %%% Planar Shock at shock intersection means xsi = l_toroid/2
78
79 l_toroid = xsi * 2;
80
81 x_intersect_inlet_bottom = xsi;
82 y_intersect_inlet_bottom = tan(theta_cone) * xsi;
83
84 x_intersect_inlet_top = xsi;
85 y_intersect_inlet_top = ysi + (ysi - y_intersect_inlet_bottom);
86
87 y_o = y_intersect_inlet_bottom;
88
89 throat_size = y_intersect_inlet_top - y_intersect_inlet_bottom;
90
91 end
92




                                       618
CA5.y Taylor-Maccoll Toroid Volume Calculator

Filename: toroid_volume_calc.m


1 function [ toroid_volume ] = toroid_volume_calc(inlet_size,throat_size,l_toroid)
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 % [ toroid_volume ] = toroid_volume_calc(inlet_size,throat_size,l_toroid)
5 %
6 %
7
8 H = l_toroid;
9 h= l_toroid/2;
10 R = inlet_size/2;
11 r = throat_size/2;
12
13 %find volume of a frustum
14 V_frustum = ((pi*h)/3)*(R^2 + (R*r) + r^2);
15
16 %find volume of cylinder
17 V_cylinder = pi*(R^2)*H;
18
19 toroid_volume = V_cylinder-(2*V_frustum);
20
21 end
22




CA5.z Kantrowitz Toroid Volume Calculator

Filename: toroid_volume_calc_cone_half_angle.m


1 function [ toroid_volume ] =
toroid_volume_calc_cone_half_angle(inlet_size,throat_size,
theta_cone_half_angle)
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 %
toroid_volume_calc_cone_half_angle(inlet_size,throat_size,theta_cone_half_angle)
6 %
7
8 y = (inlet_size/2) - (throat_size/2);
9 x = y/tan(deg2rad(theta_cone_half_angle));
10
11 H = 2 * x;
12 h= H/2;
13 R = inlet_size/2;
14 r = throat_size/2;
15
16 %find volume of a frustum
17 V_frustum = ((pi*h)/3)*(R^2 + (R*r) + r^2);
18
                                       619
19 %find volume of cylinder
20 V_cylinder = pi*(R^2)*H;
21
22 toroid_volume = V_cylinder-(2*V_frustum);
23
24 end

CODING APPENDIX.6 Coding Appendix Chapter 6

This is a collection of all the MATLAB code used in Chapter 6

CA6.a Convective Heat Transfer Calculation

Filename: convective_heat_flux.m


1 function [heat_flux_at_wall] = ...
2 convective_heat_flux(velocity, ...
3 enthalpy_gas_static,density_gas,pressure_at_wall,gamma, ...
4 T_avg_freestream,T_wall)
5 %
6 % The purpose of this function is to implement D. W. Bogdanoff's
7 % convective-heat-transfer calculation formula from Appendix A of the
8 % paper
9 % "Strategies to protect ram accelerator projectiles from in-tube
10 % gasdynamic heating," J. Phys. IV France, v. 10 (2000), pp. 9-10.
11 %
12 % Usage:
13 %
14 % [heat_flux_at_wall] = ...
15 % convective_heat_flux(velocity,...
16 % enthalpy_gas_static,density_gas,pressure_at_wall,gamma,...
17 % T_avg_freestream,T_wall)
18
19 %length = sqrt( ((1/3)^2) + ((4/5)^2) )
20
21 length = 0.0620 ;
22
23 molar_mass_mixture = ( ((8*2.01588) + (1*31.9988)) / 9 ) * (1/1000) ;
24
25 R = 8.3145 ; % J mol^-1 K^-1
26
27 speed_of_sound = sqrt(R * T_avg_freestream * gamma / molar_mass_mixture ) ;
28
29 Mach_num = velocity / speed_of_sound ;
30
31 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
32 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
33 %
34 % Calculate Viscosity
35 %
36 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
37 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
38
39 % golubev, viscosities of gases and gas mixtures, p. 62

                                         622
40
41 % viscosity of H2 at 25 C: 890 (10^-7) g cm^-1 s^-1
42
43 % Viscosity of O2 at 25 C: 2052 (10^-7) g cm^-1 s^-1
44
45 viscosity_H2 = 890e-8 % kg m^-1 s^-1
46
47 viscosity_O2 = 2052e-8 % kg m^-1 s^-1
48
49 viscosity_mixture = ((8*viscosity_H2)+viscosity_O2) / 9 ;
50
51 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
52 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
53 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
54 %
55 % Find Reference Properties
56 %
57 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
58 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
59 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
60
61 T_reference = ( 0.9 * T_avg_freestream ) + ( 0.03 * Mach_num ) + ( 0.1 * T_wall
) ;
62
63 % The calculation of viscosity comes from Lapin, p. 118, eq. 3.61
64
65 viscosity_reference = viscosity_mixture * (T_reference/T_avg_freestream)^0.76 ;
66
67 %density_reference = molar_mass_mixture * pressure_at_wall / (R * T_reference)
;
68
69 density_reference = density_gas * (T_avg_freestream/T_reference) ;
70
71 Reynolds_num_reference = density_reference * velocity * length /
viscosity_reference ;
72
73 skin_friction_coefficient_reference = (2*log10(Reynolds_num_reference)) - 0.65
;
74
75 density_point_2 = molar_mass_mixture * pressure_at_wall / ( R * T_wall )
76
77 %skin_friction_coefficient = skin_friction_coefficient_reference *
(density_reference/density_gas) ; % NOTE: should divide by gas density at point 2
78
79 skin_friction_coefficient = skin_friction_coefficient_reference *
(density_reference/density_point_2) ; % NOTE: should divide by gas density at
point 2
80
81 % recovery factor from Shapiro vol. II, p.1123
82
83 recovery_factor = 0.89 ;
84
85 enthalpy_adiabatic_wall = enthalpy_gas_static * ( 1 + ( recovery_factor *
((gamma-
1)/2) .* (Mach_num.^2) ) ) ;
86
87 %term_1 = 0.5 * skin_friction_coefficient * density_gas .* velocity ; % NOTE:
should
                                       623
use gas density at point 2
88
89 term_1 = 0.5 * skin_friction_coefficient * density_point_2 .* velocity ; %
NOTE: should
use gas density at point 2
90
91 term_2 = enthalpy_gas_static + ( recovery_factor .* ((velocity.^2)/2) ) -
enthalpy_adiabatic_wall ;
92
93 heat_flux_at_wall = term_1 .* term_2 ;
94 end

89 % [x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,...
90 % inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes,outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes] = ...
91 %
create_ring_of_boxes_7(size_of_cube,number_of_meshgrid_points,number_of_cubes,...
92 % skip_every_nth_box,cube_orientation,...
93 % plot_ring_of_boxes,plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure)
94
95
96 v = axis;
97 v(1,1) = 0;
98 axis(v)
99
100
101 surf_1_x_mat = x_nozzle_mat;
                                       628
102 surf_1_y_mat = y_nozzle_mat;
103 surf_1_z_mat = z_nozzle_mat;
104
105
106 surf_2_x_mat = x_cylinder_mat;
107 surf_2_y_mat = y_cylinder_mat;
108 surf_2_z_mat = z_cylinder_mat;
109
110 obs_surf_x_mat = x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat;
111 obs_surf_y_mat = y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat;
112 obs_surf_z_mat = z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat;
113
114 n_simulation_runs = 4; %256*2
115 n_point_pairs = 8192*2; %1024 8192*2
116 expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs = 70;
117 contraction_factor_denom =1;

120 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 = +1;
121 true_val = 0;

...

CA6.d Construct Meshgrid Matrices for Busemann Toroid

Filename: Busemann_toroid_7.m


1 function
[diagonal_length_of_leading_cone,diagonal_length_of_frustum,cone_full_angle, ...
2 emissivity_inlet,x_inlet_mat,y_inlet_mat,z_inlet_mat, ...
3 emissivity_nozzle,x_nozzle_mat,y_nozzle_mat,z_nozzle_mat, ...
4 emissivity_cylinder,x_cylinder_mat,y_cylinder_mat,z_cylinder_mat, ...
5 phi_cylinder_mat] = ...
6 Busemann_toroid_7(r_inlet,r_throat,l_Busemann_toroid, ...
                                       629
7 num_r_inlet_cone,phi_num_inlet, ...
8 phi_num_cylinder,h_num_cylinder, ...
9 emissivity_inlet,emissivity_nozzle,emissivity_cylinder, ...
10 plot_Busemann_toroid)
11 %
12 % The purpose of this function is to construct the three major surfaces
13 % that constitute a Busemann toroid: its inlet region, its nozzle region,
14 % and its cylinder region. It will return the coordinates of these three
15 % surfaces as meshgrid matrices in Cartesian coordinates.
16 %
17 % Input terms:
18 %
19 % r_inlet = ; r_throat = ; l_Busemann_toroid = ;
20 % num_r_inlet_cone = ; phi_num_inlet = ;
21 % phi_num_cylinder = ; h_num_cylinder = ;
22 % emissivity_inlet = ; emissivity_nozzle = ; emissivity_cylinder = ;
23 % plot_Busemann_toroid = ;
24 %
25 % where
26 %
27 % r_inlet = the radius of the outermost periphery
28 % of the toroid ;
29 %
30 % r_throat = the radius of the innermost periphery
31 % of the toroid ;
32 %
33 % l_Busemann_toroid = the overall length of the toroid as
34 % measured from its inlet lip to its
35 % nozzle lip;
36 %
37 % num_r_inlet_cone = the number of radial values that will
38 % be assessed for the conical frustom of
39 % the inlet (and, by association, the
40 % nozzle) ;
41 %
42 % phi_num_inlet = the number of angular values that will
43 % be assessed for the conical frustum of
44 % the inlet (and, by association, the
45 % nozzle) ;
46 %
47 % phi_num_cylinder = the number of angular values that will
48 % be assessed for the outer cylindrical
49 % surface of the Busemann toroid ;
50 %
51 % h_num_cylinder = the number of height (z-axis) values
52 % that will be assessed for the outer
53 % cylindrical surface of the Busemann
54 % toroid ;
55 %
56 % emissivity_inlet
57 % = the scaling factor that represents the extent to
58 % which the inlet resembles a true blackbody (in the
59 % range from 0 to 1) ;
60 %
61 % emissivity_nozzle
62 % = the scaling factor that represents the extent to
63 % which the nozzle resembles a true blackbody (in the
64 % range from 0 to 1) ;
                                       630
65 %
66 % emissivity_cylinder
67 % = the scaling factor that represents the extent to
68 % which the cylinder resembles a true blackbody (in
69 % the range from 0 to 1) ;
70 %
71 % and
72 %
73 % plot_Busemann_toroid = the truth value of whether or not this
74 % routine should plot the Busemann
75 % toroid's surfaces (1 = yes, 0 = no).
76 %
77 % Usage:
78 %
79 %
[diagonal_length_of_leading_cone,diagonal_length_of_frustum,cone_full_angle,...
80 % emissivity_inlet,x_inlet_mat,y_inlet_mat,z_inlet_mat,...
81 % emissivity_nozzle,x_nozzle_mat,y_nozzle_mat,z_nozzle_mat,...
82 % emissivity_cylinder,x_cylinder_mat,y_cylinder_mat,z_cylinder_mat,...
83 % phi_cylinder_mat] =...
84 % Busemann_toroid_7(r_inlet,r_throat,l_Busemann_toroid,...
85 % num_r_inlet_cone,phi_num_inlet,...
86 % phi_num_cylinder,h_num_cylinder,...
87 % emissivity_inlet,emissivity_nozzle,emissivity_cylinder,...
88 % plot_Busemann_toroid) ;
89
90 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
91 %
92 % Emissivity terms for the three surfaces have been explicitly
93 % added as input. They are directly returned with the
94 % meshgrids for the corresponding surfaces. This is being done to
95 % facilitate integration of the routine's data with the Daun algorithm
96 % code.
97
98 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
99 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
100 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
101 %
102 % Construct Inlet Frustum
103 %
104 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
105 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
106 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
107
108 % Construct the inlet frustum in spherical coordinates.
109 % Since the frustum is a segment of a conical surface, and physics
110 % conventions are used to describe this system:
111 % a) the r value will be stepped through a series of values:
112 % b) the theta value (angle from the z-axis) is defined by the cone's
113 % angle, and is thus constant; and
114 % c) the phi value (rotation in the xy-plane) ranges from 0 to 2*pi.
115
116 theta = atan( (r_inlet-r_throat) / (l_Busemann_toroid/2) ) ;
117
118 % Calculate and return the parameters required by C111a.
119
120 cone_full_angle = 2 * theta ;
121
                                       631
122 diagonal_length_of_frustum = sec(theta) * (l_Busemann_toroid/2) ;
123
124 full_diagonal_length_of_cone = csc(theta) * r_inlet ;
125
126 diagonal_length_of_leading_cone = full_diagonal_length_of_cone -
diagonal_length_of_frustum ;
127
128 theta_el = pi/2 - theta ;
129
130 r_inlet_cone_min = r_throat * (1/sin(theta)) ;
131
132 r_inlet_cone_max = r_inlet * (1/sin(theta)) ;
133
134 r_inlet_cone_vec = r_inlet_cone_min : (r_inlet_cone_max-r_inlet_cone_min) /
(num_r_inlet_cone-1) : r_inlet_cone_max ;
135
136
137 phi_inlet_vec = 0: (2*pi) / (phi_num_inlet-1) : 2*pi ;
138
139 [r_inlet_cone_mat,phi_mat] = meshgrid(r_inlet_cone_vec,phi_inlet_vec) ;
140
141 theta_el_mat = theta_el .* ones(size(r_inlet_cone_mat)) ;
142
143 % Transform the inlet frustum coordinates into Cartesian coordinates.
144
145 [x_inlet_mat,y_inlet_mat,z_inlet_mat] =
sph2cart(phi_mat,theta_el_mat,r_inlet_cone_mat) ;
146
147 % Translate the inlet frustum, collinear with the z-axis, so that the plane
148 % of the throat intersects the origin.
149
150 z_inlet_mat = z_inlet_mat - (r_throat/tan(theta)) ;
151
152 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
153 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
154 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
155 %
156 % Construct Nozzle Frustum
157 %
158 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
159 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
160 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
161
162 % Generate the nozzle coordinates by reflecting the inlet frustum through
163 % the xy-plane.
164
165 x_nozzle_mat = x_inlet_mat ;
166 y_nozzle_mat = y_inlet_mat ;
167 z_nozzle_mat = -z_inlet_mat ;
168
169 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
170 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
171 %
172 % Construct Cylinder
173 %
174 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
175 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
176
                                       632
177 % Construct the outer radiative surface in cylindrical coordinates.
178
179 phi_cylinder_vec = 0: (2*pi) / (phi_num_cylinder-1) : 2*pi ;
180
181 h_cylinder_vec = -l_Busemann_toroid/2: l_Busemann_toroid / (h_num_cylinder -
1):
l_Busemann_toroid/2 ;
182
183 [phi_cylinder_mat,h_mat] = meshgrid(phi_cylinder_vec,h_cylinder_vec) ;
184
185 r_cylinder_mat = r_inlet * ones(size(phi_cylinder_mat)) ;
186
187 % Transform the outer surface's coordinates into Cartesian coordinates.
188
189 [x_cylinder_mat,y_cylinder_mat,z_cylinder_mat] =
pol2cart(phi_cylinder_mat,r_cylinder_mat,
h_mat) ;
190
191 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
192 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
193 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
194 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
195 %
196 % Plot Surfaces If Asked
197 %
198 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
199 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
200 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
201 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
202
203 if plot_Busemann_toroid == 1
204
205 figure
206
207 surf(x_inlet_mat,y_inlet_mat,z_inlet_mat, 'EdgeColor' ,'flat')
208
209 hold on
210
211 axis equal
212
213 surf(x_nozzle_mat,y_nozzle_mat,z_nozzle_mat, 'EdgeColor' ,'flat')
214
215 surf(x_cylinder_mat,y_cylinder_mat,z_cylinder_mat, 'EdgeColor' ,'flat')
216
217 cva = camva ;
218
219 camva(0.8*cva) ;
220
221 camva( 'manual')
222
223 xlabel( 'x axis')
224 ylabel( 'y axis')
225 zlabel( 'z axis')
226
227 else
228 end
229
230 end
