CA6.e Construct Hyperbolic Toroid Inside Busemann Toroid

Filename: hyperbolic_toroid_for_Busemann_11.m


1 function
[emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid,x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,
z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat, ...
2 vol_of_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
3 inner_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid,outer_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
4 max_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid,min_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
5 max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
6
max_square_area,inner_radial_extent_of_max_square,outer_radial_extent_of_max_squar
e, ...
7 max_quadrilateral_area,h_for_max_area_outer_vertex,r_for_max_area_outer_vertex,
...
8 max_circle_area,r_of_circle_center,max_circle_radius] = ...
9 ...
10 hyperbolic_toroid_for_Busemann_11(r_inlet,r_throat,l_Busemann_toroid, ...
11 num_x_points,phi_num_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
12 emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid, ...
13 plot_hyperbolic_toroid,plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure)
14 %
15 % Considwer a Busemann toroid, a pairing of an outer cylinder and an
16 % inner, converging/diverging surface made from two conical fustrums.
17 % This surface is generated by rotating a radially offset
18 % right triangle around the z-axis, and reflecting it around the
19 % xy-plane.
20 %
21 % Now, suppose there is a hyperbola inside that right triangle, which has
22 % that right triangle's major leg and hypotenuse as its asymptotes. The
23 % rotation and reflection described above will then generate a hyperbolic
24 % toroid that resides within the Busemann toroid.
25 %
26 % The purpose of this function, then, is to generate the surface of this
27 % hyperbolic toroid.
28 %
29 % Input terms:
30 %
31 % r_inlet = ; r_throat = ; l_Busemann_toroid = ;
32 % num_x_points = ; phi_num_hyperbolic_toroid = ;
33 % emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid,...
34 % plot_hyperbolic_toroid = ; plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure = ;
35 %
36 % where
37 %
38 % r_inlet = the radius of the inlet of the Busemann toroid that
39 % hyperbolic toroid will reside within ;
40 %
41 %
42 % r_throat = the radius of the throat of the Busemann toroid that
43 % the hyperbolic toroid will reside within ;
44 %
45 % l_Busemann_toroid
46 % = the overall length of the Busemann toroid that the
47 % hyperbolic toroid will reside within ;
                                       634
48 %
49 % num_x_points
50 % = the number of x-axis points that will be used in
51 % the initial creation of the two branches of the 2D
52 % hyperbola, that will be rotated/reflected to
53 % generate the 3D hyperbolic toroid ;
54 %
55 % phi_num_hyperbolic_toroid
56 % = the number of azimuthal angles, with respect to the
57 % z-axis, the 2D hyperbola will be rotated through to
58 % create the 3D hyperbolic toroid ;
59 %
60 % emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid
61 % = the scaling factor that represents the extent to
62 % which the hyperbolic toroid resembles a true
63 % blackbody (in the range from 0 to 1) ;
64 %
65 % plot_hyperbolic_toroid
66 % = the truth value of whether or not the hyperbolic
67 % toroid should be plotted (1 = yes, 0 = no) ;
68 %
69 % and
70 %
71 % plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure
72 % = the truth value of whether or not the hyperbolic
73 % toroid should be plotted as a new figure (1 = yes,
74 % 0 = no) ;
75 %
76 %
77 % Usage:
78 %
79 %
[emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid,x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,
z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,...
80 % vol_of_hyperbolic_toroid,...
81 % inner_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid,outer_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid,...
82 % max_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid,min_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid,...
83 % max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid,...
84 %
max_square_area,inner_radial_extent_of_max_square,outer_radial_extent_of_max_squar
e,...
85 %
max_quadrilateral_area,h_for_max_area_outer_vertex,r_for_max_area_outer_vertex,...
86 % max_circle_area,r_of_circle_center,max_circle_radius] = ...
87 % ...
88 % hyperbolic_toroid_for_Busemann_11(r_inlet,r_throat,l_Busemann_toroid,...
89 % num_x_points,phi_num_hyperbolic_toroid,...
90 % emissivity_hyperbolic_toroid,...
91 % plot_hyperbolic_toroid,plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure) ;
92
93 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
94 %
95 % 1) The emissivity of the hyperbolic toroid's surface
96 % has been explicitly added as input.
97 % The emissivity is directly returned with the meshgrids for the
98 % corresponding surface. This is being done to facilitate integration
99 % of the routine's data with the Daun algorithm code.
100 %
                                       635
101 % 2) Additionally, the fliplr commands required for proper function of
102 % the largest-circle and largest-quadrilateral subroutines are
103 % reversed after their execution, for the sake of ensuring the
104 % subsequently generated hyperbolic toroid will plot correctly.
105 %
106 % 3) The number_of_dividing_line_points needs to be manually set
107 % at line 457.
108 %
109 % 4) This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
110 %
111 % hyperbola_in_right_triangle_4
112 % largest_quadrilateral_in_hyperbolic_toroid
113 % largest_circle_in_hyperbolic_toroid
114
115 % BBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBB
116 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
117 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
118 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
119 %
120 % Busemann Toroid's Right Triangle
121 %
122 % BBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBB
123 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
124 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
125 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
126
127 % Generate the right triangle that defines each "quarter" of the Busemann
128 % toroid, as seen in its longitudinal cross section.
129
130 l_major = l_Busemann_toroid / 2 ;
131
132 l_minor = r_inlet - r_throat ;
133
134 plot_results = 0 ;
135
136 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
137 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
138 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
139 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
140 %
141 % Make and Translate Hyperbola
142 %
143 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
144 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
145 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
146 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
147
148 % Generate a hyperbola that has the major leg and hypotenuse of that
149 % right triangle as asymptotes, whose origin-most point is located by two
150 % complementary (i.e. equally fractionally displaced) points on the right
151 % triangle.
152
153 [x_filtered_vec,y_filtered_vec] =
hyperbola_in_right_triangle_4(l_major,l_minor, ...
154 num_x_points, ...
155 plot_results) ;
156
157 % Split this hyperbola up into two branches, an "upper" branch and a
                                       636
158 % "lower" branch. This is being done so that the function can always be
159 % evaluated in a one-to-one manner.
160
161 % Find the point on the hyperbola with the smallest value of x.
162
163 [~,min_x_ind] = min(x_filtered_vec) ;
164
165 y_at_min_x = y_filtered_vec(1,min_x_ind) ;
166
167 % The hyperbola can then be separated into:
168 % 1) a branch with y-values less than or equal to that of the "smallest
169 % x" point; and
170 % 2) a branch with y-values greater than that of the "smallest x" point.
171 %
172 % These two branches of the hyperbola will be henceforth referred to as the
173 % "lower branch" and "upper branch," respectively.
174
175 y_lower_ind_vec = find( y_filtered_vec <= y_at_min_x ) ;
176
177 x_lower_vec = x_filtered_vec(y_lower_ind_vec) ;
178
179 y_lower_vec = y_filtered_vec(y_lower_ind_vec) ;
180
181 y_upper_ind_vec = find( y_filtered_vec > y_at_min_x ) ;
182
183 x_upper_vec = x_filtered_vec(y_upper_ind_vec) ;
184
185 y_upper_vec = y_filtered_vec(y_upper_ind_vec) ;
186
187 % Shift the hyperbola so that its largest x-values (i.e. the ones
188 % coinciding with the minor leg of the Busemann toroid's right triangle)
189 % lie on the y-axis.
190
191 x_lower_vec = x_lower_vec - l_major ;
192
193 x_upper_vec = x_upper_vec - l_major ;
194
195 % Shift the hyperbola so that its y-axis location corresponds to where it
196 % would be in a Busemann toroid centered on the x axis. This toroid is
197 % defined by the right triangle discussed earlier.
198
199 y_lower_vec = y_lower_vec - r_inlet ;
200
201 y_upper_vec = y_upper_vec - r_inlet ;
202
203 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
204 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
205 %
206 % Augment Hyperbola
207 %
208 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
209 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
210
211 % The initial translation of these points of the hyperbola will leave a gap
212 % in between their points that are closest to the y-axis, and the y-axis
213 % itself. To fill these gaps, a call to pchip must be made; the
214 % corresponding vectors will then be augmented with these new values.
215
                                       637
216 x_lower_vec_max_x = max(x_lower_vec) ;
217
218 x_upper_vec_max_x = max(x_upper_vec) ;
219
220 aug_num = 10 ;
221
222 % Piecewise spline in a patch for the gap in the lower branch of the
223 % hyperbola.
224
225 x_lower_vec_aug_step = abs( x_lower_vec_max_x - 0 ) / (aug_num-1) ;
226
227 x_lower_vec_aug_vec = x_lower_vec_max_x : x_lower_vec_aug_step : 0 ;
228
229 x_lower_vec_aug_vec = x_lower_vec_aug_vec(1,2:max(size(x_lower_vec_aug_vec)))
;
230
231 %disp(' ')
232 %disp('Before I chop out duplicated values....')
233
234 %disp(' ')
235 %disp('I chop out duplicated values....')
236
237 [x_lower_vec,ia,~] = unique(x_lower_vec) ;
238
239 y_lower_vec = y_lower_vec(1,ia) ;
240
241 [y_lower_vec_aug_vec] = pchip(x_lower_vec,y_lower_vec,x_lower_vec_aug_vec) ;
242
243 x_lower_vec = horzcat(x_lower_vec,x_lower_vec_aug_vec) ;
244
245 y_lower_vec = horzcat(y_lower_vec,y_lower_vec_aug_vec) ;
246
247 % Piecewise spline in a patch for the gap in the upper branch of the
248 % hyperbola.
249
250 x_upper_vec_aug_step = abs( x_upper_vec_max_x - 0 ) / (aug_num-1) ;
251
252 x_upper_vec_aug_vec = x_upper_vec_max_x:x_upper_vec_aug_step:0 ;
253
254 x_upper_vec_aug_vec = x_upper_vec_aug_vec(1,2:max(size(x_upper_vec_aug_vec)))
;
255
256 %disp(' ')
257 %disp('I chop out duplicated values....')
258
259 [x_upper_vec,ia,~] = unique(x_upper_vec) ;
260
261 y_upper_vec = y_upper_vec(1,ia) ;
262
263 [y_upper_vec_aug_vec] = pchip(x_upper_vec,y_upper_vec,x_upper_vec_aug_vec) ;
264
265 x_upper_vec = horzcat(x_upper_vec,x_upper_vec_aug_vec) ;
266
267 y_upper_vec = horzcat(y_upper_vec,y_upper_vec_aug_vec) ;
268
269 % The y-axis locations of each point within this cross-section are
270 % equivalent to the radial displacements of the hyperbolic toroid's points
271 % within a cylindrical coordinate system, once it is rotated 90 degrees to
                                       638
272 % have its central axis coincide with the z-axis. Similarly, the x-axis
273 % locations of these points correspond to the vertical displacements of the
274 % toroid's points within that same coordinate system.
275 %
276 % To put these transformations in other terms, the
277 % "upper" branch of the hyperbola becomes the radially "inner" surface of
278 % the resulting hyperbolic toroid.
279 %
280 % By the same token, the "lower" branch of the hyperbola becomes the
281 % radially "outer" surface of the resulting hyperbolic toroid.
282
283 r_outer_vec = abs(y_lower_vec) ;
284
285 r_inner_vec = abs(y_upper_vec) ;
286
287 h_outer_vec = x_lower_vec ;
288
289 h_inner_vec = x_upper_vec ;
290
291 phi_vec = 0: (2*pi) / (phi_num_hyperbolic_toroid-1) : 2*pi ;
292
293 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
294 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
295 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
296 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
297 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
298 %
299 % Calculate Volume of Hyperbolic Toroid
300 %
301 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
302 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
303 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
304 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
305 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
306
307 % Augment the outer and inner vectors, so that the two branches of the
308 % hyperbola will always have height values in common.
309
310 h_outer_not_in_inner_vec = setdiff(h_outer_vec,h_inner_vec) ;
311
312 r_aug_inner_vec = pchip(h_inner_vec,r_inner_vec,h_outer_not_in_inner_vec) ;
313
314 h_inner_vec = horzcat(h_inner_vec,h_outer_not_in_inner_vec) ;
315
316 r_inner_vec = horzcat(r_inner_vec,r_aug_inner_vec) ;
317
318 [h_inner_vec,sorted_h_inner_vec_ind] = sort(h_inner_vec, 'ascend') ;
319
320 r_inner_vec = r_inner_vec(1,sorted_h_inner_vec_ind) ;
321
322 h_inner_not_in_outer_vec = setdiff(h_inner_vec,h_outer_vec) ;
323
324 r_aug_outer_vec = pchip(h_outer_vec,r_outer_vec,h_inner_not_in_outer_vec) ;
325
326 h_outer_vec = horzcat(h_outer_vec,h_inner_not_in_outer_vec) ;
327
328 r_outer_vec = horzcat(r_outer_vec,r_aug_outer_vec) ;
329
                                       639
330 [h_outer_vec,sorted_h_outer_vec_ind] = sort(h_outer_vec, 'ascend') ;
331
332 r_outer_vec = r_outer_vec(1,sorted_h_outer_vec_ind) ;
333
334 % Set up the variables and vectors that will be used to compile data within
335 % the loop.
336
337 volume_of_half_hyperbolic_toroid = 0 ;
338
339 radial_difference_vec = zeros(1,max(size(h_inner_vec))) ;
340
341 abs_h_displacement_x2_vec = zeros(1,max(size(h_inner_vec))) ;
342
343 for h_val_ind = 1:1:max(size(h_inner_vec)) - 1
344
345 % Compile the radial differences, and the 2 * z-axis-displacement
346 % values, for later use.
347
348 radial_difference_vec(1,h_val_ind) = r_outer_vec(1,h_val_ind) -
r_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)
;
349
350 abs_h_displacement_x2_vec(1,h_val_ind) = 2 * abs(h_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)) ;
351
352 if h_val_ind == max(size(h_inner_vec)) - 1
353
354 radial_difference_vec(1,max(size(h_inner_vec))) = r_outer_vec(1,max(size
(h_inner_vec))) - r_inner_vec(1,max(size(h_inner_vec))) ;
355
356 abs_h_displacement_x2_vec(1,max(size(h_inner_vec))) = 2 *
h_inner_vec(1,max(size
(h_inner_vec))) ;
357
358 else
359 end
360
361 % Find the "differential" volume element of the hyperbolic toroid, by
362 % finding the difference between the volumes of the outer and inner
363 % frustums bounding it.
364
365 vol_of_outer_frustum = (pi/3) ...
366 * ( (r_outer_vec(1,h_val_ind)^2) + (r_outer_vec(1,h_val_ind)*r_outer_vec(1,
h_val_ind+1)) + (r_outer_vec(1,h_val_ind+1)^2) ) ...
367 * abs(h_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)-h_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind+1)) ;
368
369 vol_of_inner_frustum = (pi/3) ...
370 * ( (r_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)^2) + (r_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)*r_inner_vec(1,
h_val_ind+1)) + (r_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind+1)^2) ) ...
371 * abs(h_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind)-h_inner_vec(1,h_val_ind+1)) ;
372
373 vol_of_annulus = vol_of_outer_frustum - vol_of_inner_frustum ;
374
375 volume_of_half_hyperbolic_toroid = volume_of_half_hyperbolic_toroid +
vol_of_annulus ;
376
377 end
378
379 vol_of_hyperbolic_toroid = 2 * volume_of_half_hyperbolic_toroid ;
                                       640
380
381 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
382 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
383 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
384 %
385 % Largest Square Calculations
386 %
387 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
388 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
389 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
390
391 % Use pchip interpolation to estimate the point where the difference
392 % between the radial extent of a box, and its height (z-axis) extent, is
393 % zero. This will represent the length of the largest z-axis aligned square
394 % that can fit in the hyperbolic toroid.
395
396 diff_between_radial_extent_and_2x_h_displacement_vec =
abs_h_displacement_x2_vec -
radial_difference_vec ;
397
398 max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid = pchip
(diff_between_radial_extent_and_2x_h_displacement_vec,abs_h_displacement_x2_vec,0)
;
399
400 % Using the size of the square, determine the inner radial extent of the
401 % square using pchip. This is done by expressing the inner radii as a
402 % function of the radial differences, then using pchip to interpolate the
403 % radial value.
404
405 inner_radial_extent_of_max_square = pchip(radial_difference_vec,r_inner_vec,
max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid) ;
406
407 % Using the size of the square, determine the outer radial extent of the
408 % square using pchip. This is done by expressing the inner radii as a
409 % function of the radial differences, then using pchip to interpolate the
410 % radial value.
411
412 outer_radial_extent_of_max_square = pchip(radial_difference_vec,r_outer_vec,
max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid) ;
413
414 max_square_area =
max_length_of_z_axis_aligned_square_inside_hyperbolic_toroid^2 ;
415
416 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
417 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
418 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
419 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
420 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
421 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
422 %
423 % Find Largest Quadrilateral And Largest Circle
424 %
425 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
426 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
427 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
428 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
429 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
430 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
                                       641
431
432 % Condition the radial and height vectors for the hyperbola, so that they
433 % will work properly within the "largest quadrilateral" and "largest
434 % circle" routines.
435 %
436 % As a reminder, the cylindrical coordinates of the toroid relate to the
437 % Cartesian coordinates of the hyperbola in the following manner....
438 %
439 % r = y
440 % h = x
441 % inner = upper
442 % outer = lower
443
444 r_inner_vec = -fliplr(r_inner_vec) ;
445
446 h_inner_vec = fliplr(h_inner_vec) ;
447
448 r_total_hyperbola_vec = horzcat(r_inner_vec,-r_outer_vec) ;
449
450 h_total_hyperbola_vec = horzcat(h_inner_vec,h_outer_vec) ;
451
452
[max_quadrilateral_area,h_for_max_area_outer_vertex,r_for_max_area_outer_vertex] =
...
453
largest_quadrilateral_in_hyperbolic_toroid(h_total_hyperbola_vec,r_total_hyperbola
_vec) ;
454
455 r_for_max_area_outer_vertex = abs(r_for_max_area_outer_vertex) ;
456
457 number_of_dividing_line_points = 100 ;
458
459 [max_circle_area,r_of_circle_center,max_circle_radius] = ...
460
largest_circle_in_hyperbolic_toroid(h_total_hyperbola_vec,r_total_hyperbola_vec,
number_of_dividing_line_points) ;
461
462 r_of_circle_center = abs(r_of_circle_center) ;
463
464 % Reverse the previous fliplr commands, so that the hyperbolic toroid
465 % surface generated in the following step will render properly in surf.
466
467 r_inner_vec = -fliplr(r_inner_vec) ;
468
469 h_inner_vec = fliplr(h_inner_vec) ;
470
471 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
472 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
473 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
474 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
475 %
476 % Generate Hyperbolic Torus Surface
477 %
478 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
479 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
480 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
481 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
482
                                       642
483 % Generate a meshgrid to yield the resulting segments of the hyperbolic
484 % torus.
485
486 % lhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlh
487 %
488 % --lower half--
489 %
490 % lhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlhlh
491
492 % Generate the outer segment of the lower half.
493
494 [phi_mat,r_outer_mat] = meshgrid(phi_vec,r_outer_vec) ;
495
496 h_outer_vec = h_outer_vec .* (r_outer_vec./r_outer_vec) ;
497
498 h_outer_mat = h_outer_vec' .* ones(max(size(r_outer_vec)),max(size(phi_vec)))
;
499
500 [x_lh_outer_mat,y_lh_outer_mat,z_lh_outer_mat] =
pol2cart(phi_mat,r_outer_mat,h_outer_mat) ;
501
502 % Generate the inner segment of the lower half.
503
504 [phi_mat,r_inner_mat] = meshgrid(phi_vec,r_inner_vec) ;
505
506 h_inner_vec = h_inner_vec .* (r_inner_vec./r_inner_vec) ;
507
508 h_inner_mat = h_inner_vec' .* ones(max(size(r_inner_vec)),max(size(phi_vec)))
;
509
510 [x_lh_inner_mat,y_lh_inner_mat,z_lh_inner_mat] =
pol2cart(phi_mat,r_inner_mat,h_inner_mat) ;
511
512 % Merge the meshgrids corresponding to the "inner" and "outer" surfaces of
513 % the toroid's lower half.
514
515 x_lh_inner_2_mat = flipud(x_lh_inner_mat);
516 y_lh_inner_2_mat = flipud(y_lh_inner_mat);
517 z_lh_inner_2_mat = flipud(z_lh_inner_mat);
518
519 x_lh_inner_outer_mat = vertcat(x_lh_inner_2_mat,x_lh_outer_mat);
520 y_lh_inner_outer_mat = vertcat(y_lh_inner_2_mat,y_lh_outer_mat);
521 z_lh_inner_outer_mat = vertcat(z_lh_inner_2_mat,z_lh_outer_mat);
522
523 % uhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuh
524 %
525 % --upper half--
526 %
527 % uhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuhuh
528
529 % Generate the upper half of the toroid by reflection.
530
531 x_uh_inner_outer_mat = x_lh_inner_outer_mat ;
532
533 y_uh_inner_outer_mat = y_lh_inner_outer_mat ;
534
535 z_uh_inner_outer_mat = -z_lh_inner_outer_mat ;
536
                                       643
537 % mthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmth
538 %
539 % --merge two halves--
540 %
541 % mthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmthmth
542
543 % Excise the first row of each "upper half" meshgrid, since this is a set
544 % of redundant points, along the innermost radius of the toroid, that is
545 % shared in common with the lower half of the toroid.
546
547 [row_num,~] = size(x_uh_inner_outer_mat);
548
549 x_uh_inner_outer_mat = x_uh_inner_outer_mat(2:1:row_num,:) ;
550
551 y_uh_inner_outer_mat = y_uh_inner_outer_mat(2:1:row_num,:) ;
552
553 z_uh_inner_outer_mat = z_uh_inner_outer_mat(2:1:row_num,:) ;
554
555 % Reverse the order of the meshgrids for the upper half of the hyperbolic
556 % toroid. This ensures that, when the two sets of meshgrids are merged, the
557 % running order of the points will proceed with a counterclockwise
558 % rotation (i.e. outer-upper-inner-lower-outer), when viewed from the +x
559 % section of the longitudinally intersecting xz-plane.
560 %
561 % NOTE: The radially outermost ring of points on the hyperbolic toroid is
562 % also duplicated between the upper and lower half meshgrids of the torus.
563 % However, the corresponding duplicate rows cannot be deleted without
564 % splitting open the surface of the toroid.
565
566 x_uh_inner_outer_mat = flipud(x_uh_inner_outer_mat) ;
567
568 y_uh_inner_outer_mat = flipud(y_uh_inner_outer_mat) ;
569
570 z_uh_inner_outer_mat = flipud(z_uh_inner_outer_mat) ;
571
572 x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat = vertcat(x_uh_inner_outer_mat,x_lh_inner_outer_mat);
573
574 y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat = vertcat(y_uh_inner_outer_mat,y_lh_inner_outer_mat);
575
576 z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat = vertcat(z_uh_inner_outer_mat,z_lh_inner_outer_mat);
577
578 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
579 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
580 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
581 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
582 %
583 % Return Other Geometric Parameters
584 %
585 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
586 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
587 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
588 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
589
590 % Return the outer radius of the hyperbolic toroid.
591
592 outer_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid = max(max(x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat)) ;
593
594 % Return the inner radius of the hyperbolic toroid.
                                       644
595
596 radii_squared_mat = (x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat.^2) +
(y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat.^2) ;
597
598 radii_mat = radii_squared_mat.^0.5 ;
599
600 inner_radius_of_hyperbolic_toroid = min(min(radii_mat)) ;
601
602 % Return the highest z extent of the hyperbolic toroid.
603
604 max_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid = max(max(z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat)) ;
605
606 % Return the lowest z extent of the hyperbolic toroid.
607
608 min_z_value_of_hyperbolic_toroid = min(min(z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat)) ;
609
610 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
611 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
612 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
613 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
614 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
615 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
616 %
617 % Plot Hyperbolic Toroid Surfaces If Asked
618 %
619 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
620 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
621 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
622 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
623 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
624 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
625
626 if plot_hyperbolic_toroid == 1
627
628 if plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure == 1
629
630 figure
631
632 surf(x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,
z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat, 'EdgeColor' ,'none')
633
634 hold on
635 axis equal
636
637 xlabel( 'X axis (m)' )
638 ylabel( 'Y axis (m)' )
639 zlabel( 'Z axis (m)' )
640
641 else
642
643 hold on
644 axis equal
645
646 surf(x_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,y_hyperbolic_toroid_mat,
z_hyperbolic_toroid_mat, 'EdgeColor' ,'k')
647
648 end
649
                                       645
650 if plot_hyperbolic_toroid_as_new_figure == 1
651
652 cva = camva ;
653
654 camva(0.8*cva);
655
656 camva( 'manual')
657
658 else
659 end
660
661 else
662 end

664 end
665

Use Right Triangle to Construct Hyperbola
Filename: hyperbola_in_right_triangle_4.m
1 function [x_filtered_vec,y_filtered_vec] =
hyperbola_in_right_triangle_4(l_major,l_minor, ...
2 num_x_points, ...
3 plot_results)
4 %
5 % Consider a right triangle, with its major leg coincident with the x
6 % axis, its minor leg displaced in the +x direction, and its most-acute
7 % angle at the origin. Within this right triangle, a hyperbola is
8 % incribed. This hyperbola's axis of symmetry lies along the line
9 % bisecting the most acute angle of the right triangle. Additionally, the
10 % asymptotes of this hyperbola coincide with the x axis and the
11 % hypotenuse. Finally, the "origin-most" point on the hyperbola is
12 % positioned so that, when its tangent line is drawn, that line
13 % intersects the major leg and hypotenuse at places that are both equally
14 % displaced from the origin.
15 %
16 % Usage:
17 % [x_filtered_vec,y_filtered_vec] = ...
18 % hyperbola_in_right_triangle_4(l_major,l_minor,...
19 % num_x_points,...
20 % plot_results) ;
21
22 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
23 %
24 % 1) The number of x points to be assessed on each branch of
25 % the hyperbola is set by the user as an
26 % input, and not by the program itself.
27 %
28 % 2) This routine calls the following non-MATLAB subroutine:
29 %
30 % A_and_C_equidistant_from_O
31 % hyperbola
32
33 l_hypotenuse = sqrt((l_minor^2)+(l_major^2)) ;
34
35 % Find the most-acute angle of the right triangle.
36
37 theta = atan( l_minor / l_major ) ;
38
                                       646
39 % Determine the points on the right triangle that need to be intersected by
40 % the innermost tangent line of the hyperbola.
41
42 [f_eq] = A_and_C_equidistant_from_O(l_minor,l_major) ;
43
44 l_rh = f_eq * l_hypotenuse ;
45
46 % Determine the parameters for the "un-rotated" version of the hyperbola.
47
48 a = l_rh * cos(theta/2) ;
49
50 b = a * tan(theta/2) ;
51
52 % Generate the two branches of the un-rotated hyperbola.
53
54 % Two x vectors need to be generated to accomplish this. The lower branch
55 % will need to have a smaller x range, to prevent it from jutting
56 % excessively past the minor leg of the right triangle when it is rotated
57 % into position.
58 % Similarly, the upper branch of the hyperbola will need to have a larger x
59 % range, to prevent it from falling short of the minor leg of the right
60 % triangle when it is rotated into position.
61 % In both cases,the routine will err on the side of having values of the
62 % hyperbola's branches that stick out past l_major on the x axis.
63
64 length_of_bisecting_line_seg = l_major / cos(theta/2) ;
65
66 %delta_x = length_of_bisecting_line_seg - l_major ;
67
68 %max_x_for_neg_branch = cos(theta/2) * l_major ;
69
70 max_x_for_neg_branch = length_of_bisecting_line_seg ;
71
72 max_x_for_pos_branch = cos(theta/2) * l_hypotenuse ;
73
74 x_neg_vec = a:(max_x_for_neg_branch-a)/(num_x_points-1):max_x_for_neg_branch ;
75
76 [y_neg_vec,~] = hyperbola(a,b,x_neg_vec) ;
77
78 x_pos_vec = a:(max_x_for_pos_branch-a)/(num_x_points-1):max_x_for_pos_branch ;
79
80 [~,y_pos_vec] = hyperbola(a,b,x_pos_vec) ;
81
82 % Rotate the hyperbola to its correct orientation.
83
84 R = [ cos(theta/2) -sin(theta/2); sin(theta/2) cos(theta/2)] ;
85
86 old_xy_pos_mat = vertcat(x_pos_vec,y_pos_vec);
87
88 new_xy_pos_mat = R * old_xy_pos_mat ;
89
90 old_xy_neg_mat = vertcat(x_neg_vec,y_neg_vec);
91
92 new_xy_neg_mat = R * old_xy_neg_mat ;
93
94 new_xy_mat = horzcat(new_xy_neg_mat,new_xy_pos_mat) ;
95
96 [x_sorted_vec,x_sorted_ind_vec] = sort(new_xy_mat(1,:)) ;
                                       647
97
98 y_sorted_vec = new_xy_mat(2,x_sorted_ind_vec) ;
99
100 x_filtered_ind_vec = find(x_sorted_vec<=l_major) ;
101
102 x_filtered_vec = x_sorted_vec(x_filtered_ind_vec) ;
103
104 y_filtered_vec = y_sorted_vec(x_filtered_ind_vec) ;
105
106 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
107 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
108 %
109 % Plot Results
110 %
111 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
112 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
113
114 % Plot the results, if requested.
115
116 if plot_results == 1
117
118 figure
119
120 % Plot the hyperbola.
121
122 plot(x_filtered_vec,y_filtered_vec, 'g*','MarkerSize' ,12);
123
124 % Adjust the settings for the plot.
125
126 hold on;
127 axis equal;
128 grid
129
130 v = axis;
131 v(1) = -0.1 * l_major ;
132 v(2) = 1.1 * l_major ;
133 v(3) = -0.1 * l_minor ;
134 v(4) = 1.1 * l_minor ;
135 axis(v);
136 axis manual
137
138 % Plot the right triangle.
139
140 plot([0,l_major],[0,0], 'b-','LineWidth' ,2.5)
141 plot([0,l_major],[0,l_minor], 'b-','LineWidth' ,2.5)
142 plot([l_major,l_major],[0,l_minor], 'b-','LineWidth' ,2.5)
143
144 % Plot the bisecting line segment.
145
146 y_bisect = l_major * tan(theta/2) ;
147
148 plot([0,l_major],[0,y_bisect], 'c-','LineWidth' ,2.5)
149
150 else
151 end
152
153 end
154
                                       648
CA6.f Complementary Points Equidistant From Origin

Filename: A_and_C_equidistant_from_O.m


1 function [f_eq] = A_and_C_equidistant_from_O(l_minor,l_major)
2 %
3 % Consider a right triangle, with its major leg coincident with the x
4 % axis, its minor leg displaced in the +x direction, and its most-acute
5 % angle at the origin.
6 %
7 % Next, suppose that there are two "complementary" points A and C on
8 % this right triangle. Point A is constrained to lie on the major leg,
9 % and point C is constrained to lie on the hypotenuse. Both of these
10 % points, furthermore, are displaced by some common factor along the
11 % major leg and hypotenuse, albeit in opposite directions.
12 %
13 % Example:
14 % If point A is 10% of the way from the origin to the major leg's
15 % "x-most" vertex,
16 % it follows that
17 % point C is 10% of the way from the hypotenuse's "x-most" vertex to the
18 % origin.
19 %
20 % Now, consider a factor that places both point A and C at identical
21 % distances from the origin. What is this factor?
22 % This routine is meant to answer this question.
23 %
24 % Usage:
25 % [f_eq] = A_and_C_equidistant_from_O(l_minor,l_major)
26
27 l_hypotenuse = sqrt((l_minor^2)+(l_major^2)) ;
28
29 major_hyp_ratio = l_major / l_hypotenuse ;
30
31 f_eq = 1 / ( major_hyp_ratio + 1 ) ;
32
33 end
34




CA6.g Hyperbola Generator

Filename: hyperbola.m


1 function [y_neg_vec,y_pos_vec] = hyperbola(a,b,x_vec)
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to plot the positive half of a
4 % hyperbola that is centered on the origin, whose functional form is
5 % given by the formula
6 % x^2/a^2 - y^2/b^2 = 1.
7 %
8 % Usage:
9 % [y_neg_vec,y_pos_vec] = hyperbola(a,b,x_vec)
                                       649
10
11 % Generate the +y branch of the hyperbola.
12
13 y_pos_vec = sqrt( (b^2) .* ( ((x_vec.^2)/(a^2)) - 1 ) ) ;
14
15 % Generate the -y branch of the hyperbola.
16
17 y_neg_vec = -y_pos_vec ;
18
19 end
20




CA6.h Find Largest Quadrilateral in Hyperbolic Toroid

Filename: largest_quadrilateral_in_hyperbolic_toroid.m


1 function
[max_quadrilateral_area,x_for_max_area_outer_vertex,y_for_max_area_outer_vertex] =
...
2 largest_quadrilateral_in_hyperbolic_toroid(x_hyperbola_vec,y_hyperbola_vec)
3 %
4 % Consider the case of a hyperbolic toroid. This toroid is generated by
5 % revolution and reflection of a rotated and translated hyperbola in
6 % cylindrical coordinates. More specifically, the hyperbola that
7 % generates this toroid will start out with its uppermost and lowermost
8 % points on the y-axis, and all of its other points will be at negative
9 % values of both the x and y coordinates.
10 %
11 % The question then becomes, "What is the largest-area quadrilateral that
12 % can fit within a radial cross-section of this toroid?" Since this
13 % quadrilateral must consist of two reflected copies of the largest
14 % triangle that can fit within the original hyperboloid, our problem
15 % simplifies to one of finding the largest-area triangle that can be
16 % inscribed within the hyperbola.
17 %
18 % NOTE:
19 %
20 % For this routine to function correctly, the uppermost point must be at
21 % the beginning of each Cartesian vector: the lowermost point must be at
22 % teh end of each Cartesian vector.
23 %
24 % Usage:
25 %
26 %
[max_quadrilateral_area,x_for_max_area_outer_vertex,y_for_max_area_outer_vertex] =
...
27 % largest_quadrilateral_in_hyperbolic_toroid(x_hyperbola_vec,y_hyperbola_vec) ;
28
29 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
30 %
31 % Validation
32 %
33 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
34
                                       650
35 if max(size(x_hyperbola_vec)) ~= max(size(y_hyperbola_vec))
36 error( 'The x and y vectors for the hyperbola must be the same size.' )
37 else
38 end
39
40 % first_x_hyperbola_vec = x_hyperbola_vec(1,1)
41
42 % last_x_hyperbola_vec = x_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(y_hyperbola_vec)))
43
44 % first_y_hyperbola_vec = y_hyperbola_vec(1,1)
45
46 % last_y_hyperbola_vec = y_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(y_hyperbola_vec)))
47
48 if y_hyperbola_vec(1,1) <= y_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(y_hyperbola_vec)))
49 error( 'The first point on the hyperbola must be above the last point on the
hyperbola.' )
50 else
51 end
52
53 % For each and every point on the hyperbola...
54
55 uppermost_point_vec = [x_hyperbola_vec(1,1),y_hyperbola_vec(1,1)] ;
56
57 lowermost_point_vec =
[x_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(x_hyperbola_vec))),y_hyperbola_vec(1,max
(size(x_hyperbola_vec)))] ;
58
59 hyperbola_mat = horzcat(x_hyperbola_vec',y_hyperbola_vec') ;
60
61 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
62 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
63 %
64 % Make Triangles
65 %
66 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
67 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
68
69 % Let side a be the leg running from the uppermost point of the hyperbola
70 % to a selected point on the hyperbola.
71
72 uppermost_point_mat = uppermost_point_vec .* ones(max(size(x_hyperbola_vec)),2)
;
73
74 % size_hyperbola_mat = size(hyperbola_mat)
75
76 % size_uppermost_point_mat = size(uppermost_point_mat)
77
78 upper_adj_hyperbola_mat = hyperbola_mat-uppermost_point_mat ;
79
80 side_a_vec = magnitude( upper_adj_hyperbola_mat ) ;
81
82 % Let side b be the leg running from a selected point on the hyperbola to
83 % the lowermost point on the hyperbola.
84
85 %side_b_vec = magnitude( hyperbola_mat(:,:) - lowermost_point_vec )
86
87 %side_b_vec = magnitude( hyperbola_mat - (lowermost_point_vec.*ones(max(size
(x_hyperbola_vec)),2)) )
                                       651
88
89 lowermost_point_mat = lowermost_point_vec .* ones(max(size(x_hyperbola_vec)),2)
;
90
91 lower_adj_hyperbola_mat = hyperbola_mat-lowermost_point_mat ;
92
93 side_b_vec = magnitude( lower_adj_hyperbola_mat ) ;
94
95 % Let side c be the leg running from the uppermost point on the hyperbola
96 % to the lowermost point on the hyperbola.
97
98 side_c_vec = ( uppermost_point_vec(1,2) - lowermost_point_vec(1,2) ) .*
ones(max(size
(x_hyperbola_vec)),1) ;
99
100 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
101 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
102 %
103 % Find Areas
104 %
105 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
106 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
107
108 % Calculate the semiperimeters.
109
110 semiperimeter_vec = 0.5 * ( side_a_vec + side_b_vec + side_c_vec ) ;
111
112 % Use Heron's formula to calculate the area of the corresponding triangle.
113
114 area_vec = sqrt( semiperimeter_vec .* (semiperimeter_vec-side_a_vec) .*
(semiperimeter_vecside_
b_vec) .* (semiperimeter_vec-side_c_vec) ) ;
115
116 area_vec = 2.*area_vec ;
117
118 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
119 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
120 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
121 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
122 %
123 % Return Maximum Area Quadrilateral
124 %
125 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
126 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
127 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
128 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
129
130 [max_quadrilateral_area,ind_max_area] = max(area_vec) ;
131
132 x_for_max_area_outer_vertex = x_hyperbola_vec(1,ind_max_area) ;
133
134 y_for_max_area_outer_vertex = y_hyperbola_vec(1,ind_max_area) ;
135
136 end

CA6.i Find Largest Circle in Hyperbolic Toroid

Filename: largest_circle_in_hyperbolic_toroid.m


1 function [max_circle_area,y_of_circle_center,max_circle_radius] = ...
2 largest_circle_in_hyperbolic_toroid(x_hyperbola_vec,y_hyperbola_vec,
number_of_dividing_line_points)
3 %
4 % Consider the case of a hyperbolic toroid. This toroid is generated by
5 % revolution and reflection of a rotated and translated hyperbola in
6 % cylindrical coordinates. More specifically, the hyperbola that
7 % generates this toroid will start out with its uppermost and lowermost
8 % points on the y-axis, and all of its other points will be at negative
9 % values of both the x and y coordinates.
10 %
11 % The question then becomes, "What is the largest-area circle that
12 % can fit within a radial cross-section of this toroid?"
13 %
14 % NOTE:
15 %
16 % For this routine to function correctly, the uppermost point of the
17 % hyperbola must be at the beginning of each Cartesian vector: the
18 % lowermost point of the hyperbola must be at the end of each Cartesian
19 % vector.
20 %
21 % Usage:
22 %
23 % [max_circle_area,y_of_circle_center,max_circle_radius] = ...
24 % largest_circle_in_hyperbolic_toroid(x_hyperbola_vec,y_hyperbola_vec,
number_of_dividing_line_points) ;
25 %
26
27 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
28 %
29 % Validation
30 %
31 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
32
33 if max(size(x_hyperbola_vec)) ~= max(size(y_hyperbola_vec))
34 error( 'The x and y vectors for the hyperbola must be the same size.' )
35 else
36 end
37
38 if number_of_dividing_line_points <= 0
39 error( 'The number of dividing line points must be a positive, nonzero number.'
)
40 else
41 if mod(number_of_dividing_line_points,1) > 0
42 error( 'The number of dividing line points must be a positive integer.' )
43 else
44 end
45 end
46
47 if y_hyperbola_vec(1,1) <= y_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(y_hyperbola_vec)))
48 error( 'The first point on the hyperbola must be above the last point on the
hyperbola.' )
                                       653
49 else
50 end
51
52 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
53 %
54 % Setup
55 %
56 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
57
58 % For each and every point on the hyperbola...
59
60 uppermost_point_vec = [x_hyperbola_vec(1,1),y_hyperbola_vec(1,1)] ;
61
62 lowermost_point_vec =
[x_hyperbola_vec(1,max(size(x_hyperbola_vec))),y_hyperbola_vec(1,max
(size(x_hyperbola_vec)))] ;
63
64 hyperbola_mat = horzcat(x_hyperbola_vec',y_hyperbola_vec') ;
65
66 % Create a line running from the uppermost point on the hyperbola to the
67 % lowest point.
68
69 y_dividing_line_vec = uppermost_point_vec(1,2) : (lowermost_point_vec(1,2)-
uppermost_point_vec(1,2))/(number_of_dividing_line_points-1) :
lowermost_point_vec(1,2) ;
70
71 dividing_line_mat =
horzcat(zeros(number_of_dividing_line_points,1),y_dividing_line_vec') ;
72
73 radii_mat = zeros(number_of_dividing_line_points,max(size(x_hyperbola_vec))) ;
74
75 % For each point on the dividing_line...
76
77 for dividing_line_itr = 1:1:number_of_dividing_line_points
78 % Find the distance between the dividing line point and each point on
79 % the hyperbola. These represent the radii of all circles that can be
80 % drawn from the dividing line point, which are also either tangent to,
81 % or intersecting,the hyperbola.
82
83 dividing_line_working_mat = dividing_line_mat(dividing_line_itr,:) .*
ones(max(size
(x_hyperbola_vec)),2) ;
84
85 adj_hyperbola_mat = hyperbola_mat-dividing_line_working_mat ;
86
87 size_adj_hyperbola_mat = size(magnitude_for_matrices(adj_hyperbola_mat))
88
89 radii_mat(dividing_line_itr,:) = ( magnitude_for_matrices(adj_hyperbola_mat) )'
;
90
91 end
92
93 %radii_mat = radii_mat ;
94
95 % Find the minimum radius for each dividing line point. This will represent
96 % the largest circle that can fit within the hyperbola at each dividing
97 % line point.
98
                                       654
99 min_radii_vec = min(radii_mat,[],2) ;
100
101 % For all of these radii, find the largest one. This will represent the
102 % largest circle, centered on the dividing line, that can fit in the
103 % hyperbola.
104
105 [max_circle_radius,ind_of_max_radius] = max(min_radii_vec) ;
106
107 max_circle_area = pi*(max_circle_radius^2) ;
108
109 y_of_circle_center = y_dividing_line_vec(1,ind_of_max_radius) ;
110
111 end




CA6.j Create Ring of Boxes Inside Hyperbolic Toroid

Filename: create_ring_of_boxes_7.m


1 function
[x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat, ...
2 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes,outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes] = ...
3 create_ring_of_boxes_7(size_of_cube,number_of_meshgrid_points,number_of_cubes,
...
4 skip_every_nth_box,cube_orientation, ...
5 plot_ring_of_boxes,plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure)
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to take, as input, the size of a given
8 % cube, and the number of copies of this cube that will be fastened
9 % together, at their "inner" (z-axis-facing) faces, to create a ring.
10 % This function will then return, as output, meshgrids that define each
11 % and every one of the cubes in the ring.
12 %
13 % Input terms:
14 %
15 % size_of_cube = the length of one side of the cube;
16 %
17 % number_of_meshgrid_points = the number of rows and columns that the
18 % initial meshgrids defining each face of
19 % the cube will have;
20 %
21 % number_of_cubes = the number of cubes (ignoring deletions
22 % ...more on this below) that will be
23 % joined together to create the ring of
24 % cubes;
25 %
26 % skip_every_nth_box = if boxes are being omitted, the routine
27 % will skip every nth box, but plot all
28 % others;
29 %
30 % cube_orientation = a number specifying how the cubes will
31 % abut one another, where...
32 %
33 % 1 = cubes joined along lower edges,
34 % with their inner faces joined in a
                                       655
35 % continuous ribbon having as many
36 % squares as there are cubes;
37 %
38 % 2 = cubes joined along side edges,
39 % with their +/- z-axis-oriented
40 % faces joined along face diagonals,
41 % such that their faces form a
42 % necklace of diamonds;
43 %
44 % 3 = cubes joined at vertices along
45 % common side edges, with those side
46 % edges oriented inward toward the z
47 % azis, such that the cubes form a
48 % charm bracelet of diamonds;
49 %
50 % 4 = cubes joined at the vertices lying
51 % on their face diagonals, along
52 % their inward-oriented faces,
53 % such that their faces form a ring
54 % of diamonds; and
55 %
56 % 5 = cubes joined at the vertices lying
57 % on their body diagonals, such that
58 % they form a "necklace" of cubes;
59 %
60 % plot_ring_of_boxes = the truth value of whether or not the
61 % ring of boxes is to be plotted (1 if
62 % yes, 0 if no) ;
63 %
64 % and
65 %
66 % plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure
67 % = the truth value of whether the ring of
68 % boxes is to be plotted as a new figure
69 % (1 if yes, 0 if no).
70 %
71 % Usage:
72 %
73 % [x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat,...
74 % inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes,outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes] = ...
75 %
create_ring_of_boxes_7(size_of_cube,number_of_meshgrid_points,number_of_cubes,...
76 % skip_every_nth_box,cube_orientation,...
77 % plot_ring_of_boxes,plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure)
78
79 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
80 %
81 % Validation
82 %
83 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
84
85 if size_of_cube <= 0
86 error( 'The size of the cube must be a positive, non-zero number.' )
87 else
88 end
89
90 tol = 1e-14 ;
91
                                       656
92 if abs(mod(number_of_meshgrid_points,1)) > tol
93 error( 'The number of meshgrid points must be a whole number.' )
94 else
95 if number_of_meshgrid_points <= 0
96 error( 'The number of meshgrid points must be a positive, nonzero integer.' )

150 end
151
152 plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure = logical(plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure) ;
153
154 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
155 % XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
156 % YYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY
157 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
158 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
159 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
160 %
161 % Generate xy-Aligned Cube Faces
162 %
163 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
164 % XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
165 % YYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY
166 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
167 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
168 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
169
170 % Create a cube with one of its eight vertices at the origin.
171
172 x_vec = 0:1/(number_of_meshgrid_points-1):1 ;
173
174 y_vec = 0:1/(number_of_meshgrid_points-1):1 ;
175
176 z_vec = 0:1/(number_of_meshgrid_points-1):1 ;
177
178 % lower
179
180 [x_cube_lower_xy_face_mat,y_cube_lower_xy_face_mat] = meshgrid(x_vec,y_vec) ;
181
182 z_cube_lower_xy_face_mat = zeros(number_of_meshgrid_points) ;
183
184 % upper
185
186 x_cube_upper_xy_face_mat = x_cube_lower_xy_face_mat ;
187
188 y_cube_upper_xy_face_mat = y_cube_lower_xy_face_mat ;
189
190 z_cube_upper_xy_face_mat = z_cube_lower_xy_face_mat + 1 ;
191
192 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
193 % YYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY
194 % ZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZ
195 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
196 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
197 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
198 %
199 % Generate yz-Aligned Cube Faces
                                       658
200 %
201 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
202 % YYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY
203 % ZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZ
204 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
205 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
206 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
207
208 % left
209
210 [y_cube_left_yz_face_mat,z_cube_left_yz_face_mat] = meshgrid(y_vec,z_vec) ;
211
212 x_cube_left_yz_face_mat = zeros(number_of_meshgrid_points) ;
213
214 % right
215
216 y_cube_right_yz_face_mat = y_cube_left_yz_face_mat ;
217
218 z_cube_right_yz_face_mat = z_cube_left_yz_face_mat ;
219
220 x_cube_right_yz_face_mat = x_cube_left_yz_face_mat + 1 ;
221
222 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
223 % XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
224 % ZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZ
225 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
226 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
227 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
228 %
229 % Generate xz-Aligned Cube Faces
230 %
231 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
232 % XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX
233 % ZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZZ
234 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
235 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
236 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
237
238 % back
239
240 [x_cube_back_xz_face_mat,z_cube_back_xz_face_mat] = meshgrid(x_vec,z_vec) ;
241
242 y_cube_back_xz_face_mat = zeros(number_of_meshgrid_points) ;
243
244 % front
245
246 x_cube_front_xz_face_mat = x_cube_back_xz_face_mat ;
247
248 z_cube_front_xz_face_mat = z_cube_back_xz_face_mat ;
249
250 y_cube_front_xz_face_mat = y_cube_back_xz_face_mat + 1 ;
251
252 x_orig_cube_mat = vertcat( x_cube_lower_xy_face_mat, ...
253 x_cube_back_xz_face_mat, ...
254 x_cube_right_yz_face_mat, ...
255 x_cube_front_xz_face_mat, ...
256 x_cube_left_yz_face_mat, ...
257 x_cube_upper_xy_face_mat ) ;
                                       659
258
259 y_orig_cube_mat = vertcat( y_cube_lower_xy_face_mat, ...
260 y_cube_back_xz_face_mat, ...
261 y_cube_right_yz_face_mat, ...
262 y_cube_front_xz_face_mat, ...
263 y_cube_left_yz_face_mat, ...
264 y_cube_upper_xy_face_mat ) ;
265
266 z_orig_cube_mat = vertcat( z_cube_lower_xy_face_mat, ...
267 z_cube_back_xz_face_mat, ...
268 z_cube_right_yz_face_mat, ...
269 z_cube_front_xz_face_mat, ...
270 z_cube_left_yz_face_mat, ...
271 z_cube_upper_xy_face_mat ) ;
272
273 % Shift this cube so that the center of this cube is at the origin.
274
275 x_orig_cube_mat = x_orig_cube_mat - 0.5 ;
276
277 y_orig_cube_mat = y_orig_cube_mat - 0.5 ;
278
279 z_orig_cube_mat = z_orig_cube_mat - 0.5 ;
280
281 % Change the size of this cube so that it is consistent with the specified
282 % size.
283
284 x_orig_cube_mat = x_orig_cube_mat .* size_of_cube ;
285
286 y_orig_cube_mat = y_orig_cube_mat .* size_of_cube ;
287
288 z_orig_cube_mat = z_orig_cube_mat .* size_of_cube ;
289
290 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
291 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
292 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
293 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
294 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
295 %
296 % Copy, Translate and Rotate Cubes
297 %
298 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
299 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT
300 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
301 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
302 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
303
304 % If the first, "ribbon of squares" arrangement is chosen, no angular
305 % reorientations of the cube will be needed before the loop.
306
307 [row_num,col_num] = size(x_orig_cube_mat) ;
308
309 if cube_orientation == 1
310 else
311
312 % If the second, "ribbon of diamonds, joined along edges" arrangement
313 % is chosen, the cube will need to be rotated by pi/4 around the z-axis
314 % before the loop.
315
                                       660
316 if cube_orientation == 2
317
318 current_cube_angle = pi/4 ;
319
320 z_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle),-sin(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
321 sin(current_cube_angle), cos(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
322 0, 0, 1] ;
323
324 % Convert the meshgrids into a single n x 3 matrix of Cartesian
325 % triples.
326
327 x_orig_cube_vec = reshape(x_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
328
329 y_orig_cube_vec = reshape(y_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
330
331 z_orig_cube_vec = reshape(z_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
332
333 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat =
[x_orig_cube_vec,y_orig_cube_vec,z_orig_cube_vec] ;
334
335 % Rotate the Cartesian points by multiplying them into the rotation
336 % matrix; re-orient the resulting 3 x n matrix when done.
337
338 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = z_rotation_mat *
cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1:3)' ;
339
340 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
341
342 x_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1),row_num,col_num) ;
343
344 y_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,2),row_num,col_num) ;
345
346 z_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,3),row_num,col_num) ;
347
348 else
349 if cube_orientation == 3
350
351 % If the third, "charm bracelet of diamonds" arrangement is
352 % chosen, the cube will need to be rotated by pi/4 around the
353 % y-axis before the loop.
354
355 current_cube_angle = pi/4 ;
356
357 y_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle), 0, sin(current_cube_angle) ; ...
358 0, 1, 0 ; ...
359 -sin(current_cube_angle), 0, cos(current_cube_angle) ] ;
360
361 % Convert the meshgrids into a single n x 3 matrix of Cartesian
362 % triples.
363
364 x_orig_cube_vec = reshape(x_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
365
366 y_orig_cube_vec = reshape(y_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
367
368 z_orig_cube_vec = reshape(z_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
369
370 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat =
[x_orig_cube_vec,y_orig_cube_vec,z_orig_cube_vec] ;
                                       661
371
372 % Rotate the Cartesian points by multiplying them into the rotation
373 % matrix; re-orient the resulting 3 x n matrix when done.
374
375 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = y_rotation_mat *
cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1:
3)' ;
376
377 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
378
379 x_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1),row_num,col_num) ;
380
381 y_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,2),row_num,col_num) ;
382
383 z_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,3),row_num,col_num) ;
384
385
386 else
387 if cube_orientation == 4
388
389 % If the fourth, "ribbon of diamonds, joined at inner face
390 % vertices" arrangement is chosen, the cube will need to be
391 % rotated by pi/4 around the x-axis before the loop.
392
393 current_cube_angle = pi/4 ;
394
395 x_rotation_mat = [ 1, 0, 0; ...
396 0, cos(current_cube_angle), -sin
(current_cube_angle); ...
397 0, sin(current_cube_angle), cos
(current_cube_angle) ] ;
398
399 % Convert the meshgrids into a single n x 3 matrix of Cartesian
400 % triples.
401
402 x_orig_cube_vec = reshape(x_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
403
404 y_orig_cube_vec = reshape(y_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
405
406 z_orig_cube_vec = reshape(z_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
407
408 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = [x_orig_cube_vec,y_orig_cube_vec,
z_orig_cube_vec] ;
409
410 % Rotate the Cartesian points by multiplying them into the rotation
411 % matrix; re-orient the resulting 3 x n matrix when done.
412
413 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = x_rotation_mat * cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,
1:3)' ;
414
415 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
416
417 x_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1),row_num,col_num) ;
418
419 y_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,2),row_num,col_num) ;
420
421 z_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,3),row_num,col_num) ;
422
                                       662
423 else
424 % If the fifth, "necklace of cubes" arrangement is chosen, three separate
425 % angular reorientations of the cube will be required before the loop.
426
427 % 1) The first angular reorientation will be a rotation of the original
428 % cube by pi/4 around the z-axis.
429
430 current_cube_angle = pi/4 ;
431
432 z_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle),-sin(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
433 sin(current_cube_angle), cos(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
434 0, 0, 1] ;
435
436 % Convert the meshgrids into a single n x 3 matrix of Cartesian
437 % triples.
438
439 x_orig_cube_vec = reshape(x_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
440
441 y_orig_cube_vec = reshape(y_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
442
443 z_orig_cube_vec = reshape(z_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
444
445 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = [x_orig_cube_vec,y_orig_cube_vec,
z_orig_cube_vec] ;
446
447
448 % Rotate the Cartesian points by multiplying them into the rotation
449 % matrix; re-orient the resulting 3 x n matrix when done.
450
451 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = z_rotation_mat * cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,
1:3)' ;
452
453 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
454
455 % 2) The second angular reorientation will take the cube produced by
456 % step 1, and rotate it by an angle of atan(1/sqrt(2)) (i.e. the
457 % elevation of the body diagonal from the cube face) around the
458 % y-axis.
459
460 current_cube_angle = atan(1/sqrt(2)) ;
461
462 y_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle), 0, sin(current_cube_angle)
;...
463 0, 1, 0 ; ...
464 -sin(current_cube_angle), 0, cos(current_cube_angle) ] ;
465
466 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = y_rotation_mat * cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,
1:3)' ;
467
468 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
469
470 % 3) The third and final reorientation will take the cube produced by
471 % step 2, and rotate it by an angle of pi/2 around the x-axis. At
472 % this point, the body diagonal of the cube will be coincident with
473 % the xy-plane, and orthogonal to the x axis.
474
475 current_cube_angle = pi/2 ;
476
                                       663
477 z_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle),-sin(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
478 sin(current_cube_angle), cos(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
479 0, 0, 1] ;
480
481 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = z_rotation_mat * cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,
1:3)' ;
482
483 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat' ;
484
485 x_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1),row_num,col_num) ;
486
487 y_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,2),row_num,col_num) ;
488
489 z_orig_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,3),row_num,col_num) ;
490 end
491 end
492
493 end
494
495 end
496
497 % For the specified number of cubes...
498
499 if plot_ring_of_boxes_as_new_figure == 1
500 figure
501 grid
502 hold on
503 axis equal
504 camva manual
505 else
506 end
507
508 %[row_num,col_num] = size(x_orig_cube_mat) ;
509
510 x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat = zeros(row_num,col_num,number_of_cubes) ;
511
512 y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat = zeros(row_num,col_num,number_of_cubes) ;
513
514 z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat = zeros(row_num,col_num,number_of_cubes) ;
515
516 for cube_itr = 1:1:number_of_cubes
517
518 % ...translate and rotate the original cube so that it will correspond to the
current
cube of the ring.
519
520 ring_angle = 2*pi / number_of_cubes ;
521
522 if cube_orientation == 1
523
524 % ...i.e. the "ribbon of squares" case...
525
526 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = (size_of_cube/2) / tan(ring_angle/2) ;
527
528 cube_center_radius = inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes + (size_of_cube/2) ;
529
530 r_inner_vec = [0,inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes] ;
531
                                       664
532 diag_half_cube = size_of_cube * sqrt(5) / 2 ;
533
534 theta_half_cube_2 = atan(2) ;
535
536 diag_half_cube_vec = [diag_half_cube*cos(theta_half_cube_2),diag_half_cube*sin
(theta_half_cube_2)] ;
537
538 r_outer_vec = r_inner_vec + diag_half_cube_vec ;
539
540 outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = magnitude(r_outer_vec) ;
541
542 else
543 if cube_orientation == 2
544
545 % ...i.e. the "ring of diamonds, joined along edges" case...
546
547 cube_center_radius = (sqrt(2)*size_of_cube/2) / tan(ring_angle/2) ;
548
549 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = cube_center_radius - (sqrt(2)*size_of_cube/2)
;
550
551 outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = cube_center_radius + (sqrt(2)*size_of_cube/2)
;
552
553 else
554 if cube_orientation == 3
555
556 % ... i.e. the "charm bracelet of diamonds" case...
557
558 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = (size_of_cube/2) / tan(ring_angle/2) ;
559
560 cube_center_radius = inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes + (sqrt(2)
*size_of_cube/2);
561
562
563 r_inner_vec = [inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes,0] ;
564
565 diag_half_cube = size_of_cube * 3/2 ;
566
567 theta_half_cube_3 = atan(2*sqrt(2)) ;
568
569 diag_half_cube_vec = [diag_half_cube*sin(theta_half_cube_3),
diag_half_cube*cos(theta_half_cube_3)] ;
570
571
572 r_outer_vec = r_inner_vec + diag_half_cube_vec ;
573
574 outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = magnitude(r_outer_vec) ;
575
576
577 else
578 if cube_orientation == 4
579
580 % ...i.e. the "ring of diamonds, joined at vertices"
581 % case...
582
583 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = (sqrt(2)*size_of_cube/2) / tan
(ring_angle/2) ;
                                       665
584
585 cube_center_radius = inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes + (size_of_cube/2) ;
586
587 outer_face_radius = cube_center_radius + (size_of_cube/2) ;
588
589 outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = sqrt((outer_face_radius^2)+((sqrt(2)
*size_of_cube/2)^2)) ;
590
591 else
592
593 % ...i.e. the "necklace of cubes, joined at vertices"
594 % case...
595
596 cube_center_radius = (sqrt(3)*size_of_cube/2) / tan(ring_angle/2) ;
597
598 inner_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = cube_center_radius - (sqrt(2)
*size_of_cube/2) ;
599
600 outer_radius_of_ring_of_boxes = cube_center_radius + (sqrt(2)
*size_of_cube/2) ;
601
602 end
603 end
604 end
605 end
606
607 current_cube_angle = ring_angle * ( cube_itr - 1 ) ;
608
609 %current_cube_angle = pi/6 ;
610
611 z_rotation_mat = [ cos(current_cube_angle),-sin(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
612 sin(current_cube_angle), cos(current_cube_angle), 0; ...
613 0, 0, 1] ;
614
615 % Convert the meshgrids into a single n x 3 matrix of Cartesian
616 % triples.
617
618 x_orig_cube_vec = reshape(x_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
619
620 y_orig_cube_vec = reshape(y_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
621
622 z_orig_cube_vec = reshape(z_orig_cube_mat,[],1) ;
623
624 cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat =
[x_orig_cube_vec,y_orig_cube_vec,z_orig_cube_vec] ;
625
626 % Rotate the Cartesian points by multiplying them into the rotation
627 % matrix; re-orient the resulting 3 x n matrix when done.
628
629 cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat = z_rotation_mat *
cartesian_xyz_orig_cube_mat(:,1:3)' ;
630
631 cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat = cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat' ;
632
633 x_rot_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat(:,1),row_num,col_num) ;
634
635 y_rot_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat(:,2),row_num,col_num) ;
636
                                       666
637 z_rot_cube_mat = reshape(cartesian_xyz_rot_cube_mat(:,3),row_num,col_num) ;
638
639 x_trans_rot_cube_mat = x_rot_cube_mat +
(cube_center_radius*cos(current_cube_angle)) ;
640
641 y_trans_rot_cube_mat = y_rot_cube_mat +
(cube_center_radius*sin(current_cube_angle)) ;
642
643 z_trans_rot_cube_mat = z_rot_cube_mat ;
644
645 if skip_every_nth_box==0
646
647 x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = x_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
648
649 y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = y_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
650
651 z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = z_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
652
653 if plot_ring_of_boxes == 1
654 surf(x_trans_rot_cube_mat,y_trans_rot_cube_mat,z_trans_rot_cube_mat, "
LineStyle" ,'none')
655 %colormap("pink")
656 else
657 end
658
659 else
660
661 if and( skip_every_nth_box~=0, mod(cube_itr,skip_every_nth_box) > tol )
662
663 x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = x_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
664
665 y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = y_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
666
667 z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = z_trans_rot_cube_mat ;
668
669 if plot_ring_of_boxes == 1
670 surf(x_trans_rot_cube_mat,y_trans_rot_cube_mat,z_trans_rot_cube_mat, "
LineStyle" ,'none')
671 else
672 end
673
674 else
675
676 x_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = nan(row_num,col_num) ;
677
678 y_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = nan(row_num,col_num) ;
679
680 z_meshes_for_boxes_3mat(:,:,cube_itr) = nan(row_num,col_num) ;
681
682 end
683
684 end
685
686 end
687
688 if plot_ring_of_boxes == 1
689 rotate3d
690 else
                                       667
691 end
692
693 end




CA6.k Monte Carlo View Factor Analysis Between Two Obstructed Surfaces

Filename: Monte_Carlo_view_factor_obstructed_fix_par_2.m


1 function [F12_view_factor_vec, ...
2 is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat, ...
3 dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat, ...
4 n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat, ...
5 mag_root_12_valid_3mat, ...
6 mag_root_12_bogus_3mat, ...
7 avg_F12,error, ...
8 std_F12,RSD, ...
9 number_of_bogus_runs, ...
10 run_time_in_s, ...
11 total_valid_point_pairs_assessed, ...
12 grand_total_point_pairs_assessed] = ...
13 Monte_Carlo_view_factor_obstructed_fix_par_2(n_simulation_runs,n_point_pairs,
...
14 expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs, ...
15 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
16 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
17 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...
18 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2, ...
19 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat, ...
20 true_val)
21 %
22 % The purpose of this function is to calculate the view function between
23 % two finite surfaces, using the Monte Carlo method. It assumes that
24 % these two surfaces are obstructed by one other surface or object.
25 %
26 % Input terms:
27 %
28 % n_simulation_runs = the number of rounds of Monte Carlo
29 % approximation that are to be done in this run
30 % of the routine;
31 %
32 % n_point_pairs = the number of pairs of points that are to be
33 % chosen on surface 1 and surface 2, within each
34 % Monte Carlo run;
35 %
36 % expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs
37 %
38 % = the ratio of the grand total of point pairs the
39 % routine is anticipated to assess, divided by
40 % the total of geometrically and
41 % thermodynamically valid point pairs the routine
42 % is expected to return via the valid Monte Carlo
43 % runs;
44 %
45 % surf_1_x_mat = ; surf_1_y_mat = ; surf_1_z_mat = ;
                                       668
46 %
47 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 1 in Cartesian
48 % coordinates.
49 %
50 % surf_2_x_mat = ; surf_2_y_mat = ; surf_2_z_mat = ;
51 %
52 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 2 in Cartesian
53 % coordinates;
54 %
55 % surf_obs_x_mat = ; surf_obs_y_mat = ; surf_obs_z_mat = ;
56 %
57 % where these are meshgrids representing the obstructing surface in
58 % Cartesian coordinates;
59 %
60 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1
61 %
62 % = one of three possible values...
63 %
64 % +1 iff rays are emitted out and away from
65 % the center of surface 1 (as in the case
66 % of rays streaming away from the outer
67 % surface of a hot sphere);
68 %
69 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
70 % center of surface 1 (as in the case
71 % of rays streaming in toward the center
72 % of a hot spherical cavity);
73 %
74 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
75 % radiation coming from surface 1 is
76 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
77 % geometry being considered (as in the
78 % case of an LED panel emitting light in
79 % all directions forward of its front
80 % face).
81 %
82 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2
83 %
84 % = one of three possible values...
85 %
86 % +1 iff incoming rays must move out and
87 % away from the center of surface 2 (as
88 % in the case of rays streaming toward
89 % the inner surface of an integrating sphere);
90 %
91 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
92 % center of surface 2 (as in the case
93 % of rays streaming toward the center
94 % of a hemispherical insolation sensor);
95 %
96 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
97 % radiation coming toward surface 2 is
98 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
99 % geometry being considered (as in the
100 % case of a flat solar cell receiving
101 % radiated energy from all directions in
102 % front of its receiving face).
103 %
                                       669
104 % Output terms:
105 %
106 % F12_view_factor_vec = a vector containing all of the physically
107 % reasonable values of F12 (i.e. F12 <= 1)
108 % generated by the Monte Carlo runs;
109 %
110 % is_ray_obstructed_3mat = the truth values of whether a ray
111 % travelling between the two differential
112 % surfaces of a given geometrically valid
113 % point pair, in a given Monte
114 % Carlo run, is blocked by the obstructing
115 % surface;
116 %
117 % obstruction_point_3mat = the Cartesian coordinates of where a given
118 % obstructed ray is blocked by the
119 % obstructing surface;
120 %
121 % dA1_center_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
122 % the Cartesian (x,y,z) vectors locating
123 % the center-points of quadrilaterals on
124 % surface 1, and whose pages correspond to
125 % each individual cycle of the Monte Carlo
126 % run;
127 %
128 % dA2_center_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
129 % the Cartesian (x,y,z) vectors locating
130 % the center-points of quadrilaterals on
131 % surface 2, and whose pages correspond to
132 % each individual cycle of the Monte Carlo
133 % run;
134 %
135 % n_dA1_normal_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
136 % Cartesian (x,y,z) coordinates
137 % describing the extents of the normal
138 % vectors located at the centers of the
139 % quadrilaterals on surface 1, and whose
140 % pages correspond to each individual cycle
141 % of the Monte Carlo run;
142 %
143 % n_dA2_normal_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
144 % Cartesian (x,y,z) coordinates
145 % describing the extents of the normal
146 % vectors located at the centers of the
147 % quadrilaterals on surface 2, and whose
148 % pages correspond to each individual cycle
149 % of the Monte Carlo run;
150 %
151 % aug_Sobol_mat = a 2-dimensional matrix where each row
152 % contains a vector within the 4-dimensional
153 % Sobol set, along with a probability term
154 % weighting its future choice by a Monte
155 % Carlo routine;
156 %
157 % mag_root_12_valid_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows (and 1
158 % column) represent the r12 values associated
159 % with individual point pairs generated
160 % during a valid (i.e. F12 <= 1) Monte Carlo
161 % cycle, and whose pages represent the
                                       670
162 % simulation run over which that combination
163 % of r12 values occurred;
164 %
165 % mag_root_12_bogus_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows (and 1
166 % column) represent the r12 values associated
167 % with individual point pairs generated
168 % during a bogus (i.e. F12 > 1) Monte Carlo
169 % cycle, and whose pages represent the
170 % simulation run over which that combination
171 % of r12 values occurred;
172 %
173 % avg_F12 = the average value of F12 observed over all
174 % cycles of the Monte Carlo run;
175 %
176 % error = the percent error of the average value of
177 % F12, in comparison with the known value of
178 % F12;
179 %
180 % std_F12 = the absolute standard deviation (unitless)
181 % of the values of F12 obtained by the Monte
182 % Carlo runs;
183 %
184 % and
185 %
186 % RSD = the relative standard deviation (in
187 % percent) of the values of F12 obtained by
188 % the Monte Carlo runs.
189 % Usage:
190 %
191 % [F12_view_factor_vec,...
192 % is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat,...
193 % dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat,...
194 % n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat,...
195 % mag_root_12_valid_3mat,...
196 % mag_root_12_bogus_3mat,...
197 % avg_F12,error,...
198 % std_F12,RSD,...
199 % number_of_bogus_runs,...
200 % run_time_in_s,...
201 % total_valid_point_pairs_assessed,...
202 % grand_total_point_pairs_assessed] =...
203 %
Monte_Carlo_view_factor_obstructed_fix_par_2(n_simulation_runs,n_point_pairs,...
204 % expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs,...
205 % surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
206 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
207 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1,...
208 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2,...
209 % obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat,...
210 % true_val) ;
211
212 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
213 %
214 % 1) This code is restructured to enable parallel execution via parfor.
215 % This is accomplished through the following approaches:
216 %
217 % a) The Sobol matrix is still generated outside the loop in its
218 % entirety. Within the loop, Sobol_select_itr can no longer be passed
                                       671
219 % from cycle to cycle as a monotonically-increasing indexing
220 % variable. (In parallel, each cycle will be executed on a separate
221 % worker core, with no guarantee that any one cycle will be
222 % sequential with any preceding or following cycle.). For this
223 % reason, the Sobol matrix will be executed in blocks that are
224 % indexed directly by the cycle number.
225 %
226 % This is accomplished by:
227 %
228 % i) requiring that the size of the Sobol matrix be an integer
229 % multiple of the number of point pairs;
230 %
231 % ii) removing the contraction-factor denominator as a
232 % user-settable parameter; and
233 %
234 % iii) setting the contraction-factor denominator to 1 within the
235 % code.
236 %
237 % b) Information generated by a given cycle will be passed to the
238 % output vectors and matrices in a cycle-by-cycle, indexed fashion,
239 % as opposed to the sequential, in-place updating scheme employed by
240 % "obs_3."
241 %
242 % 2) This function makes direct use of the following non-MATLAB
243 % subroutines:
244 %
245 % surf_to_area
246 % probabilistic_n_point_pairs_select_w_obstruction_3
247 % aug_sobol_select_8
248 %
249 % 3) This function makes indirect use of the following non-MATLAB
250 % subroutines:
251 %
252 % quadrilateral_pairs_select
253 % diff_view_factor_8
254 % Sobol_learning_system_3
255 % double_check_if_ray_obstructed
256 % is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4
257
258 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
259 %
260 % Validation
261 %
262 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
263
264 if n_simulation_runs <= 0
265 error( 'The number of simulation runs must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
266 else
267 if mod(n_simulation_runs,1) > 0
268 error( 'The number of simulation runs must be an integer.' )
269 else
270 end
271 end
272
273 if n_point_pairs <= 0
274 error( 'The number of point pairs must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
275 else
276 if mod(n_point_pairs,1) > 0
                                       672
277 error( 'The number of point pairs must be an integer.' )
278 else
279 end
280 end

284 else

286 error( 'The number of point pairs must be an integer.' )
287 else

[mean(mean(surf_1_x_mat)),mean(mean(surf_1_y_mat)),mean(mean
(surf_1_z_mat))] ;

[mean(mean(surf_2_x_mat)),mean(mean(surf_2_y_mat)),mean(mean
(surf_2_z_mat))] ;

366 % Monte Carlo Loop

370 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL

372 % For each round of calculation of the view factor...

374 F12_view_factor_vec = zeros(1,n_simulation_runs) ;

376 %n_rept = ceil(n_simulation_runs/10) ;

                                       674
387 contraction_factor_denom = 1 ;

(expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs) ;

expected_ratio_of_total_point_pairs_to_accepted_point_pairs ) * (
n_simulation_runs ) * ( 1 /
contraction_factor_denom ) ) ;
