436 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
                                       675
437 % TTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTT

451 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
452 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL

aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_beginpoint:Sobol_select_endpoint,:) ;

                                       676

501 probabilistic_n_point_pairs_select_w_obstruction_3(n_point_pairs, ...
502 temp_aug_Sobol_mat, ...

504 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
505 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...

522

sum(dF12_vec) ;

533 % one.

536 number_of_valid_runs = number_of_valid_runs + 1
537 disp( ' ')

539 F12_view_factor_vec(1,simulation_itr) = F12_view_factor_value ;
540

549 out_n_dA1_normal_mat = temp_n_dA1_normal_3mat(:,:,simulation_itr) ;

598 % attempt is made to correct it.

CA6.l Monte Carlo Unobstructed View Factor Calculator

Filename: Monte_Carlo_view_factor_27.m


1 function [F12_view_factor_vec, ...
2 dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat, ...
3 n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat, ...
4 aug_Sobol_mat, ...
5 mag_root_12_valid_3mat, ...
6 mag_root_12_bogus_3mat, ...
7 avg_F12,error, ...
8 std_F12,RSD] = ...
9 Monte_Carlo_view_factor_27(n_simulation_runs,n_point_pairs, ...
10 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
11 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
12 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...
13 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2, ...
14 true_val)
15 %
16 % The purpose of this function is to calculate the view factors between
17 % two finite surfaces, using the Monte Carlo method. It assumes that
18 % these two surfaces are unobstructed by any other surface or object.
19 %
20 %
21 % Input terms:
22 %
                                       686
23 % n_simulation_runs = the number of rounds of Monte Carlo
24 % approximation that are to be done in this run
25 % of the routine;
26 %
27 % n_point_pairs = the number of pairs of points that are to be
28 % chosen on surface 1 and surface 2, within each
29 % Monte Carlo run;
30 %
31 % surf_1_x_mat = ; surf_1_y_mat = ; surf_1_z_mat = ;
32 %
33 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 1 in Cartesian
34 % coordinates.
35 %
36 % surf_2_x_mat = ; surf_2_y_mat = ; surf_2_z_mat = ;
37 %
38 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 2 in Cartesian
39 % coordinates.
40 %
41 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1
42 %
43 % = one of three possible values...
44 %
45 % +1 iff rays are emitted out and away from
46 % the center of surface 1 (as in the case
47 % of rays streaming away from the outer
48 % surface of a hot sphere);
49 %
50 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
51 % center of surface 1 (as in the case
52 % of rays streaming in toward the center
53 % of a hot spherical cavity);
54 %
55 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
56 % radiation coming from surface 1 is
57 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
58 % geometry being considered (as in the
59 % case of an LED panel emitting light in
60 % all directions forward of its front
61 % face).
62 %
63 %
64 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2
65 %
66 % = one of three possible values...
67 %
68 % +1 iff incoming rays must move out and
69 % away from the center of surface 2 (as
70 % in the case of rays streaming toward
71 % the inner surface of an integrating sphere);
72 %
73 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
74 % center of surface 2 (as in the case
75 % of rays streaming toward the center
76 % of a hemispherical insolation sensor);
77 %
78 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
79 % radiation coming toward surface 2 is
80 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
                                       687
81 % geometry being considered (as in the
82 % case of a flat solar cell receiving
83 % radiated energy from all directions in
84 % front of its receiving face).
85 %
86 %
87 % Output terms:
88 %
89 % F12_view_factor_vec = a vector containing all of the physically
90 % reasonable values of F12 (i.e. F12 <= 1)
91 % generated by the Monte Carlo runs;
92 %
93 % dA1_center_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
94 % the Cartesian (x,y,z) vectors locating
95 % the center-points of quadrilaterals on
96 % surface 1, and whose pages correspond to
97 % each individual cycle of the Monte Carlo
98 % run;
99 %
100 % dA2_center_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
101 % the Cartesian (x,y,z) vectors locating
102 % the center-points of quadrilaterals on
103 % surface 2, and whose pages correspond to
104 % each individual cycle of the Monte Carlo
105 % run;
106 %
107 % n_dA1_normal_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
108 % Cartesian (x,y,z) coordinates
109 % describing the extents of the normal
110 % vectors located at the centers of the
111 % quadrilaterals on surface 1, and whose
112 % pages correspond to each individual cycle
113 % of the Monte Carlo run;
114 %
115 % n_dA2_normal_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows are
116 % Cartesian (x,y,z) coordinates
117 % describing the extents of the normal
118 % vectors located at the centers of the
119 % quadrilaterals on surface 2, and whose
120 % pages correspond to each individual cycle
121 % of the Monte Carlo run;
122 %
123 % aug_Sobol_mat = a 2-dimensional matrix where each row
124 % contains a vector within the 4-dimensional
125 % Sobol set, along with a probability term
126 % weighting its future choice by a Monte
127 % Carlo routine;
128 %
129 % mag_root_12_valid_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows (and 1
130 % column) represent the r12 values assocated
131 % with individual point pairs generated
132 % during a valid (i.e. F12 <= 1) Monte Carlo
133 % cycle, and whose pages represent the
134 % simulation run over which that combination
135 % of r12 values occured;
136 %
137 % mag_root_12_bogus_3mat = a 3-dimensional matrix whose rows (and 1
138 % column) represent the r12 values assocated
                                       688
139 % with individual point pairs generated
140 % during a bogus (i.e. F12 > 1) Monte Carlo
141 % cycle, and whose pages represent the
142 % simulation run over which that combination
143 % of r12 values occured;
144 %
145 % avg_F12 = the average value of F12 observed over all
146 % cycles of the Monte Carlo run;
147 %
148 % error = the percent error of the average value of
149 % F12, in comparison with the known value of
150 % F12;
151 %
152 % std_F12 = the absolute standard deviation (unitless)
153 % of the values of F12 obtained by the Monte
154 % Carlo runs;
155 %
156 % and
157 %
158 % RSD = the relative standard deviation (in
159 % percent) of the values of F12 obtained by
160 % the Monte Carlo runs.
161 %
162 % Usage:
163 %
164 % [F12_view_factor_vec,...
165 % dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat,...
166 % n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat,...
167 % aug_Sobol_mat,...
168 % mag_root_12_valid_3mat,...
169 % mag_root_12_bogus_3mat,...
170 % avg_F12,error,...
171 % std_F12,RSD] =...
172 % Monte_Carlo_view_factor_27(n_simulation_runs,n_point_pairs,...
173 % surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
174 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
175 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1,...
176 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2,...
177 % true_val);
178
179 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
180 %
181 % 1) This routine differs from its predecessor,
182 % Monte_Carlo_view_factor_26, in that its Sobol matrix generating
183 % subroutine has been altered to make more-efficient use of memory.
184 %
185 % 2) This function makes use of the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
186 % surf_to_area
187 % aug_sobol_select_8
188 % quadrilateral_pairs_select
189 % diff_view_factor_8
190 % Sobol_learning_system_3
191 %
192
193 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
194 %
195 % Validation
196 %
                                       689
197 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV

199 if n_simulation_runs <= 0
200 error( 'The number of simulation runs must be a positive, nonzero number.' )
201 else
202 if mod(n_simulation_runs,1) > 0
203 error( 'The number of simulation runs must be an integer.' )
204 else
205 end
206 end

(n_point_pairs-128) / 128) )

expected_ratio_of_total_points_to_accepted_points ) * ( n_simulation_runs *
expected_ratio_of_total_runs_to_valid_runs ) * ( 1 / contraction_factor_denom ) )

                                       691
305

307
308 % rows_surf_1_x_mat_num = int32(rows_surf_1_x_mat_num) ;

325 rows_surf_2_x_mat_num,cols_surf_2_x_mat_num, ...
326 Sobol_matrix_row_num) ;

328 whos
329
330 Sobol_select_itr = 0 ;
331
332 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix = 0 ;
333
334 for simulation_itr = 1:1:n_simulation_runs
335
336 is_view_factor_valid = 0 ;
337
338 while is_view_factor_valid == 0
339
340 sum_of_diff_view_factors = 0 ;
341
342 valid_point_pairs_num = 0 ;

345
346 %while valid_point_pairs_num <= n_point_pairs
347 for point_pair_itr = 1:1:n_point_pairs
348
349 % Loop back to the beginning of the Sobol matrix if its end has
350 % been reached.
351
352 if Sobol_select_itr == Sobol_matrix_row_num
353 Sobol_select_itr = 1 ;
354 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix = number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix
+ 1
355 else
356 Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr + 1;
357 % if mod(Sobol_select_itr,1000)==0
358 % Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr
359 % else
360 % end
361 end
                                       692
362
363 % Select a point pair probabilistically.
364
365 point_pair_selected = 0 ;
366
367 point_pair_search_itr = 0 ;
368
369 while point_pair_selected == 0
370
371 rand_num = rand() ;
372
373 if aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) >= rand_num
374 point_pair_selected = 1 ;
375 else
376
377 point_pair_search_itr = point_pair_search_itr + 1 ;

380 % point pair, if 100 cycles have elapsed without a
381 % point-pair selection.
382

384 disp( ' ')
385 disp( 'Point pair search halted after 100 cycles.' )

387 else

389 % Loop back to the beginning of the Sobol matrix if its end has
390 % been reached.
391
392 if Sobol_select_itr == Sobol_matrix_row_num
393 Sobol_select_itr = 1 ;
394 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix =
number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix + 1
395 else
396 Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr + 1;
397
398 % if mod(Sobol_select_itr,1000)==0
399 % Sobol_select_itr =
Sobol_select_itr

401 % end
402
403 end

405 end

412 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII

                                       693
418

452 % Generate Quadrilaterals

455 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ

459
460 [surf_1_a_vec,surf_1_b_vec,surf_1_c_vec,surf_1_d_vec, ...

467

469

476 diff_view_factor_8(dA1_mat,dA2_mat, ...
477 surf_1_center_vec, ...

482 % If the resulting differential view factor corresponds to a
483 % physically valid combination of point pairs...
484
485 if is_point_valid == 1

497 % Store the information about the center points of each
498 % differential surface, and their corresponding normals.

500 dA1_center_vec = mean(dA1_mat,1) ;

506 dA2_center_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = dA2_center_vec ;

515 % factor contributions.

521 % Reset the probability of this physically invalid point to
522 % zero, so it cannot be selected again by the routine.
523
524 aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) = 0 ;
525
526 [aug_Sobol_mat] = Sobol_learning_system_3(aug_Sobol_mat,Sobol_select_itr,
is_point_valid);
527
528 end
529
530 end
531
                                       695
532 F12_view_factor_value = ( surf_2_area / valid_point_pairs_num ) *
sum_of_diff_view_factors
533
534 % If the view factor thus obtained is physically realistic...
535
536 if F12_view_factor_value <= 1
537 % ...keep the value, and increment the number of valid runs by
538 % one.
539 is_view_factor_valid = 1 ;
540
541 number_of_valid_runs = number_of_valid_runs + 1
542
543 F12_view_factor_vec(1,simulation_itr) = F12_view_factor_value ;
544
545 % Otherwise...
546 else
547 % ...increment the number of bogus runs by 1, and save the
548 % associated r12 lengths.
549
550 number_of_bogus_runs = number_of_bogus_runs + 1 ;
551
552 mag_root_12_bogus_3mat(:,:,number_of_bogus_runs) = mag_root_12_valid_3mat
(point_pair_itr,1,simulation_itr) ;
553
554 % Periodically update the user on the number of bogus runs that
555 % has been generated.
556
557 if mod(number_of_bogus_runs,10) == 0
558 number_of_bogus_runs = number_of_bogus_runs
559 else
560 end
561
562 end
563
564 end
565
566 % Periodically update the user on the status of the calculation.
567
568 if mod(simulation_itr,n_rept) == 0
569 percent_done = 100*simulation_itr/n_simulation_runs ;
570 formatSpec = 'Run is %4.2f percent done.' ;
571 disp( ' ')
572 fprintf(formatSpec,percent_done)
573 disp( ' ')
574 else
575 end
576
577 %Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr
578
579 %Sobol_matrix_row_num = Sobol_matrix_row_num
580
581 end

583 disp( ' ')
584
585 toc
586
587 % Take the absolute value of the probabilities in the augmented Sobol
                                       696
588 % matrix, so that the physically reasonable points are made available for
589 % use by subsequent library-using Monte Carlo codes.
590
591 %aug_Sobol_mat(:,5) = abs(aug_Sobol_mat(:,5)) ;
592
593 % Output the relevant data from the Monte Carlo run that has just been
594 % completed.
595
596 figure
597 histogram(aug_Sobol_mat(:,5))
598
599 number_of_valid_runs = number_of_valid_runs
600
601 number_of_bogus_runs = number_of_bogus_runs
602
603 avg_F12 = mean(F12_view_factor_vec)
604 error = 100*abs(avg_F12-true_val)/true_val
605 std_F12 = std(F12_view_factor_vec)
606 RSD = 100*(std_F12/avg_F12)
607
608 end

CA6.m Sobol Quadrilateral Point Pairs Generator

Filename: quadrilateral_pairs_select.m


1 function [surf_1_a_vec,surf_1_b_vec,surf_1_c_vec,surf_1_d_vec, ...
2 surf_2_a_vec,surf_2_b_vec,surf_2_c_vec,surf_2_d_vec] = ...
3 quadrilateral_pairs_select(surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
4 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
5 row_col_ind_vec)
6 %
7 % The purpose of this function is to generate a series of quasi-randomly
8 % selected vectors of adjacent points on a surface, using a Sobol-set-based
9 % routine to choose these points.
10 %
11 % Input terms:
12 %
13 % surf_1_x_mat = ; surf_1_y_mat = ; surf_1_z_mat = ;
14 %
15 % surf_2_x_mat = ; surf_2_y_mat = ; surf_2_z_mat = ;
16 %
17 % num_points = ;
18 %
19 % where
20 %
21 % surf_1_x_mat = the meshgrid of x-coordinates of points on
22 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
23 %
24 % surf_1_y_mat = the meshgrid of y-coordinates of points on
25 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
26 %
27 % surf_1_z_mat = the meshgrid of z-coordinates of points on
                                       697
28 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
29 %
30 %
31 % surf_2_x_mat = the meshgrid of x-coordinates of points on
32 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
33 %
34 % surf_2_y_mat = the meshgrid of y-coordinates of points on
35 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
36 %
37 % surf_2_z_mat = the meshgrid of z-coordinates of points on
38 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
39 %
40 % and
41 %
42 % row_col_ind_vec = a vector extracted from the row_col_ind_mat
43 % output of aug_sobol_select_6, with the
44 % structure
45 %
46 % [surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind,surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind]
47 %
48 % Output terms:
49 %
50 % surf_1_a_vec = ; surf_1_b_vec = ; surf_1_c_vec = ; surf_1_d_vec = ;
51 %
52 % surf_2_a_vec = ; surf_2_b_vec = ; surf_2_c_vec = ; surf_2_d_vec = ;
53 %
54 % where
55 %
56 % surf_1_a_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
57 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
58 % coordinates of each "a" point, in each
59 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
60 % 1, that is selected with reference to the
61 % Sobol set;
62 %
63 % surf_1_b_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
64 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
65 % coordinates of each "b" point, in each
66 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
67 % 1, that is selected with reference to the
68 % Sobol set;
69 %
70 % surf_1_c_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
71 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
72 % coordinates of each "c" point, in each
73 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
74 % 1, that is selected with reference to the
75 % Sobol set;
76 %
77 % surf_1_d_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
78 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
79 % coordinates of each "b" point, in each
80 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
81 % 1, that is selected with reference to the
82 % Sobol set;
83 %
84 %
85 % surf_2_a_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
                                       698
86 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
87 % coordinates of each "a" point, in each
88 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
89 % 2, that is selected with reference to the
90 % Sobol set.
91 %
92 % surf_2_b_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
93 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
94 % coordinates of each "b" point, in each
95 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
96 % 2, that is selected with reference to the
97 % Sobol set.
98 %
99 % surf_2_c_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
100 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
101 % coordinates of each "c" point, in each
102 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
103 % 2, that is selected with reference to the
104 % Sobol set.
105 %
106 % surf_2_d_vec = a vector with num_points rows, and 3
107 % columns, representing the (x,y,z)
108 % coordinates of each "b" point, in each
109 % quadrilateral cluster of points in surface
110 % 2, that is selected with reference to the
111 % Sobol set.
112 %
113 % Usage:
114 %
115 % [aug_Sobol_mat,...
116 % surf_1_a_mat,surf_1_b_mat,surf_1_c_mat,surf_1_d_mat,...
117 % surf_2_a_mat,surf_2_b_mat,surf_2_c_mat,surf_2_d_mat] =...
118 % sobol_surface_element_select_5(surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
119 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
120 % num_points);
121
122 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
123 %
124 % This routine only returns vectors of
125 % coordinates for surfaces 1 and 2, given indices specified by a separate
126 % Sobol subroutine (aug_sobol_select_8).
127
128 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
129 %
130 % Validation
131 %
132 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
133
134 if size(surf_1_x_mat)~=size(surf_1_y_mat)
135 error( 'The x and y matrices for suface 1 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
136 else
137 if size(surf_1_x_mat)~=size(surf_1_z_mat)
138 error( 'The x and z matrices for surface 1 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
139 else
140 if size(surf_1_y_mat)~=size(surf_1_z_mat)

                                       699
141 error( 'The y and z matrices for surface 1 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
142 else
143 end
144 end
145 end
146
147
148 if size(surf_2_x_mat)~=size(surf_2_y_mat)
149 error( 'The x and y matrices for surface 2 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
150 else
151 if size(surf_2_x_mat)~=size(surf_2_z_mat)
152 error( 'The x and z matrices for surface 2 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
153 else
154 if size(surf_2_y_mat)~=size(surf_2_z_mat)
155 error( 'The y and z matrices for surface 2 must be meshgrids of identical
size.' )
156 else
157 end
158 end
159 end
160
161 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
162 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
163 %
164 % Extract Indices
165 %
166 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
167 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
168
169 surf_1_row_ind = row_col_ind_vec(1,1) ;
170
171 surf_1_col_ind = row_col_ind_vec(1,2) ;
172
173 surf_2_row_ind = row_col_ind_vec(1,3) ;
174
175 surf_2_col_ind = row_col_ind_vec(1,4) ;
176
177 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
178 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
179 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
180 %
181 % Generate Surface Quadrilaterals
182 %
183 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
184 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
185 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
186
187 % Given these row and column indices, generate the coordinates for the
188 % corresponding (a,b,c,d) quadrilaterals on each surface.
189
190 % For surface 1...
191
192 surf_1_a_x = surf_1_x_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
193
194 surf_1_a_y = surf_1_y_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
                                       700
195
196 surf_1_a_z = surf_1_z_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
197
198 surf_1_a_vec = [ surf_1_a_x, surf_1_a_y, surf_1_a_z ] ;
199
200
201 surf_1_b_x = surf_1_x_mat( surf_1_row_ind, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
202
203 surf_1_b_y = surf_1_y_mat( surf_1_row_ind, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
204
205 surf_1_b_z = surf_1_z_mat( surf_1_row_ind, surf_1_col_ind+1 ) ;
206
207 surf_1_b_vec = [ surf_1_b_x, surf_1_b_y, surf_1_b_z ] ;
208
209
210 surf_1_c_x = surf_1_x_mat( surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind ) ;
211
212 surf_1_c_y = surf_1_y_mat( surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind ) ;
213
214 surf_1_c_z = surf_1_z_mat( surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind ) ;
215
216 surf_1_c_vec = [ surf_1_c_x, surf_1_c_y, surf_1_c_z ] ;
217
218
219 surf_1_d_x = surf_1_x_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind ) ;
220
221 surf_1_d_y = surf_1_y_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind ) ;
222
223 surf_1_d_z = surf_1_z_mat( surf_1_row_ind+1, surf_1_col_ind) ;
224
225 surf_1_d_vec = [ surf_1_d_x, surf_1_d_y, surf_1_d_z ] ;
226
227
228 % ...and for surface 2.
229
230 surf_2_a_x = surf_2_x_mat( surf_2_row_ind+1, surf_2_col_ind+1 ) ;

232 surf_2_a_y = surf_2_y_mat( surf_2_row_ind+1, surf_2_col_ind+1 ) ;

237

240
241 surf_2_b_y = surf_2_y_mat( surf_2_row_ind, surf_2_col_ind+1 ) ;
242
243 surf_2_b_z = surf_2_z_mat( surf_2_row_ind, surf_2_col_ind+1 ) ;
244
245 surf_2_b_vec = [ surf_2_b_x, surf_2_b_y, surf_2_b_z ] ;
246
247
248 surf_2_c_x = surf_2_x_mat( surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind ) ;
249
250 surf_2_c_y = surf_2_y_mat( surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind ) ;
251
252 surf_2_c_z = surf_2_z_mat( surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind ) ;
                                       701
253
254 surf_2_c_vec = [ surf_2_c_x, surf_2_c_y, surf_2_c_z ] ;
255
256
257 surf_2_d_x = surf_2_x_mat( surf_2_row_ind+1, surf_2_col_ind ) ;
258
259 surf_2_d_y = surf_2_y_mat( surf_2_row_ind+1, surf_2_col_ind ) ;
260
261 surf_2_d_z = surf_2_z_mat( surf_2_row_ind+1, surf_2_col_ind) ;
262
263 surf_2_d_vec = [ surf_2_d_x, surf_2_d_y, surf_2_d_z ] ;

CA6.n Generate Quasi-Randomly Selected Vectors of Adjacent Points on a Surface

using Sobol-set Based Routine

Filename: aug_sobol_select_8.m


1 function [aug_Sobol_mat]= ...
2 aug_sobol_select_8(rows_surf_1_x_mat_num,cols_surf_1_x_mat_num, ...
3 rows_surf_2_x_mat_num,cols_surf_2_x_mat_num, ...
4 num_points)
5 %
6 % The purpose of this function is to generate a series of quasi-randomly
7 % selected vectors of adjacent points on a surface, using a Sobol-set-based
8 % routine to choose these points.
9 %
10 % Input terms:
11 %
12 % surf_1_x_mat = ; surf_1_y_mat = ; surf_1_z_mat = ;
13 %
14 % surf_2_x_mat = ; surf_2_y_mat = ; surf_2_z_mat = ;
15 %
16 % num_points = ;
17 %
18 % where
19 %
20 % surf_1_x_mat = the meshgrid of x-coordinates of points on
21 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
22 %
23 % surf_1_y_mat = the meshgrid of y-coordinates of points on
24 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
25 %
26 % surf_1_z_mat = the meshgrid of z-coordinates of points on
27 % surface 1 that are being investigated;
28 %
29 %
30 % surf_2_x_mat = the meshgrid of x-coordinates of points on
31 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
32 %

                                       702
33 % surf_2_y_mat = the meshgrid of y-coordinates of points on
34 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
35 %
36 % surf_2_z_mat = the meshgrid of z-coordinates of points on
37 % surface 2 that are being investigated;
38 %
39 % and
40 %
41 % num_points = the number of points that are to be
42 % selected on each surface.
43 %
44 %
45 % Output terms:
46 %
47 % aug_Sobol_mat = a matrix, where each row is structured as follows:
48 %
49 % [index_num,s1(index_num),s2(index_num),s3(index_num),s4(index_num),
probability_ranking]
50 %
51 % where
52 %
53 % index_num = an integer number representing the position of the
54 % row within the matrix;
55 %
56 % s1(index_number) et al.
57 % = numbers, in the (0,1) domain, from the 4-
58 % dimensional Sobol set being used to select
59 % coordinates within a view factor problem;
60 %
61 % and
62 %
63 % probability_ranking
64 % = a number, in the (0,1) domain, expressing the
65 % probability that a given row will be accepted for
66 % a Monte Carlo step in a view factor calculation.
67 %
68 %
69 % Usage:
70 %
71 % [aug_Sobol_mat]=...
72 % aug_sobol_select_8(rows_surf_1_x_mat_num,cols_surf_1_x_mat_num,...
73 % rows_surf_2_x_mat_num,cols_surf_2_x_mat_num,...
74 % num_points)
75
76 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
77 %
78 % This routine contains code for handling the
79 % preliminary Sobol matrix with
80 % more-efficient use of memory.
81
82 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
83 %
84 % Validation
85 %
86 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
87
88 if num_points < 1
89 error( 'The number of points must be greater than or equal to 1.' )
                                       703
90 else
91 if mod(num_points,1) > 0
92 error( 'The number of points must be an integer number.' )
93 else
94 end
95 end
96
97 num_points = int32(num_points) ;
98
99 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
100 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
101 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
102 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
103 %
104 % Sobol Set Selection System
105 %
106 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
107 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
108 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
109 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
110
111 % Consider the following concepts:
112 %
113 % 1) A Sobol set with four dimensions, and 1000 times the
114 % number of rows requested, is supposed to exist.
115 %
116 % 2) Furthermore, the actual beginning of the Sobol matrix being
117 % generated by this routine happens somewhere within the first
118 % 998*(number of rows) rows of this hypothetical, ginormous Sobol set.
119 %
120 % 3) Additionally, the first 53 rows of any Sobol matrix generated by
121 % sobolset must be skipped, as these represent the initialization length
122 % of the matrix, a region in which the true quasi-random behavior of the
123 % Sobol set does not occur.
124 %
125
126 % Randomly select one run of rows within the output of Sobol set numbers.
127
128 Sobol_row_start_num = ceil( rand() * (num_points*998) ) ;
129
130 % Generate a Sobol set with 4 dimensions, i.e. the number of dimensions in
131 % a view factor calculation. Skip the first 53 rows worth of points, since
132 % these correspond to the "initialization length" of the Sobol set.
133
134 p = sobolset(4, 'skip',((4*53)+(4*Sobol_row_start_num))) ;
135
136 % Using that Sobol set, create a matrix with 4 columns and (100 x number
137 % of points) rows.
138
139 X = tall(net(p,4*num_points*2)) ;
140
141 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
142 % UUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUU
143 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
144 %
145 % Set Up Loop
146 %
147 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
                                       704
148 % UUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUU
149 % LLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLLL
150
151 % Preallocate the matrix for the row and column indices.
152
153 %row_col_ind_mat = zeros(num_points,4) ;
154
155 % Preallocate the augmented Sobol matrix.
156
157 aug_Sobol_mat = zeros(num_points,5) ;
158
159 X0 = gather(X(1:(1+(2*num_points)-1),:)) ;
160
161 size_X0 = size(X0)
162
163 % For each of the points that are to be selected on the surface, using this
164 % routine...
165
166 additional_row_shift = 0 ;
167
168 for point_itr = 1:1:num_points
169
170 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
171 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
172 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
173 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
174 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
175 %
176 % Create Row and Column Indices
177 %
178 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
179 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
180 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
181 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
182 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
183
184 % The Sobol numbers, which are always between 0 and 1, will be
185 % multiplied into (number of rows - 1); the ceiling of this number
186 % will then be taken. This procedure guarantees that, if the number of
187 % rows is 10 (for example), the returned row index will be no lower
188 % than 1, and no higher than 9.
189 %
190 % The same general procedure will also be carried out to generate the
191 % column indices.
192
193 valid_set_of_indices = 0 ;
194
195 while valid_set_of_indices == 0
196
197 % Use the first entry in the Sobol row to generate the row index for
198 % surface 1.
199
200 %X0_row_num = point_itr + additional_row_shift
201
202 surf_1_row_Sobol = X0( 0 + point_itr + additional_row_shift, 1 );
203
204 surf_1_row_ind = ceil(surf_1_row_Sobol * (rows_surf_1_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
205
                                       705
206 surf_1_row_ind = int32(surf_1_row_ind) ;
207
208 % Use the second entry in the Sobol row to generate the column index
209 % for surface 1.
210
211 surf_1_col_Sobol = X0( 0 + point_itr + additional_row_shift, 2 );
212
213 surf_1_col_ind = ceil(surf_1_col_Sobol * (cols_surf_1_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
214
215 surf_1_col_ind = int32(surf_1_col_ind) ;
216
217 % Use the third entry in the Sobol row to generate the row index for
218 % surface 2.
219
220 surf_2_row_Sobol = X0( 0 + point_itr + additional_row_shift, 3 );
221
222 surf_2_row_ind = ceil(surf_2_row_Sobol * (rows_surf_2_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
223
224 surf_2_row_ind = int32(surf_2_row_ind) ;
225
226 % Use the fourth entry in the Sobol row to generate the column index
227 % for surface 2.
228
229 surf_2_col_Sobol = X0( 0 + point_itr + additional_row_shift, 4 );
230
231 surf_2_col_ind = ceil(surf_2_col_Sobol * (cols_surf_2_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
232
233 surf_2_col_ind = int32(surf_2_col_ind) ;
234
235
236 if [surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind] == [surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind]
237 %disp(' ')
238 %disp('Differential surfaces 1 and 2 have identical row and column indices.')
239 additional_row_shift = additional_row_shift + 1 ;
240 else
241 valid_set_of_indices = 1 ;
242
243 aug_Sobol_mat(point_itr,1) = surf_1_row_Sobol ;
244
245 aug_Sobol_mat(point_itr,2) = surf_1_col_Sobol ;
246
247 aug_Sobol_mat(point_itr,3) = surf_2_row_Sobol ;
248
249 aug_Sobol_mat(point_itr,4) = surf_2_col_Sobol ;
250
251 end
252
253
254 end
255
256 end
257
258 % Set up the probability indices of the augmented Sobol matrix before
259 % halting.
260
261 probability_vec = 0.5 .* ones(num_points,1) ;
262
263 probability_vec = probability_vec';
                                       706
264
265 aug_Sobol_mat(:,5) = probability_vec ;
266
267 end




CA6.o Differential View Factor Calculator with Three Normal Orientation Checks

Filename: diff_view_factor_8.m


1 function [is_point_valid, ...
2 diff_view_factor_val, ...
3 n_dA1_normal_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec, ...
4 mag_root_12] = ...
5 diff_view_factor_8(dA1_mat,dA2_mat, ...
6 surf_1_center_vec, ...
7 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...
8 surf_2_center_vec, ...
9 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2)
10 %
11 % Consider two opaque surfaces,1 and 2, that have a fully unobstructed
12 % view of one another. There are no shadowing elements between these
13 % surfaces. Also, there are no convolutions on either surface that shade
14 % parts of that same surface.
15 % Radiant energy is transferred from surface 1 to 2. A view factor, F_12,
16 % must then be constructed to describe the proportion of energy radiated
17 % from surface 1 that reaches surface 2. Computing this view factor will
18 % require summing up all the contributions of differential areas dA1 and
19 % dA2 on these two surfaces.
20 %
21 % The purpose of this function, then, is to calculate the contribution
22 % made by one pair of these areas to the overall view factor.
23 %
24 %
25 % Input terms:
26 %
27 % Each differential surface element is described by a matrix of four
28 % (x,y,z) triples, describing four immediately adjacent points on the
29 % surface.
30 %
31 % If we designate those points on each surface as being arranged in a
32 % counterclockwise manner...
33 %
34 % c------b
35 % |      |
36 % |      |
37 % d------a
38 %
39 % it follows that
40 %
41 % dA1_mat = [ (x1a, y1a, z1a)
42 % (x1b, y1b, z1b)
43 % (x1c, y1c, z1c)
44 % (x1d, y1d, z1d) ]
45 %
                                       707
46 % and
47 %
48 % dA2_mat = [ (x2a, y2a, z2a)
49 % (x2b, y2b, z2b)
50 % (x2c, y2c, z2c)
51 % (x2d, y2d, z2d) ]
52 %
53 %
54 % surf_1_center_vec = the 3D location of the center of surface 1.
55 %
56 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1
57 %
58 % = one of three possible values...
59 %
60 % +1 iff rays are emitted out and away from
61 % the center of surface 1 (as in the case
62 % of rays streaming away from the outer
63 % surface of a hot sphere);
64 %
65 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
66 % center of surface 1 (as in the case
67 % of rays streaming in toward the center
68 % of a hot spherical cavity);
69 %
70 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
71 % radiation coming from surface 1 is
72 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
73 % geometry being considered (as in the
74 % case of an LED panel emitting light in
75 % all directions forward of its front
76 % face).
77 %
78 % surf_2_center_vec = the 3D location of the center of surface 2.
79 %
80 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2
81 %
82 % = one of three possible values...
83 %
84 % +1 iff incoming rays must move out and
85 % away from the center of surface 2 (as
86 % in the case of rays streaming toward
87 % the inner surface of an integrating sphere);
88 %
89 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
90 % center of surface 2 (as in the case
91 % of rays streaming toward the center
92 % of a hemispherical insolation sensor);
93 %
94 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
95 % radiation coming toward surface 2 is
96 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
97 % geometry being considered (as in the
98 % case of a flat solar cell receiving
99 % radiated energy from all directions in
100 % front of its receiving face).
101 % Usage:
102 %
103 % [is_point_valid,...
                                       708
104 % diff_view_factor_val,...
105 % n_dA1_normal_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec,...
106 % mag_root_12] = ...
107 % diff_view_factor_8(dA1_mat,dA2_mat,...
108 % surf_1_center_vec,...
109 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1,...
110 % surf_2_center_vec,...
111 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2)
112
113 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
114 %
115 % This routine uses a third round of normal
116 % orientation checks is being implemented, to
117 % enforce correct orientation of the normals in cases where convex surfaces
118 % are being used. Finally, the "sanity check" step
119 % is being used, to assess whether or not a proposed combination of dA1
120 % and dA2 will yield physically realistic results, i.e. a ray propagating
121 % out of surface 1 as it goes toward surface 2.
122
123 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
124 %
125 % Validation
126 %
127 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
128
129 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1 ~= -1
130 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1 ~= 0
131 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1 ~= +1
132 disp( ' ')
133 error( 'The value for movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1 must be
-1,
0 or +1.' )
134 else
135 end
136 else
137 end
138 else
139 end
140
141 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 ~= -1
142 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 ~= 0
143 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 ~= +1
144 disp( ' ')
145 error( 'The value for movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 must be
-1,
0 or +1.' )
146 else
147 end
148 else
149 end
150 else
151 end
152
153 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
154 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
155 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
156 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
157 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
                                       709
158 %
159 % Generate Normals of Differential Areas
160 %
161 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
162 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
163 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
164 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
165 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
166
167 % Calculate the surface normal to both of these surface elements. This is
168 % done in two steps:
169 % 1) Find the cross product of the two diagonals in each surface
170 % element.
171 % 2) Find the orientation of these two normals that makes them point
172 % both in opposite senses, and "toward" one another.
173
174 % dA1 Diagonal 1 is defined as the (a,c) vector of dA1.
175
176 dA1_diag_1_vec = [ (dA1_mat(3,1)-dA1_mat(1,1)), (dA1_mat(3,2)-dA1_mat(1,2)),
(dA1_mat(3,3)-
dA1_mat(1,3)) ] ;
177
178 % dA1 Diagonal 2 is defined as the (b,d) vector of dA1.
179
180 dA1_diag_2_vec = [ (dA1_mat(4,1)-dA1_mat(2,1)), (dA1_mat(4,2)-dA1_mat(2,2)),
(dA1_mat(4,3)-
dA1_mat(2,3)) ] ;
181
182 % Using these two vectors, construct the normal to area 1, n_1.
183
184 dA1_normal_vec = cross_product( dA1_diag_1_vec,dA1_diag_2_vec );
185
186 n_dA1_normal_vec = dA1_normal_vec / magnitude(dA1_normal_vec) ;
187
188 % dA2 Diagonal 1 is defined as the (a,c) vector of dA2.
189
190 dA2_diag_1_vec = [ (dA2_mat(3,1)-dA2_mat(1,1)), (dA2_mat(3,2)-dA2_mat(1,2)),
(dA2_mat(3,3)-
dA2_mat(1,3)) ] ;
191
192 % dA2 Diagonal 2 is defined as the (b,d) vector of dA2.
193
194 dA2_diag_2_vec = [ (dA2_mat(4,1)-dA2_mat(2,1)), (dA2_mat(4,2)-dA2_mat(2,2)),
(dA2_mat(4,3)-
dA2_mat(2,3)) ] ;
195
196 % Using these two vectors, construct the normal to area 2, n_2.
197
198 dA2_normal_vec = cross_product( dA2_diag_1_vec,dA2_diag_2_vec );
199
200 n_dA2_normal_vec = dA2_normal_vec / magnitude(dA2_normal_vec) ;
201
202 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
203 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
204 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
205 %
206 % Orientation of Normals
207 %
                                       710
208 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
209 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
210 % NNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNNN
211
212 % Step 2 is accomplished in the following manner:
213 % a) Construct the line r_12 that connects the roots of n_1 and n_2.
214 % Call the normalized vector that describes this line's direction
215 % n_12.
216 % b) Project n_1 and n_2 onto n_12.
217 % c) If the projection of n_1 has the same sign as the projection of
218 % n_2, reverse the orientation of n_2.
219 % d) Add n_12 to the projection of n_2. If the result is larger than
220 % n_12, leave the normals as they are. Otherwise, reverse the
221 % orientations of both normals.
222
223 % r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12
224 % Construct line r_12
225 % r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12r12
226
227 % Determine the coordinates of the "roots" of each surface.
228
229 dA1_root_vec = mean(dA1_mat,1) ;
230
231 dA2_root_vec = mean(dA2_mat,1) ;
232
233 % Calculate the line segment r_12 joining these elements.
234
235 root_12_vec = dA2_root_vec - dA1_root_vec ;
236
237 % Determine the magnitude of r_12.
238
239 mag_root_12 = magnitude(root_12_vec) ;
240
241 % Determine the direction of r_12.
242
243 n_root_12_vec = root_12_vec ./ mag_root_12 ;
244
245 % DNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNOD
246 % Determine Normals' Orientation
247 % DNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNODNOD
248
249 % Find the dot product of n_1 and n_2.
250
251 dp_of_n1_and_n2 = dot_product(n_dA1_normal_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec) ;
252
253 theta_dp_of_n1_and_n2 = acos( dp_of_n1_and_n2
/(magnitude(n_dA1_normal_vec)*magnitude
(n_dA2_normal_vec)) ) ;
254
255 % If the resulting angle is greater than or equal to pi/2...
256
257 if theta_dp_of_n1_and_n2 >= pi/2
258 %disp('n_1 and n_2 are pointing the opposite way')
259 % ...keep the normals as they are.
260 % Otherwise...
261 else
262 %disp('n_1 and n_2 are pointing the same way')
263 % ...reverse the orientation of n_2.
                                       711
264 n_dA2_normal_vec = -n_dA2_normal_vec ;
265 end
266
267 % At this point, it is guaranteed that n_1 and n_2 will both be
268 % antiparallel to one another. This means that they must either be:
269 % a) pointing toward one another (the correct orientation); or
270 % b) pointing away from one another (the incorrect orientation).
271
272 % Find the projection of n1 on r12.
273
274 n1_proj_on_r12 = dot_product(n_dA1_normal_vec,root_12_vec) ;
275
276 % Find the projection of n2 on r12.
277
278 n2_proj_on_r12 = dot_product(n_dA2_normal_vec,root_12_vec) ;
279
280 % Vectorize the two projections using the normalized r12, then adjust
281 % their magnitudes so that they are at most ||r12||/2.
282
283 n1_proj_on_r12_vec = n1_proj_on_r12 * n_root_12_vec ;
284
285 n2_proj_on_r12_vec = n2_proj_on_r12 * n_root_12_vec ;
286
287 rescaled_n1_proj_on_r12_vec = n1_proj_on_r12_vec *
(1/magnitude(n1_proj_on_r12_vec)) *
(mag_root_12/2) ;
288
289 rescaled_n2_proj_on_r12_vec = n2_proj_on_r12_vec *
(1/magnitude(n2_proj_on_r12_vec)) *
(mag_root_12/2) ;
290
291 % Flip the first vector, then add these two vectors to r12.
292
293 sum_of_three_vec = -rescaled_n1_proj_on_r12_vec + root_12_vec +
rescaled_n2_proj_on_r12_vec ;
294
295 % If the resulting vector is longer than r_12...
296 if magnitude(sum_of_three_vec) > mag_root_12
297 % ...it follows that n_1 and n_2 are pointing away from each other.
298 % Reverse the orientation of both normals.
299 n_dA1_normal_vec = -n_dA1_normal_vec ;
300 n_dA2_normal_vec = -n_dA2_normal_vec ;
301 % Otherwise....
302 else
303 % ...leave the normals as they are.
304 end
305
306 % This series of steps is guaranteed to provide the correct orientation of
307 % normals for surfaces that are at angles less than pi/2 to one another.
308 % "Open-book cases," where the surfaces are at greater angles than this,
309 % will need to have a second round of adjustments performed in the next
310 % step.
311
312 %n_dA1_normal_vec = n_dA1_normal_vec
313
314 %n_dA2_normal_vec = n_dA2_normal_vec
315
316 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
                                       712
317 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
318 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
319 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
320 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
321 %
322 % Calculation of Differential View Factor
323 %
324 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
325 % OOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO
326 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
327 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
328 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
329
330 % Find the angles between the surface normals and n_12.
331
332 beta_1 = acos(dot_product(n_dA1_normal_vec,n_root_12_vec)) ;
333
334 %cos_beta_1 = cos(beta_1)
335
336 % CNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNO
337 % --Confirm Normals' Orientation--
338 % CNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNOCNO
339
340 % As was noted above, the above normals-orientation scheme can yield
341 % incorrect (beta > pi/2) results in the open-book normals case. Reversing
342 % the orientation of associated normals will fix this problem, in cases
343 % where it does arise. It will do so, furthermore, without interfering with
344 % the "canonical" cases of normals sprouting from directly-opposing
345 % surfaces.
346
347 if beta_1 > pi/2
348 %beta_1 = beta_1
349 %disp(' ')
350 %disp('revise beta 1')
351 n_dA1_normal_vec = -n_dA1_normal_vec ;
352 %n_root_12_vec = n_root_12_vec
353 beta_1 = acos(dot_product(n_dA1_normal_vec,n_root_12_vec)) ;
354 else
355 end
356
357 %size(beta_1)
358
359 beta_2 = acos(dot_product(-n_root_12_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec)) ;
360
361 %cos_beta_2 = cos(beta_2)
362
363 if beta_2 > pi/2
364 %beta_2 = beta_2
365 %disp(' ')
366 %disp('revise beta 2')
367 %negative_n_root_12_vec = -n_root_12_vec
368 %beta_2 = acos(dot_product(-n_root_12_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec))
369 beta_2 = pi - beta_2 ;
370 n_dA2_normal_vec = -n_dA2_normal_vec;
371 else
372 end
373
374 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
                                       713
375 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
376 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
377 %
378 % Concave Surfaces Check
379 %
380 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
381 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
382 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
383
384 % A third level of normal orientation checks has to be performed in cases
385 % where concave surfaces are involved (e.g. capped frustums, cylinders
386 % sleeved around internal radiating surfaces). In such cases, the user
387 % needs to explicitly specify whether a surface is radiating away from its
388 % center, or toward its center. If this step is not performed, bogus
389 % results, such as rays originating from both the outer and inner aspects
390 % of a surface, can occur.
391
392 % If the user has specified that the radiating direction is important for
393 % surface 1....
394
395 is_point_valid = 1 ;
396
397 if abs(movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1) > 0
398 ...check that the corresponding conditions are satisfied.
399
400 dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center = sqrt( ((dA1_root_vec(1,1)-
surf_1_center_vec(1,1))
^2) + ((dA1_root_vec(1,2)-surf_1_center_vec(1,2))^2) + ((dA1_root_vec(1,3)-
surf_1_center_vec
(1,3))^2) ) ;
401
402 s1_to_n1_delta_x =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center.*n_dA1_normal_vec(1,1)) +
dA1_root_vec(1,1) - surf_1_center_vec(1,1) ;
403
404 s1_to_n1_delta_y =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center.*n_dA1_normal_vec(1,2)) +
dA1_root_vec(1,2) - surf_1_center_vec(1,2) ;
405
406 s1_to_n1_delta_z =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center.*n_dA1_normal_vec(1,3)) +
dA1_root_vec(1,3) - surf_1_center_vec(1,3) ;
407
408 dist_from_surf_1_center_to_n1 = sqrt( (s1_to_n1_delta_x^2) +
(s1_to_n1_delta_y^2) +
(s1_to_n1_delta_z^2) ) ;
409
410 % If the user has specified that rays must be moving away from
411 % the center of surface 1...
412
413 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1 > 0
414 % ...confirm that the normal at dA1 is oriented outward from the
415 % center of surface 1.
416
417 % If n1 is not oriented outward...
418
419 if dist_from_surf_1_center_to_n1 < dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center
420 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
                                       714
421 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
422
423 %disp(' ')
424 %disp('point pair rejected at n1 outward check')
425 is_point_valid = 0 ;
426
427 else
428
429 % If the user has specified that the radiating direction is important for
430 % surface 2....
431
432 if abs(movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2) > 0
433
434 % If the user has specified that rays must be moving away from
435 % the center of surface 2...
436
437 dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center = sqrt( ((dA2_root_vec(1,1)-
surf_2_center_vec(1,1))^2) + ((dA2_root_vec(1,2)-surf_2_center_vec(1,2))^2) +
((dA2_root_vec(1,3)
-surf_2_center_vec(1,3))^2) ) ;
438
439 %dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center = dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
440
441 %n_dA2_normal_vec = n_dA2_normal_vec
442
443 %dA2_root_vec = dA2_root_vec
444
445 %surf_2_center_vec = surf_2_center_vec
446
447 s2_to_n2_delta_x =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,1)) + dA2_root_vec(1,1) - surf_2_center_vec(1,1) ;
448
449 s2_to_n2_delta_y =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,2)) + dA2_root_vec(1,2) - surf_2_center_vec(1,2) ;
450
451 s2_to_n2_delta_z =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,3)) + dA2_root_vec(1,3) - surf_2_center_vec(1,3) ;
452
453 dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 = sqrt( (s2_to_n2_delta_x^2) +
(s2_to_n2_delta_y^2)
+ (s2_to_n2_delta_z^2) ) ;
454
455 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 > 0
456 % ...confirm that the normal at dA2 is oriented inward, toward the
457 % center of surface 2.
458
459 % If n2 is not oriented inward...
460
461 if dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 > dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
462 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
463 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
464
465 %disp(' ')
466 %disp('point pair rejected at n2 inward check')
467
                                       715
468 is_point_valid = 0 ;
469
470 else
471 end
472
473 % Otherwise, if the user has specified that rays must be moving
474 % toward the center of surface 2...
475 else
476 % ...confirm that the normal at dA2 is oriented outward, toward
477 % these incoming rays.
478
479 % If n2 is not oriented outward...
480
481 if dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 < dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
482 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
483 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
484
485 %disp(' ')
486 %disp('point pair rejected at n2 outward check')
487
488 is_point_valid = 0 ;
489
490 else
491 end
492
493 end
494
495 else
496 end
497
498 end
499
500 % Otherwise, if the user has specified that rays must be moving toward
501 % the center of surface 1...
502
503 else
504 % ...confirm that the normal at dA1 is oriented inward, toward the
505 % center of surface 1.
506
507 % If n1 is not oriented inward...
508
509 if dist_from_surf_1_center_to_n1 > dist_from_surf_1_center_to_dA1_center
510 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
511 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
512
513 %disp(' ')
514 %disp('point pair rejected at n1 inward check')
515
516 is_point_valid = 0 ;
517
518 else
519
520 % If the user has specified that the radiating direction is important for
521 % surface 2....
522
523 if abs(movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2) > 0
524
525 % If the user has specified that rays must be moving away from
                                       716
526 % the center of surface 2...
527
528
529 dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center = sqrt( ((dA2_root_vec(1,1)-
surf_2_center_vec(1,1))^2) + ((dA2_root_vec(1,2)-surf_2_center_vec(1,2))^2) +
((dA2_root_vec(1,3)
-surf_2_center_vec(1,3))^2) ) ;
530
531 %dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center = dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
532
533 %n_dA2_normal_vec = n_dA2_normal_vec
534
535 %dA2_root_vec = dA2_root_vec
536
537 %surf_2_center_vec = surf_2_center_vec
538
539 s2_to_n2_delta_x =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,1)) + dA2_root_vec(1,1) - surf_2_center_vec(1,1) ;
540
541 s2_to_n2_delta_y =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,2)) + dA2_root_vec(1,2) - surf_2_center_vec(1,2) ;
542
543 s2_to_n2_delta_z =
(0.1*dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center.*n_dA2_normal_vec
(1,3)) + dA2_root_vec(1,3) - surf_2_center_vec(1,3) ;
544
545 dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 = sqrt( (s2_to_n2_delta_x^2) +
(s2_to_n2_delta_y^2)
+ (s2_to_n2_delta_z^2) ) ;
546
547 if movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2 > 0
548 % ...confirm that the normal at dA2 is oriented inward, toward the
549 % center of surface 2.
550
551 % If n2 is not oriented inward...
552
553 if dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 > dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
554 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
555 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
556 is_point_valid = 0 ;
557
558 else
559 end
560
561 % Otherwise, if the user has specified that rays must be moving
562 % toward the center of surface 2...
563 else
564 % ...confirm that the normal at dA2 is oriented outward, toward
565 % these incoming rays.
566
567 % If n2 is not oriented outward...
568
569 if dist_from_surf_2_center_to_n2 < dist_from_surf_2_center_to_dA2_center
570 % ...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
571 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
572 is_point_valid = 0 ;
                                       717
573
574 else
575 end
576
577 end
578
579 else
580 end
581
582 end
583
584 end
