586 else
587 end
588
589 % SCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSC
590 % Sanity Check
591 % SCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSCSC
592 %
593 % Check the orientation of the r12 direction vector, relative to the normal
594 % at dA1. If the angle between these two vectors is greater than pi/2, this
595 % corresponds to a situation where the ray is going backwards into surface
596 % 1, which is unphysical.
597
598 dot_prod_n_r12_and_n1 = dot_product(n_root_12_vec,n_dA1_normal_vec) ;
599
600 if is_point_valid==0
601
602 diff_view_factor_val = [] ;
603
604 n_dA1_normal_vec = [] ;
605
606 n_dA2_normal_vec = [] ;
607
608 mag_root_12 = [] ;
609
610 else
611
612 if acos(dot_prod_n_r12_and_n1) >= pi/2
613 %...this specific combination of dA1 and dA2 yields bogus results, and
614 % there is no point in calculating the differential view factor.
615
616 is_point_valid = 0 ;
617
618 diff_view_factor_val = [] ;
619
620 n_dA1_normal_vec = [] ;
621
622 n_dA2_normal_vec = [] ;
623
624 mag_root_12 = [] ;
625
626 else
627
628 % This specific combination of dA1 and dA2 will yield legitimate
629 % results, and the calculation of the differential view factor should
630 % proceed.
                                       718
631
632 is_point_valid = 1 ;
633
634 % Compute the value of the differential view factor for these
635 % two differential areas.
636
637 if beta_1 > pi/2
638 beta_1 = beta_1
639 else
640 end
641
642 if beta_2 > pi/2
643 beta_2 = beta_2
644 else
645 end
646
647 diff_view_factor_val = (cos(beta_1)*cos(beta_2)) / (pi * (mag_root_12^2)) ;
648
649 end
650
651 end
652
653 end
654




CA6.p Meshgrid X,Y,Z Surface Points to Area

Filename: surf_to_area.m


1 function [surf_area] = surf_to_area(surf_x_mat,surf_y_mat,surf_z_mat)
2 %
3 % This function takes, as input, meshgrids that correspond to the (x,y,z)
4 % Cartesian coordinates of a 3-D surface. It then returns, as output, the
5 % overall area of this surface, as estimated using repeated application
6 % of the Bretschneider formula.
7 %
8 % Usage:
9 %
10 % [surf_area] = surf_to_area(surf_x_mat,surf_y_mat,surf_z_mat)
11 %
12 %
13 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
14 %
15 % This function makes indirect use of the following non-MATLAB
16 % subroutine:
17 %
18 % Bretschneider
19
20 % Validate the input.
21
22 if size(surf_x_mat)~=size(surf_y_mat)
23 error( 'The x and y matrices must be meshgrids of identical size.' )
24 else
25 if size(surf_x_mat)~=size(surf_z_mat)
                                       719
26 error( 'The x and z matrices must be meshgrids of identical size.' )
27 else
28 if size(surf_y_mat)~=size(surf_z_mat)
29 error( 'The y and z matrices must be meshgrids of identical size.' )
30 else
31 end
32 end
33 end
34
35 surf_area = 0 ;
36
37 % Iterate across each quadruple of points in the meshgrids.
38
39 [row_num,col_num] = size(surf_x_mat) ;
40
41 for row_itr = 1:1:row_num-1
42 for col_itr = 1:1:col_num-1
43 a_x = surf_x_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr+1) ;
44
45 a_y = surf_y_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr+1) ;
46
47 a_z = surf_z_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr+1) ;
48
49 a_vec = [a_x,a_y,a_z] ;
50
51
52 b_x = surf_x_mat(row_itr,col_itr+1) ;
53
54 b_y = surf_y_mat(row_itr,col_itr+1) ;
55
56 b_z = surf_z_mat(row_itr,col_itr+1) ;
57
58 b_vec = [b_x,b_y,b_z] ;
59
60
61 c_x = surf_x_mat(row_itr,col_itr) ;
62
63 c_y = surf_y_mat(row_itr,col_itr) ;
64
65 c_z = surf_z_mat(row_itr,col_itr) ;
66
67 c_vec = [c_x,c_y,c_z] ;
68
69
70 d_x = surf_x_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr) ;
71
72 d_y = surf_y_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr) ;
73
74 d_z = surf_z_mat(row_itr+1,col_itr) ;
75
76 d_vec = [d_x,d_y,d_z] ;
77
78 quadrilateral_mat = vertcat(a_vec,b_vec,c_vec,d_vec) ;
79
80 [area] = Bretschneider(quadrilateral_mat) ;
81
82 surf_area = surf_area + area ;
83
                                       720
84 end
85 end
86
87 end
88




CA6.q Bretschneider Calculation Routine

Filename: Bretschneider.m


1 function [area] = Bretschneider(quadrilateral_mat)
2 %
3 % Input terms:
4 %
5 % Each area matrix has four (x,y,z) triples, describing four immediately
6 % adjacent points on a 3-dimesional surface in Cartesian coordinates.
7 %
8 % If we designate those points on each surface as being arranged in a
9 % counterclockwise manner...
10 %
11 %      b
12 % C-------B
13 % |        |
14 % c|       | a
15 % |        |
16 % D-------A
17 %      d
18 %
19 % it follows that
20 %
21 % quadrilateral_mat = [ (x1A, y1A, z1A)
22 % (x1B, y1B, z1B)
23 % (x1C, y1C, z1C)
24 % (x1D, y1D, z1D) ]
25
26 magnitude_a = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(2,:)-quadrilateral_mat(1,:)) ;
27
28 magnitude_b = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(3,:)-quadrilateral_mat(2,:)) ;
29
30 magnitude_c = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(4,:)-quadrilateral_mat(3,:)) ;
31
32 magnitude_d = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(1,:)-quadrilateral_mat(4,:)) ;
33
34 magnitude_e = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(3,:)-quadrilateral_mat(1,:)) ;
35
36 magnitude_f = magnitude(quadrilateral_mat(4,:)-quadrilateral_mat(2,:)) ;
37
38 perimeter = magnitude_a + magnitude_b + magnitude_c + magnitude_d ;
39
40 semiperimeter = perimeter / 2 ;
41
42 first_radical_term = ( semiperimeter - magnitude_a ) * ( semiperimeter -
magnitude_b ) *
( semiperimeter - magnitude_c ) * ( semiperimeter - magnitude_d ) ;
                                       721
43
44 second_radical_term = -0.25 * ( (magnitude_a*magnitude_c) +
(magnitude_b*magnitude_d) +
(magnitude_e*magnitude_f) ) * ( (magnitude_a*magnitude_c) +
(magnitude_b*magnitude_d) -
(magnitude_e*magnitude_f) ) ;
45
46 area = sqrt( first_radical_term + second_radical_term ) ;
47
48 end
49




CA6.r Probabilistic Point Pair Selector

Filename: probabilistic_n_point_pairs_select_w_obstruction_3.m


1 function [dF12_vec, ...
2 is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat, ...
3 dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat, ...
4 n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat, ...
5 mag_root_12_valid_3mat, ...
6 Sobol_select_itr,point_pair_itr,valid_point_pairs_num] = ...
7 probabilistic_n_point_pairs_select_w_obstruction_3(n_point_pairs, ...
8 aug_Sobol_mat, ...
9 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
10 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
11 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...
12 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2, ...
13 surf_1_center_vec,surf_2_center_vec, ...
14 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat, ...
15 simulation_itr, ...
16 Sobol_matrix_row_num, ...
17 Sobol_select_itr,point_pair_itr,valid_point_pairs_num, ...
18 dF12_vec, ...
19 is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat, ...
20 dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat, ...
21 n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat)
22 %
23 % The purpose of this function is to select a requested number of point
24 % pairs for a Monte Carlo view factor calculation routine, by using
25 % probabilistic codes. These probabilistic codes are based on two things:
26 %
27 % 1) The augmented Sobol matrix. This matrix consists of rows that
28 % contain both the 4-dimensional Sobol set vectors, and the probability
29 % that each row will be selected. These probabilities are chosen on the
30 % basis of how close these point pairs are, in the current Monte Carlo
31 % view factor problem, to other point pairs that are physically valid or
32 % physically invalid.
33 %
34 % 2) The libraries of r12 values. Reasonable F12 values (i.e. F12 <=1 )
35 % are associated with point-pair sets that give one distinct distribution
36 % of r12 values. Bogus F12 values (i.e. F12 > 1), in turn, are associated
37 % with point-pair sets that give a second, different distribution of r12
38 % values. New choices of points, then, can be accepted or rejected on the
                                          722
39 % basis of how these "library" r12 distributions compare to one another.
40 %
41 % Input terms:
42 %
43 % n_point_pairs = the number of pairs of points that are to be
44 % chosen on surface 1 and surface 2, within each
45 % Monte Carlo run;
46 %
47 % aug_Sobol_mat = a matrix where each row is a vector that
48 % represents a point in the 4-dimensional Sobol
49 % set, along with a 5th point that specifies the
50 % probability of that point being selected by
51 % this routine;
52 %
53 % surf_1_x_mat = ; surf_1_y_mat = ; surf_1_z_mat = ;
54 %
55 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 1 in Cartesian
56 % coordinates.
57 %
58 % surf_2_x_mat = ; surf_2_y_mat = ; surf_2_z_mat = ;
59 %
60 % where these are meshgrids representing surface 2 in Cartesian
61 % coordinates.
62 %
63 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1
64 %
65 % = one of three possible values...
66 %
67 % +1 iff rays are emitted out and away from
68 % the center of surface 1 (as in the case
69 % of rays streaming away from the outer
70 % surface of a hot sphere);
71 %
72 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
73 % center of surface 1 (as in the case
74 % of rays streaming in toward the center
75 % of a hot spherical cavity);
76 %
77 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
78 % radiation coming from surface 1 is
79 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
80 % geometry being considered (as in the
81 % case of an LED panel emitting light in
82 % all directions forward of its front
83 % face).
84 %
85 %
86 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2
87 %
88 % = one of three possible values...
89 %
90 % +1 iff incoming rays must move out and
91 % away from the center of surface 2 (as
92 % in the case of rays streaming toward
93 % the inner surface of an integrating sphere);
94 %
95 % -1 iff rays are moving into and toward the
96 % center of surface 2 (as in the case
                                       723
97 % of rays streaming toward the center
98 % of a hemispherical insolation sensor);
99 %
100 % 0 iff the "sense" of the emitted
101 % radiation coming toward surface 2 is
102 % deemed unimportant, by the user, to the
103 % geometry being considered (as in the
104 % case of a flat solar cell receiving
105 % radiated energy from all directions in
106 % front of its receiving face).
107 %
108 %
109 % Usage:
110 %
111 % [dF12_vec,...
112 % is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat,...
113 % dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat,...
114 % n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat,...
115 % mag_root_12_valid_3mat,...
116 % Sobol_select_itr,point_pair_itr,valid_point_pairs_num] =...
117 % probabilistic_n_point_pairs_select_w_obstruction_3(n_point_pairs,...
118 % aug_Sobol_mat,...
119 % surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
120 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
121 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1,...
122 % movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2,...
123 % surf_1_center_vec,surf_2_center_vec,...
124 % Sobol_matrix_row_num,...
125 % Sobol_select_itr,point_pair_itr,valid_point_pairs_num,...
126 % dF12_vec,...
127 % is_ray_obstructed_3mat,obstruction_point_3mat,...
128 % dA1_center_3mat,dA2_center_3mat,...
129 % n_dA1_normal_3mat,n_dA2_normal_3mat)
130
131 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
132 %
133 % This routine makes direct use of the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
134 %
135 % quadrilateral_pairs_select
136 % diff_view_factor_8
137 % Sobol_learning_system_3
138 % is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4
139
140 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
141 %
142 % Initialization
143 %
144 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
145
146 % Determine the size of the surface 1 x matrix.
147
148 [rows_surf_1_x_mat_num,cols_surf_1_x_mat_num] = size(surf_1_x_mat) ;
149
150 % Determine the size of the surface 2 x matrix.
151
152 [rows_surf_2_x_mat_num,cols_surf_2_x_mat_num] = size(surf_2_x_mat) ;
153
154 %dF12_vec = zeros(n_point_pairs,1) ;
                                       724
155
156 % Select the requested number of point pairs.
157
158 %Sobol_select_itr = 0 ;
159
160 %Sobol_select_itr_before_reset = 0 ;
161
162 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix = 0 ;
163
164 %sum_of_diff_view_factors = 0 ;
165
166 %valid_point_pairs_num = 0 ;
167
168 %point_pair_itr = 1 ;
169
170 tic
171
172 %valid_point_pairs_num = valid_point_pairs_num
173
174 %n_point_pairs = n_point_pairs
175
176 while valid_point_pairs_num < n_point_pairs
177
178 % Find a point pair, subject to a series of conditions.
179
180 % NOTE: The point pair that is ultimately selected by this part
181 % of the code will be referred to as the "honest-to-God point
182 % pair" (htg).
183
184 htg_point_pair_selected = 0 ;
185
186 while htg_point_pair_selected == 0
187
188 candidate_point_pair_selected = 0 ;
189
190 point_pair_search_itr = 0 ;
191
192 while candidate_point_pair_selected == 0
193
194 % Reset the Sobol iteration number to 1 if the end
195 % of the Sobol matrix has been reached.
196
197 if Sobol_select_itr == Sobol_matrix_row_num
198 %Sobol_select_itr_before_reset = Sobol_select_itr_before_reset +
Sobol_select_itr ;
199 Sobol_select_itr = 1 ;
200 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix = number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix
+ 1
201 else
202 Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr + 1;
203 end
204
205 % Choose a point pair probabilistically.
206
207 rand_num_1 = rand() ;
208
209 if aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) >= rand_num_1
210 candidate_point_pair_selected = 1 ;
                                       725
211 else
212
213 point_pair_search_itr = point_pair_search_itr + 1 ;
214
215 % Halt iteration, and force selection of the current
216 % point pair, if 100 cycles have elapsed without a
217 % point-pair selection.
218
219 if point_pair_search_itr >= 100
220 disp( ' ')
221 disp( 'Point pair search halted after 100 cycles.' )
222 candidate_point_pair_selected = 1 ;
223 else
224 % Reset the Sobol iteration number to 1 if the end
225 % of the Sobol matrix has been reached.
226
227 if Sobol_select_itr == Sobol_matrix_row_num
228 %Sobol_select_itr_before_reset = Sobol_select_itr_before_reset +
Sobol_select_itr ;
229 Sobol_select_itr = 1 ;
230 number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix =
number_of_passes_through_Sobol_matrix + 1
231 else
232 Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr + 1;
233 end
234
235 end
236
237 end
238
239 end
240
241 % Check the candidate point pair, to see if it is physically valid.
242
243 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
244 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
245 %
246 % Extract Indices
247 %
248 % EEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE
249 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
250
251 % Extract the indices for the candidate point pair, which
252 % correspond to the selected row of the Sobol matrix.
253
254 surf_1_row_Sobol = aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,1) ;
255
256 surf_1_row_ind = ceil(surf_1_row_Sobol * (rows_surf_1_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
257
258 surf_1_row_ind = int32(surf_1_row_ind) ;
259
260 surf_1_col_Sobol = aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,2) ;
261
262 surf_1_col_ind = ceil(surf_1_col_Sobol * (cols_surf_1_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
263
264 surf_1_col_ind = int32(surf_1_col_ind) ;
265
266 surf_2_row_Sobol = aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,3) ;
                                       726
267
268 surf_2_row_ind = ceil(surf_2_row_Sobol * (rows_surf_2_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
269
270 surf_2_row_ind = int32(surf_2_row_ind) ;
271
272 surf_2_col_Sobol = aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,4) ;
273
274 surf_2_col_ind = ceil(surf_2_col_Sobol * (cols_surf_2_x_mat_num - 1) ) ;
275
276 surf_2_col_ind = int32(surf_2_col_ind) ;
277
278 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
279 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
280 %
281 % Generate Quadrilaterals
282 %
283 % GGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGG
284 % QQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQQ
285
286 % Call a subroutine to obtain the pair of quadrilaterals
287 % that corresponds to the preceding indices for the
288 % candidate point pair.
289
290 [surf_1_a_vec,surf_1_b_vec,surf_1_c_vec,surf_1_d_vec, ...
291 surf_2_a_vec,surf_2_b_vec,surf_2_c_vec,surf_2_d_vec] = ...
292 quadrilateral_pairs_select(surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
293 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
294 [surf_1_row_ind,surf_1_col_ind,surf_2_row_ind,surf_2_col_ind]) ;
295
296 % Prepare and feed inputs to the differential view factor subroutine.
297
298 dA1_mat = vertcat(surf_1_a_vec,surf_1_b_vec,surf_1_c_vec,surf_1_d_vec) ;
299
300 dA2_mat = vertcat(surf_2_a_vec,surf_2_b_vec,surf_2_c_vec,surf_2_d_vec) ;
301
302 dA1_center_vec = mean(dA1_mat,1) ;
303
304 dA2_center_vec = mean(dA2_mat,1) ;
305
306 [is_point_valid, ...
307 diff_view_factor_val, ...
308 n_dA1_normal_vec,n_dA2_normal_vec, ...
309 mag_root_12] = ...
310 diff_view_factor_8(dA1_mat,dA2_mat, ...
311 surf_1_center_vec, ...
312 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_1, ...
313 surf_2_center_vec, ...
314 movement_of_ray_relative_to_center_of_surface_2) ;
315
316 % If the candidate point pair is physically valid...
317
318 if is_point_valid == 1
319
320 % Check to see if the corresponding ray intersects the
321 % obstructing surface.
322
323 % ...pass this information along to the Sobol learning
324 % system subroutine, so that the probabilities of the
                                       727
325 % adjacent points can be adjusted accordingly.
326
327 [aug_Sobol_mat] = Sobol_learning_system_3(aug_Sobol_mat,Sobol_select_itr,
is_point_valid) ;
328
329
330 if or(abs(dA2_center_vec(1,1)-dA1_center_vec(1,1))<0.1, ...
331 abs(dA2_center_vec(1,2)-dA1_center_vec(1,2))<0.1)
332
333 [intersection_mat, ...
334 ray_obstructed] = ...
335 double_check_if_ray_obstructed(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
336 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
337 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
338 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat) ;
339
340 else
341
342 [intersection_mat, ...
343 ray_obstructed] = ...
344 is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
345 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
346 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
347 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat) ;
348
349 end
350
351 if ray_obstructed == 1
352
353
354 diff_view_factor_val = 0;
355 % Find the point of obstruction that is closest to the
356 % emitting surface, surface 1.
357
358 [rows_intersection_mat,~]=size(intersection_mat) ;
359
360 % If there is only one row in the intersection point
361 % matrix...
362
363 if rows_intersection_mat == 1
364 %...make that row the intersection point vector.
365 obstruction_point_vec = intersection_mat(1,:) ;
366 % Otherwise...
367 else
368 % ...find the intersection point that is closest to
369 % surface 1, and keep that as the intersection point
370 % vector.
371
372 dist_betw_dA1_and_intersection_mat = sqrt(sum((intersection_mat -
dA1_center_vec).^2,2)) ;
373
374 min_dist_betw_dA1_and_intersection = min
(dist_betw_dA1_and_intersection_mat) ;
375
376 row_of_min_dist = find
(dist_betw_dA1_and_intersection_mat==min_dist_betw_dA1_and_intersection) ;
377
378 if max(size(row_of_min_dist)) > 1
                                       728
379 row_of_min_dist = row_of_min_dist(1,1) ;
380 else
381 end
382
383 obstruction_point_vec = intersection_mat(row_of_min_dist,:) ;
384 end
385
386 valid_point_pairs_num = valid_point_pairs_num + is_point_valid ;
387
388 is_ray_obstructed_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = ray_obstructed ;
389
390 obstruction_point_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) =
obstruction_point_vec ;
391
392 dA1_center_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = dA1_center_vec ;
393
394 dA2_center_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = dA2_center_vec ;
395
396 is_point_valid_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = is_point_valid ;
397
398 n_dA1_normal_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = n_dA1_normal_vec ;
399
400 n_dA2_normal_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = n_dA2_normal_vec ;
401
402 mag_root_12_valid_3mat(point_pair_itr,1,simulation_itr) = mag_root_12 ;
403
404 % Add the resulting output to the growing list of
405 % differential view factor contributions.
406
407 %sum_of_diff_view_factors = sum_of_diff_view_factors + diff_view_factor_val ;
408
409 dF12_vec(point_pair_itr,1) = diff_view_factor_val ;
410
411 point_pair_itr = point_pair_itr + 1 ;
412
413 htg_point_pair_selected = 1 ;
414
415 % Otherwise, if the ray is NOT obstructed...
416 else
417 obstruction_point_vec = zeros(1,3);
418
419 % Complete the current choice of point pairs without using
420 % library values to weight its choice.
421
422 aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) = -aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) ;
423
424 %[aug_Sobol_mat] = Sobol_learning_system_3(aug_Sobol_mat,Sobol_select_itr,
is_point_valid) ;
425
426 % Store the information about the center points of each
427 % differential surface, and their corresponding normals.
428
429 % Store the information about the center points of each
430 % differential surface, and their corresponding normals.
431 %
432 % NOTE: a combination of two differential surfaces that is
433 % "valid," by virtue of having a physically reasonable
434 % direction of ray propagation, may still be obstructed if
                                       729
435 % said ray is directed into the blocking surface.
436
437 valid_point_pairs_num = valid_point_pairs_num + is_point_valid ;
438
439 is_ray_obstructed_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = 0 ;
440
441 obstruction_point_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) =
obstruction_point_vec ;
442
443 dA1_center_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = dA1_center_vec ;
444
445 dA2_center_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = dA2_center_vec ;
446
447 is_point_valid_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = is_point_valid ;
448
449 n_dA1_normal_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = n_dA1_normal_vec ;
450
451 n_dA2_normal_3mat(point_pair_itr,:,simulation_itr) = n_dA2_normal_vec ;
452
453 mag_root_12_valid_3mat(point_pair_itr,1,simulation_itr) = mag_root_12 ;
454
455 % Add the resulting output to the growing list of
456 % differential view factor contributions.
457
458 %sum_of_diff_view_factors = sum_of_diff_view_factors + diff_view_factor_val ;
459
460 dF12_vec(point_pair_itr,1) = diff_view_factor_val ;
461
462 point_pair_itr = point_pair_itr + 1 ;
463
464 htg_point_pair_selected = 1 ;
465
466 end
467
468 else
469 % ...reject the (physically invalid) candidate point
470 % pair, and move on to the next point pair.
471
472 % First, reset this point pair's probability to
473 % zero, so it cannot be selected again by the
474 % routine.
475
476 aug_Sobol_mat(Sobol_select_itr,5) = 0 ;
477
478 % Second, pass this information about the candidate
479 % point pair's bogus-ness along to the Sobol learning
480 % system subroutine, so that the probabilities of the
481 % adjacent points can be adjusted accordingly.
482
483 [aug_Sobol_mat] = Sobol_learning_system_3(aug_Sobol_mat,Sobol_select_itr,
is_point_valid) ;
484
485
486 end
487
488 end
489
490 end
                                       730
491
492 is_ray_obstructed_3mat = logical(is_ray_obstructed_3mat) ;
493
494 %Sobol_select_itr = Sobol_select_itr + Sobol_select_itr_before_reset ;
495
496 time_finding_n_point_pairs = toc
497 disp( ' ')
498 end

CA6.s Augmented Sobol-set Matrix Probabilistic Weight Assigner

Filename: Sobol_learning_system_3.m


1 function [aug_Sobol_mat] =
Sobol_learning_system_3(aug_Sobol_mat,row_num,is_good)
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is to take, as input, an augmented Sobol
4 % set matrix, along with a given row index in that matrix, and whether or
5 % not that row is considered to return "good" (i.e. non-obstructed)
6 % values in a view factor context. It will then return, as output, a
7 % re-weighted version of the augmented matrix, based on that input.
8 %
9 % Input terms:
10 %
11 % aug_Sobol_mat = a matrix, where each row is structured as follows:
12 %
13 % [s1(index_num),s2(index_num),s3(index_num),s4(index_num),probability_ranking]
14 %
15 % where
16 %
17 % s1(index_number) et al.
18 % = numbers, in the (0,1) domain, from the 4-
19 % dimensional Sobol set being used to select
20 % coordinates within a view factor problem;
21 %
22 % and
23 %
24 % probability_ranking
25 % = a number, in the (0,1) domain, expressing the
26 % probability that a given row will be accepted for
27 % a Monte Carlo step in a view factor calculation.
28 %
29
30 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
31 %
32 % This routine takes and returns the revised aug_Sobol_mat
33 % format (i.e. without index numbers)
34 % being used by aug_Sobol_select_8 et al.
35
36 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
37 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
38 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
39 %
40 % Hamming Distance Calculation
41 %
42 % HHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH
                                       731
43 % DDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDDD
44 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
45
46 % Initialize the vectors for approximating distances between points in
47 % Sobol space.
48
49 dist_vec = ones( max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)), 1 ) ;
50
51 abs_delta_s1_vec = ones( max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)), 1 ) ;
52
53 abs_delta_s2_vec = ones( max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)), 1 ) ;
54
55 abs_delta_s3_vec = ones( max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)), 1 ) ;
56
57 abs_delta_s4_vec = ones( max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)), 1 ) ;
58
59 % For each row past row_num, estimate the distance between that Sobol
60 % vector and the Sobol vector at row_num.
61
62 coming_rows_vec = row_num+1:1:max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)) ;
63
64 abs_delta_s1_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) = abs ( aug_Sobol_mat(row_num,2) -
aug_Sobol_mat
(coming_rows_vec,1) ) ;
65
66 abs_delta_s2_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) = abs ( aug_Sobol_mat(row_num,3) -
aug_Sobol_mat
(coming_rows_vec,2) ) ;
67
68 abs_delta_s3_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) = abs ( aug_Sobol_mat(row_num,4) -
aug_Sobol_mat
(coming_rows_vec,3) ) ;
69
70 abs_delta_s4_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) = abs ( aug_Sobol_mat(row_num,5) -
aug_Sobol_mat
(coming_rows_vec,4) ) ;
71
72 dist_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) = 0.25 * ( abs_delta_s1_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) +
abs_delta_s2_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) + abs_delta_s3_vec(coming_rows_vec,1) +
abs_delta_s4_vec
(coming_rows_vec,1) ) ;
73
74 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
75 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
76 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
77 %
78 % Sort and Reweight
79 %
80 % SSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS
81 % AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA
82 % RRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRR
83
84 % Sort the rows past row_num in order of their increasing Sobol-set
85 % distance from row_num.
86
87 %[~,sorted_dist_ind_vec] = sort(dist_vec(coming_rows_vec,1),'ascend') ;
88
89 %sorted_dist_ind_vec = sorted_dist_ind_vec + row_num ;
                                       732
90
91 %aug_Sobol_mat(coming_rows_vec,:) = aug_Sobol_mat(sorted_dist_ind_vec,:) ;
92
93 prob_pos_reweighting_factor = 0.0025 ;
94
95 prob_neg_reweighting_factor = 0.0025 ;
96
97 % Reweight the probabilities for up to the first 48 rows past row_num.
98
99 if max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)) - row_num >= 48
100 num_reweighted_rows = 48 ;
101 else
102 if and ( (max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)) - row_num) < 48 , (max(size(aug_Sobol_mat))
- row_num)
> 0 )
103 num_reweighted_rows = max(size(aug_Sobol_mat)) - row_num ;
104 else
105 num_reweighted_rows = 0 ;
106 end
107 end
108
109 % If the number of reweighted rows is greater than zero....
110
111 if num_reweighted_rows > 0
112 % ...find the (number of reweighted rows) smallest distances between
113 % the point pair at row_num and the other point pairs in the coming
114 % rows.
115
116 [~,min_dist_ind_vec] = mink(dist_vec(coming_rows_vec,1),num_reweighted_rows) ;
117
118 for reweight_probs_itr = 1:1:num_reweighted_rows
119 if is_good == 1
120 % Increase the probability ranking by some percent of the distance
121 % between itself and 1.
122 aug_Sobol_mat(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec(reweight_probs_itr),5) = aug_Sobol_mat
(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec(reweight_probs_itr),5) + ((1-
aug_Sobol_mat(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec
(reweight_probs_itr),5))*prob_pos_reweighting_factor) ;
123 else
124 % Decrease the probability ranking by some percent of the distance
125 % between itself and 0.
126 aug_Sobol_mat(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec(reweight_probs_itr),5) = aug_Sobol_mat
(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec(reweight_probs_itr),5) -
(aug_Sobol_mat(row_num+min_dist_ind_vec
(reweight_probs_itr),5)*prob_neg_reweighting_factor) ;
127 end
128 end
129
130 else
131 end
132
133 end
134

CA6.t Check if Ray is Obstructed by a Surface

Filename: is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4.m


1 function [intersection_mat, ...
2 ray_obstructed] = ...
3 is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
4 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
5 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
6 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat)
7 %
8 % This function takes, as input, the coordinates of two points that
9 % define a line segment (i.e. ray), along with three meshgrids that
10 % define a surface. It then returns, as output, the truth value of
11 % whether or not the ray intersects--that is, is obstructed by--the
12 % surface. In addition, it returns the location of the point where the
13 % line intersects the obstructing surface.
14 %
15 % Usage:
16 %
17 % [intersection_mat,...
18 % ray_obstructed] =...
19 % is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec,...
20 % surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
21 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
22 % obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat);
23
24 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
25 %
26 % This routine makes use of the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
27 %
28 % validate_is_ray_obstructed_by_surface
29 % make_and_expand_truth_matrix
30 % scan_meshgrids_for_intersection
31
32 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
33 %
34 % Validation
35 %
36 % VVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVVV
37
38 % Validate the input data being used by this routine.
39
40 [dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
41 ~,~,~, ...
42 ~,~,~, ...
43 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat] = ...
44 validate_is_ray_obstructed_by_surface(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
45 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
46 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
47 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat);
48
49 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
50 % BBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBB
51 %
52 % Coordinate Bounds
                                       734
53 %
54 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
55 % BBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBBB
56
57 % Construct the Cartesian coordinates bounding box that
58 % encompasses the entire extent of the associated ray.
59
60 dA1_dA2_mat = vertcat(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec) ;
61
62 ray_bounding_box_x_min = min(dA1_dA2_mat(:,1),[],1) ;
63
64 ray_bounding_box_x_max = max(dA1_dA2_mat(:,1),[],1) ;
65
66 ray_bounding_box_y_min = min(dA1_dA2_mat(:,2),[],1) ;
67
68 ray_bounding_box_y_max = max(dA1_dA2_mat(:,2),[],1) ;
69
70 ray_bounding_box_z_min = min(dA1_dA2_mat(:,3),[],1) ;
71
72 ray_bounding_box_z_max = max(dA1_dA2_mat(:,3),[],1) ;
73
74 % Construct the Cartesian coordinates bounding box that encompasses the
75 % entire extent of the obstructing surface.
76
77 obs_surf_bounding_box_x_min = min(min(obs_surf_x_mat)) ;
78
79 obs_surf_bounding_box_x_max = max(max(obs_surf_x_mat)) ;
80
81 obs_surf_bounding_box_y_min = min(min(obs_surf_y_mat)) ;
82
83 obs_surf_bounding_box_y_max = max(max(obs_surf_y_mat)) ;
84
85 obs_surf_bounding_box_z_min = min(min(obs_surf_z_mat)) ;
86
87 obs_surf_bounding_box_z_max = max(max(obs_surf_z_mat)) ;
88
89 % Make notes of how far apart these bounding box limits originally are.
90
91 old_x_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_x_min - obs_surf_bounding_box_x_min) ;
92
93 old_x_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_x_max - obs_surf_bounding_box_x_max) ;
94
95 old_y_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_y_min - obs_surf_bounding_box_y_min) ;
96
97 old_y_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_y_max - obs_surf_bounding_box_y_max) ;
98
99 old_z_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_z_min - obs_surf_bounding_box_z_min) ;
100
101 old_z_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_z_max - obs_surf_bounding_box_z_max) ;
102
103 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
104 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
105 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
106 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
107 %
108 % Preliminary, Coarse Intersection Check
109 %
110 % PPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP
                                       735
111 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
112 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
113 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
114
115 tol = 1e-14 ;
116
117 % Check to see whether or not the ray crosses near or through the
118 % obstructing volume at any region within the latter's entire 3D coordinate
119 % range.
120
121 % If there is such an overlap--that is...
122
123 % ...if the x coordinates overlap...
124
125 if and(ray_bounding_box_x_max>=obs_surf_bounding_box_x_min, ...
126 ray_bounding_box_x_min<=obs_surf_bounding_box_x_max)
127
128 % ... and the y coordinates overlap...
129
130 if and(ray_bounding_box_y_max>=obs_surf_bounding_box_y_min, ...
131 ray_bounding_box_y_min<=obs_surf_bounding_box_y_max)
132
133 % ....and the z coordinates overlap...
134
135 if and(ray_bounding_box_z_max>=obs_surf_bounding_box_z_min, ...
136 ray_bounding_box_z_min<=obs_surf_bounding_box_z_max)
137
138 % ...the ray may be obstructed by the surface, and more checks need to be
139 % done to determine if this occurs.
140
141 %disp(' ')
142 %disp('Ray may be obstructed.')
143 %disp('Doing further tests to check...')
144
145 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
146 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
147 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
148 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
149 %
150 % Main, Fine Intersection Check
151 %
152 % MMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMMM
153 % FFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF
154 % IIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII
155 % CCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCCC
156
157 % There are some general possibilities that need to be checked
158 % here, which are as follows.
159 %
160 % INTERSECTION OF LINE WITH SURFACE
161 %
162 % 1) There are points on the obstructing surface that are
163 % contained within the bounding box of the ray, such that
164 % the ray goes through the surface.
165 %
166 % 2) The bounding box of the ray is contained within /
167 % surrounded by points on the obstructing surface;
168 % however, there are no points on the surface that lie
                                       736
169 % within the ray's bounding box itself.
170 %
171 % NON-INTERSECTION OF LINE AND SURFACE
172 %
173 % 3) There are points on the obstructing surface that are
174 % contained within the bounding box of the ray, but the
175 % ray does not travel through the surface.
176 %
177 % 4) There are no surface points within the bounding box of
178 % the ray, because the ray does not intersect the surface
179 % anywhere.
180
181 % These cases can be reduced to cases 1) and 3) by simply
182 % expanding the ray's bounding box every time no surface points
183 % are found within it. This box will then expand until either:
184 %
185 % a) it begins to contain some points from the surface: or
186 %
187 % b) it expands to fill the entire (x,y,z) domain available,
188 % without encompassing any points from the surface.
189
190 % spwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbb
191 %
192 % --surface points within ray bounding box--
193 %
194 % spwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbbspwrbb
195
196 % Determine what, if any, meshgrid indices are contained within
197 % the bounding box coordinates of the ray.
198
199 solution_found = 0 ;
200
201 %pass_number = 1 ;
202
203 while solution_found == 0
204
205 % First, check for overlap in the x coordinates.
206
207 [x_overlap_row_ind,x_overlap_col_ind] = find(and
(obs_surf_x_mat<=ray_bounding_box_x_max,obs_surf_x_mat>=ray_bounding_box_x_min)) ;
208
209 % If there is overlap in the x coordinates...
210
211 if isempty(x_overlap_row_ind) == 0
212
213 %disp('x coordinates overlap')
214
215 x_overlap_ind_mat = horzcat(x_overlap_row_ind,x_overlap_col_ind) ;
216
217 % ...check for overlap in the y coordinates.
218
219 [y_overlap_row_ind,y_overlap_col_ind] = find(and
(obs_surf_y_mat<=ray_bounding_box_y_max,obs_surf_y_mat>=ray_bounding_box_y_min)) ;
220
221 % If there is overlap in the y coordinates...
222
223 if isempty(y_overlap_row_ind) == 0
224
                                       737
225 %disp('y coordinates overlap')
226
227 y_overlap_ind_mat = horzcat(y_overlap_row_ind,y_overlap_col_ind) ;
228
229 % ...check for overlap in the z coordinates.
230
231 [z_overlap_row_ind,z_overlap_col_ind] = find(and
(obs_surf_z_mat<=ray_bounding_box_z_max,obs_surf_z_mat>=ray_bounding_box_z_min)) ;
232
233 % If there is overlap in the z coordinates...
234
235 if isempty(z_overlap_row_ind) == 0
236
237 %disp('z coordinates overlap')
238
239 z_overlap_ind_mat = horzcat(z_overlap_row_ind,z_overlap_col_ind);
240
241 % ...then there must be points from the surface
242 % that reside within the bounding box of the
243 % ray. As such, this ray will either intersect
244 % the surface (case 1) or barely miss the
245 % surface (case 3).
246
247 % Scan across these points on the meshgrid
248 % surface to check if and where an intersection
249 % occurs.
250
251 % Find the indices in the meshgrids where
252 % overlap occurs.
253
254 xy_overlap_ind_mat = intersect(x_overlap_ind_mat,
y_overlap_ind_mat, 'rows');
255
256 xyz_overlap_ind_mat = intersect(xy_overlap_ind_mat,
z_overlap_ind_mat, 'rows');
257
258 % At this point, the routine may or may not
259 % find that there are values on the surface
260 % that are overlapped by the ray's bounding
261 % box.
262 %
263 % If there are such points, a truth matrix
264 % should be made, and the corresponding
265 % meshgrid values should be inspected for
266 % intersections. The location of any such
267 % intersections--or, conversely, establishing
268 % that such intersections are absent-- means
269 % the search has ended.
270 %
271 % If there are points on the obstructing
272 % surface that are partially, but not totally,
273 % overlapped by the bounding box, then the ray
274 % must be skew to the obstructing surface.
275
276 if min(size(xyz_overlap_ind_mat)) > 1
277
278 % Make and expand a truth matrix corresponding
279 % to these (row,column) locations in the
                                       738
280 % meshgrids.
281
282 [obs_truth_mat] = make_and_expand_truth_matrix
(xyz_overlap_ind_mat,obs_surf_x_mat) ;
283
284 % Scan over the corresponding locations in the
285 % meshgrids to locate any intersections that
286 % occur between the obstructing surface and the
287 % ray.
288
289 [uppy_intersection_mat,downy_intersection_mat] =
scan_meshgrids_for_intersection(obs_truth_mat, ...
290 dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
291 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat);
292
293 uppy_downy_mat = vertcat(uppy_intersection_mat,
downy_intersection_mat) ;
294
295 intersection_mat = uniquetol(uppy_downy_mat,1e-14, 'ByRows',
true) ;
296
297 if ~isempty(intersection_mat)
298 ray_obstructed = 1 ;
299 else
300 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
301 end
302
303 solution_found = 1 ;
304
305 else
306
307 solution_found = 1 ;
308 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
309
310 intersection_mat = [] ;
311 end
312
313 % Otherwise...
314 else
315 % ...the bounding box of the ray does not cover
316 % multiple z locations on the surface.
317
318 z_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_z_min -
obs_surf_bounding_box_z_min ) ;
319
320 z_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_z_max -
obs_surf_bounding_box_z_max ) ;
321
322 % If the z-domain of the bounding box can be
323 % expanded...
324
325 if or( z_min_diff>tol, z_max_diff>tol )
326 % ...expand it, and allow the execution of
327 % the loop to continue.
328
329 % More specifically, if it is at all
330 % possible to expand the minimum z-value of
331 % the ray bounding box...
                                       739
332
333 if z_min_diff>tol
334 % ...expand this minimum limit toward
335 % the boundaries of the obstructing
336 % surface's minimum z extent.
337
338 ray_bounding_box_z_min = ray_bounding_box_z_min - (0.1
*old_z_min_diff) ;
339
340 % Otherwise...
341 else
342 % ...leave this minimum z limit of the ray's
343 % bounding box unchanged.
344 end
345
346 % Likewise, if it is at all
347 % possible to expand the maximum z-value of
348 % the ray bounding box...
349
350 if z_max_diff>tol
351 % ...expand this maximum limit toward
352 % the boundaries of the obstructing
353 % surface's maximum z extent.
354
355 ray_bounding_box_z_max = ray_bounding_box_z_max + (0.1
*old_z_max_diff) ;
356
357 % Otherwise...
358 else
359 % ...leave this maximum z limit of the ray's
360 % bounding box unchanged.
361 end
362
363 else
364 % Otherwise, make a note that the maximum
365 % extent of the z-domain has been reached.
366 % No intersections of the ray with the obstucting
367 % surface are possible at this point, so
368 % terminate the loop's execution.
369
370 disp( ' ')
371 disp( 'Maximum z-extent of the ray bounding box has been
reached.' )
372
373 solution_found = 1 ;
374
375 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
376
377 intersection_mat = [] ;
378
379 end
380
381 end
382 % Otherwise...
383 else
384 % ...the bounding box of the ray does not cover
385 % multiple y locations on the surface.
386
                                       740
387 y_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_y_min -
obs_surf_bounding_box_y_min ) ;
388
389 y_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_y_max -
obs_surf_bounding_box_y_max ) ;
390
391 % If the y-domain of the bounding box can be
392 % expanded...
393
394 if or( y_min_diff>tol, y_max_diff>tol )
395 % ...expand it, and allow the execution of
396 % the loop to continue.
397
398 % More specifically, if it is at all
399 % possible to expand the minimum y-value of
400 % the ray bounding box...
401
402 if y_min_diff>tol
403 % ...expand this minimum limit toward
404 % the boundaries of the obstructing
405 % surface's minimum y extent.
406
407 ray_bounding_box_y_min = ray_bounding_box_y_min - (0.1
*old_y_min_diff) ;
408
409 % Otherwise...
410 else
411 % ...leave this minimum y limit of the ray's
412 % bounding box unchanged.
413 end
414
415 % Likewise, if it is at all
416 % possible to expand the maximum y-value of
417 % the ray bounding box...
418
419 if y_max_diff>tol
420 % ...expand this maximum limit toward
421 % the boundaries of the obstructing
422 % surface's maximum y extent.
423
424 ray_bounding_box_y_max = ray_bounding_box_y_max + (0.1
*old_y_max_diff) ;
425
426 % Otherwise...
427 else
428 % ...leave this maximum y limit of the ray's
429 % bounding box unchanged.
430 end
431 else
432
433 % Otherwise, make a note that the maximum
434 % extent of the y-domain has been reached.
435 % No intersections of the ray with the obstucting
436 % surface are possible at this point, so
437 % terminate the loop's execution.
438
439 disp( ' ')
440 disp( 'Maximum y-extent of the ray bounding box has been
                                       741
reached.' )
441
442 solution_found = 1 ;
443
444 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
445
446 intersection_mat = [] ;
447
448 end
449
450 end
451
452 % Otherwise...
453 else
454 % The bounding box of the ray does not cover multiple x
455 % locations on the surface.
456
457 x_min_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_x_min - obs_surf_bounding_box_x_min
) ;
458
459 x_max_diff = abs( ray_bounding_box_x_max - obs_surf_bounding_box_x_max
) ;
460
461 % If the x-domain of the bounding box can be
462 % expanded...
463
464 if or( x_min_diff>tol, x_max_diff>tol )
465 % ...expand it, and allow the execution of
466 % the loop to continue.
467
468 % More specifically, if it is at all
469 % possible to expand the minimum x-value of
470 % the ray bounding box...
471
472 if x_min_diff>tol
473 % ...expand this minimum limit toward
474 % the boundaries of the obstructing
475 % surface's minimum x extent.
476
477 ray_bounding_box_x_min = ray_bounding_box_x_min - (0.1
*old_x_min_diff) ;
478
479 % Otherwise...
480 else
481 % ...leave this minimum x limit of the ray's
482 % bounding box unchanged.
483 end
484
485 % Likewise, if it is at all
486 % possible to expand the maximum x-value of
487 % the ray bounding box...
488
489 if x_max_diff>tol
490 % ...expand this maximum limit toward
491 % the boundaries of the obstructing
492 % surface's maximum x extent.
493
494 ray_bounding_box_x_max = ray_bounding_box_x_max + (0.1
                                       742
*old_x_max_diff) ;
495
496 % Otherwise...
497 else
498 % ...leave this maximum x limit of the ray's
499 % bounding box unchanged.
500 end
501
502 else
503
504 % Otherwise, make a note that the maximum
505 % extent of the x-domain has been reached.
506 % No intersections of the ray with the obstucting
507 % surface are possible at this point, so
508 % terminate the loop's execution.
509
510 disp( ' ')
511 disp( 'Maximum x-extent of the ray bounding box has been reached.' )
512
513 solution_found = 1 ;
514
515 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
516
517 intersection_mat = [] ;
518
519 end
520 end
521
522 end
523
524 else
525 % ...there is no z overlap. The ray categorically cannot
526 % overlap the obstructing volume, and no further checks need to
527 % be done.
528
529 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
530
531 intersection_mat = [] ;
532
533 end
534
535 else
536 % ...there is no y overlap. The ray categorically cannot overlap
537 % the obstructing volume, and no further checks need to be done.
538
539 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
540
541 intersection_mat = [] ;
542
543 end
544
545 else
546 % ...there is no x overlap. the ray categorically cannot overlap the
547 % obstructing volume, and no further checks need to be done.
548
549 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
550
551 intersection_mat = [] ;
                                       743
552
553 end
554
555 end

CA6.v Make and Expand Truth Matrix

Filename: make_and_expand_truth_matrix.m


1 function [obs_truth_mat] =
make_and_expand_truth_matrix(xyz_overlap_ind_mat,obs_surf_x_mat)
2 %
3 % The purpose of this function is twofold.
4 %
5 % First, it takes the n-by-2
6 % matrix of (row,column) values, describing points on an obstructing
7 % surface, that are overlapped by the bounding box of an intersecting
8 % ray. It then constructs a meshgrid-sized truth matrix, with "1"s
9 % entered at the locations of the overlapping points, and zeros
10 % everywhere else.
11 %
12 % Second, it takes this truth matrix and "expands" it, by ensuring that
13 % all these truth-value points are surrounded on all sides by one
14 % additional point.
15 %
16 % Usage:
17 % [obs_truth_mat] =
make_and_expand_truth_matrix(xyz_overlap_ind_mat,obs_surf_x_mat)
18 %
19 % Use this information to construct a truth
20 % matrix, where each location in the meshgrid
21 % that is overlapped by the ray bounding box is
22 % 1, and every other location is 0.
23
24 obs_truth_mat = zeros(size(obs_surf_x_mat)) ;
25
26 [obs_mat_row_num,obs_mat_col_num] = size(obs_surf_x_mat) ;
27
28 for overlap_itr = 1:1:max(size(xyz_overlap_ind_mat))
29 size_obs_truth_mat = size(obs_truth_mat) ;
30 size_xyz_overlap_ind_mat = size(xyz_overlap_ind_mat) ;
31 %overlap_itr
32
obs_truth_mat(xyz_overlap_ind_mat(overlap_itr,1),xyz_overlap_ind_mat(overlap_itr,2
)) = 1
;
33 end
34
35 % Fill in the blank spaces around the "overlap"
36 % truth values, to ensure that any ray at the
37 % boundary will be properly detected in the
38 % subsequent "line intersection" steps.
39
40 [obs_truth_mat_row_num,obs_truth_mat_col_num] = size(obs_truth_mat) ;
41
42 for i = 1:1
43
44 % Construct the four difference matrices--two
45 % rectilinear, two diagonal--needed to detect
46 % the edges of the overlapping points domain
47 % within the matrix.
                                       749
48
49 horz_diff_mat = diff(obs_truth_mat,1,2) ;
50
51 vert_diff_mat = diff(obs_truth_mat,1,1) ;
52
53 diag_diff_LL_minus_UR_mat = conv2(obs_truth_mat,[0,1;-1,0], 'valid') ;
54
55 diag_diff_LR_minus_UL_mat = conv2(obs_truth_mat,[1,0;0,-1], 'valid') ;
56
57 % Put a 6 to the left of every 1 without a
58 % left-hand neighbor.
59
60 six_pre_mat = horz_diff_mat ;
61
62 six_pre_mat(six_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
63
64 six_pre_mat = horzcat(six_pre_mat,zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num,1)) ;
65
66 six_mat = 6.* six_pre_mat ;
67
68 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + six_mat ;
69
70 % Put a 2 to the right of every 1 without a
71 % right-hand neighbor.
72
73 two_pre_mat = -horz_diff_mat ;
74
75 two_pre_mat(two_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
76
77 two_pre_mat = horzcat(zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num,1),two_pre_mat) ;
78
79 two_mat = 2.* two_pre_mat ;
80
81 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + two_mat ;
82
83 % Put a 4 directly above every 1 without an
84 % neighbor above it.
85
86 four_pre_mat = vert_diff_mat ;
87
88 four_pre_mat(four_pre_mat<0) = 0;
89
90 four_pre_mat = vertcat(four_pre_mat,zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num)) ;
91
92 four_mat = 4 .* four_pre_mat ;
93
94 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + four_mat ;
95
96 % Put an 8 directly below every 1 without an
97 % neighbor below it.
98
99 eight_pre_mat = -1 .* vert_diff_mat ;
100
101 eight_pre_mat(eight_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
102
103 eight_pre_mat = vertcat(zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num),eight_pre_mat) ;
104
105 eight_mat = 8.* eight_pre_mat ;
                                       750
106
107 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + eight_mat ;
108
109 % Put a 3 diagonally above and to the right of
110 % every 1 without a neighbor there.
111
112 three_pre_mat = diag_diff_LL_minus_UR_mat ;
113
114 three_pre_mat(three_pre_mat < 0) = 0 ;
115
116 three_pre_mat = horzcat(zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num-1,1),three_pre_mat) ;
117
118 three_pre_mat = vertcat(three_pre_mat,zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num)) ;
119
120 three_mat = 3 .* three_pre_mat ;
121
122 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + three_mat ;
123
124 % Put a 7 diagonally down and to the left of
125 % every 1 without a neighbor there.
126
127 seven_pre_mat = -diag_diff_LL_minus_UR_mat ;
128
129 seven_pre_mat(seven_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
130
131 seven_pre_mat = horzcat(seven_pre_mat,zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num-1,1)) ;
132
133 seven_pre_mat = vertcat(zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num),seven_pre_mat) ;
134
135 seven_mat = 7 .* seven_pre_mat ;
136
137 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + seven_mat ;
138
139 % Put a 5 diagonally up and to the left of
140 % every 1 without a neighbor there.
141
142 five_pre_mat = diag_diff_LR_minus_UL_mat ;
143
144 five_pre_mat(five_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
145
146 five_pre_mat = horzcat(five_pre_mat,zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num-1,1)) ;
147
148 five_pre_mat = vertcat(five_pre_mat,zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num)) ;
149
150 five_mat = 5 .* five_pre_mat ;
151
152 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + five_mat ;
153
154 % Put a 9 diagonally down and to the right of
155 % every 1 without a neighbor there.
156
157 nine_pre_mat = -diag_diff_LR_minus_UL_mat ;
158
159 nine_pre_mat(nine_pre_mat<0) = 0 ;
160
161 nine_pre_mat = horzcat(zeros(obs_truth_mat_row_num-1,1),nine_pre_mat) ;
162
163 nine_pre_mat = vertcat(zeros(1,obs_truth_mat_col_num),nine_pre_mat) ;
                                       751
164
165 nine_mat = 9 .* nine_pre_mat ;
166
167 obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat + nine_mat ;
168
169 end
170
171 % Reset all nonzero values in the truth matrix
172 % to 1.
173
174 obs_truth_mat(obs_truth_mat>1) = 1 ;
175
176 obs_truth_mat = logical(obs_truth_mat) ;
177
178 spy(obs_truth_mat)
179
180 %obs_truth_mat = obs_truth_mat
181
182 end
183




CA6.w Scan Meshgrids for Intersection

Filename: scan_meshgrids_for_intersection.m


1 function [uppy_intersection_mat,downy_intersection_mat] =
scan_meshgrids_for_intersection
(obs_truth_mat, ...
2 dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
3 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat)
4 %
5 %
6 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
7 %
8 % This routine makes use of the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
9 %
10 % line_intersects_plane
11 %
12 % Usage
13 %
14 % function [uppy_intersection_mat,downy_intersection_mat] =
scan_meshgrids_for_intersection
(obs_truth_mat,...
15 % dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec,...
16 % obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat)
17 %
18
19 uppy_intersection_mat = [] ;
20
21 downy_intersection_mat = [] ;
22
23 % Unite the two differential surface center points into a line matrix.
24
25 line_mat = vertcat(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec) ;
                                        752
26
27 % Make a note of which rows in the truth matrix are occupied by
28 % points that overlap between the surface and the ray's bounding box.
29
30 row_occupied_vec = sum(obs_truth_mat,2) ;
31
32 row_occupied_vec = find(row_occupied_vec>0) ;
33
34 row_occupied_vec = row_occupied_vec' ;
35
36 % For each one of these rows...
37
38 row_occupied_vec_row_num = max(size(row_occupied_vec)) ;
39
40 for row_itr = 1:1:row_occupied_vec_row_num - 1
41
42 % Extract the row indices to be scanned over.
43
44 %row_itr = row_itr
45
46 new_obs_mat_row = row_occupied_vec(1,row_itr) ;
47
48 % Make a note of which column locations are occupied.
49
50 occupied_columns_in_this_row_vec = find(obs_truth_mat(new_obs_mat_row,:)>0);
51
52 % Make a note of the occupied column locations in the next row down.
53
54 occupied_columns_in_next_row_vec = find(obs_truth_mat(new_obs_mat_row+1,:)>0);
55
56 % Iterate over the column locations of whichever row has fewer occupied
57 % columns.
58
59 if max(size(occupied_columns_in_this_row_vec)) <= max(size
(occupied_columns_in_next_row_vec))
60 fewest_occupied_cols_num = max(size(occupied_columns_in_this_row_vec)) ;
61 occupied_columns_to_scan_over_vec = occupied_columns_in_this_row_vec ;
62 else
63 fewest_occupied_cols_num = max(size(occupied_columns_in_next_row_vec)) ;
64 occupied_columns_to_scan_over_vec = occupied_columns_in_next_row_vec ;
65 end
66
67 for col_itr = 1:1:fewest_occupied_cols_num - 1
68
69 % Extract the column indices to be scanned over.
70
71 new_obs_mat_col = occupied_columns_to_scan_over_vec(1,col_itr) ;
72
73 % The (row,column) indices describe a net of quadrilaterals. Since
74 % each quadrilateral can be thought of as consisting of two
75 % triangular halves, the scan will involve two parts: one
76 % for the "uppy" triangles, and one for the "downy" triangles.
77
78 % Extract the point for (row,col).
79
80 x_c = obs_surf_x_mat(new_obs_mat_row,new_obs_mat_col) ;
81
82 y_c = obs_surf_y_mat(new_obs_mat_row,new_obs_mat_col) ;
                                       753
83
84 z_c = obs_surf_z_mat(new_obs_mat_row,new_obs_mat_col) ;
85
86 c_vec = [x_c,y_c,z_c] ;
87
88 % Extract the point for (row,col+1).
89
90 x_b = obs_surf_x_mat(new_obs_mat_row, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
91
92 y_b = obs_surf_y_mat(new_obs_mat_row, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
93
94 z_b = obs_surf_z_mat(new_obs_mat_row, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
95
96 b_vec = [x_b,y_b,z_b] ;
97
98 % Extract the point for (row+1,col).
99
100 x_d = obs_surf_x_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col ) ;
101
102 y_d = obs_surf_y_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col ) ;
103
104 z_d = obs_surf_z_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col ) ;
105
106 d_vec = [x_d,y_d,z_d] ;
107
108 % Extract the point for (row+1,col+1).
109
110 x_a = obs_surf_x_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
111
112 y_a = obs_surf_y_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
113
114 z_a = obs_surf_z_mat(new_obs_mat_row + 1, new_obs_mat_col + 1 ) ;
115
116 a_vec = [x_a,y_a,z_a] ;
117
118 % Feed the uppy triangle points to the
119 % line_intersects_plane subroutine.
120
121 uppy_plane_mat = vertcat(c_vec,b_vec,d_vec) ;
122
123 [~, ...
124 ~, ...
125 intersection_point_vec, ...
126 line_intersects_triangle] = ...
127 line_intersects_plane(line_mat,uppy_plane_mat);
128
129 % Store the results if an intersection between the ray and the uppy
130 % triangle is observed.
131
132 if line_intersects_triangle == 1
133 uppy_intersection_mat = vertcat(uppy_intersection_mat,intersection_point_vec)
;
134 else
135 end
136
137 % Feed the downy triangle points to the
138 % line_intersects_plane subroutine.
139
                                       754
140 downy_plane_mat = vertcat(a_vec,b_vec,d_vec) ;
141
142 [~, ...
143 ~, ...
144 intersection_point_vec, ...
145 line_intersects_triangle] = ...
146 line_intersects_plane(line_mat,downy_plane_mat);
147
148 % Store the results if an intersection between the ray and the
149 % downy triangle is observed.
150
151 if line_intersects_triangle == 1
152 downy_intersection_mat =
vertcat(downy_intersection_mat,intersection_point_vec) ;
153 else
154 end
155
156 end
157
158 end
159
160 end
CA6.x Find Intersection of Two Lines

Filename: line_line_intersection.m


1 function [x,y] = line_line_intersection(x1,y1,x2,y2,x3,y3,x4,y4)
2 %
3 % This function implements the line-line intersection equations given in
4 % Weisstein, Eric W. "Line-Line Intersection."
5 % From MathWorld--A Wolfram Web Resource.
6 % https://mathworld.wolfram.com/Line-LineIntersection.html
7 %
8 % More specifically, this function deals with two coplanar lines I and
9 % II. It takes, as input, the coordinates of two points
10 % 1 and 2 that lie on line I, and two points 3 and 4 that lie on line
11 % II. It then returns the (x,y) coordinates of the point where lines I
12 % and II cross one another.
13 %
14 % Usage:
15 %
16 % [x,y] = line_line_intersection(x1,y1,x2,y2,x3,y3,x4,y4)
17
18 x = det([det([x1 y1;x2 y2]), (x1-x2);det([x3 y3;x4 y4]), (x3-x4) ])./det([(x1-
x2),(y1-y2) ;
(x3-x4),(y3-y4)]);
19 y = det([det([x1 y1;x2 y2]), (y1-y2);det([x3 y3;x4 y4]), (y3-y4) ])./det([(x1-
x2),(y1-y2) ;
(x3-x4),(y3-y4)]);
20
21 end




                                       755
CA6.y Rotation Checks for Obstructed Rays

Filename: double_check_if_ray_obstructed.m

1 function [intersection_mat, ...
2 ray_obstructed] = ...
3 double_check_if_ray_obstructed(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
4 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
5 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
6 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat)
7 %
8 % Usage
9 %
10 % [intersection_mat,...
11 % ray_obstructed] =...
12 % double_check_if_ray_obstructed(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec,...
13 % surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat,...
14 % surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat,...
15 % obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat)
16 %
17 % PROGRAMMING NOTES
18 %
19 % This routine makes use of the following non-MATLAB subroutines:
20 %
21 % is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4
22
23 % Do an initial check on whether or not a specified ray is obstructed, when
24 % it moves between two surfaces that have an interspersed obstructing
25 % object.
26
27 [initial_intersection_mat, ...
28 initial_ray_obstructed] = ...
29 is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4(dA1_center_vec,dA2_center_vec, ...
30 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
31 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
32 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat) ;
33
34 % Rotate the ray through an angle of pi/4 in the xy-plane of the current
35 % Cartesian coordinate system, while leaving everything else in the same
36 % positions as before.
37
38 theta_pivot = pi/4 ;
39
40 rotation_mat = [cos(theta_pivot), -sin(theta_pivot), 0; ...
41 sin(theta_pivot), cos(theta_pivot), 0; ...
42 0, 0, 1 ] ;
43
44 final_dA1_center_vec = rotation_mat * dA1_center_vec' ;
45
46 final_dA1_center_vec = final_dA1_center_vec' ;
47
48 final_dA2_center_vec = rotation_mat * dA2_center_vec' ;
49
50 final_dA2_center_vec = final_dA2_center_vec' ;
51
52 % Do an second check on whether or not this new, "final ray" is obstructed,

                                       756
53 % when it moves between the same two surfaces that have the same
54 % interspersed obstructing object.
55
56 [final_intersection_mat, ...
57 final_ray_obstructed] = ...
58 is_ray_obstructed_by_surface_4(final_dA1_center_vec,final_dA2_center_vec, ...
59 surf_1_x_mat,surf_1_y_mat,surf_1_z_mat, ...
60 surf_2_x_mat,surf_2_y_mat,surf_2_z_mat, ...
61 obs_surf_x_mat,obs_surf_y_mat,obs_surf_z_mat) ;
62
63 un_rotation_mat = [ cos(-theta_pivot), -sin(-theta_pivot), 0; ...
64 sin(-theta_pivot), cos(-theta_pivot), 0; ...
65 0, 0, 1 ] ;
66
67 % Compare the results from these two runs.
68
69 %size_initial_intersection_mat = size(initial_intersection_mat)
70
71 % If the "initial ray" is obstructed...
72 if initial_ray_obstructed == 1
73 % ...check on the status of the "final ray."
74
75 % If both the initial and final ray are obstructed...
76 if and(initial_ray_obstructed==1,final_ray_obstructed==1)
77 % ...it follows that the ray is categorically obstructed, and
78 % should thus be reported as an obstructed ray.
79
80 % Compare the intersection points: keep the one that is closest to
81 % the emitting surface (i.e. surface 1).
82
83 initial_dist = sqrt(sum((initial_intersection_mat-dA1_center_vec).^2)) ;
84
85 final_dist = sqrt(sum((final_intersection_mat-final_dA1_center_vec).^2)) ;
86
87
88 if initial_dist < final_dist
89 intersection_mat = initial_intersection_mat ;
90 else
91 intersection_mat = un_rotation_mat*final_intersection_mat' ;
92
93 intersection_mat = intersection_mat' ;
94
95 end
96
97 %intersection_mat = initial_intersection_mat ;
98
99 ray_obstructed = 1 ;
100
101 % Otherwise...
102 else
103 % ...if the initial ray is obstructed, but the final ray is NOT
104 % obstructed, it follows that the original assignment was correct,
105 % and the ray should be reported as an obstructed ray.
106
107 intersection_mat = initial_intersection_mat ;
108
109 ray_obstructed = 1 ;
110
                                       757
111 end
112
113 % Otherwise, if the "initial ray" is NOT obstructed...
114 else
115 % ...check on the status of the "final ray."
116
117
118 % If both the initial and final ray are NOT obstructed...
119 if and(initial_ray_obstructed==0,final_ray_obstructed==0)
120 % ...it follows that the ray is categorically NOT obstructed, and
121 % should thus be reported as a NOT-obstructed ray.
122
123 intersection_mat = initial_intersection_mat ;
124
125 ray_obstructed = 0 ;
126
127 % Otherwise...
128 else
129 % ...if the initial ray is NOT obstructed, but the final ray is
130 % obstructed, it follows that the final assignment was correct,
131 % and the ray should be reported as an obstructed ray.
132
133 intersection_mat = un_rotation_mat*final_intersection_mat' ;
134
135 intersection_mat = intersection_mat' ;
136
137 ray_obstructed = 1 ;
138
139 end
140
141 end
142
143 end

CA6.z Cross Product Calculator

Filename: cross_product.m


1 function [ a_cross_b_vec ] = cross_product( a_vec,b_vec )
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [ a_cross_b_vec ] = cross_product( a_vec,b_vec )
6 % The purpose of this function is to take the cross product of two
7 % vectors in Cartesian coordinates.
8
9 a_cross_b_delta_x = ( a_vec(1,2) * b_vec(1,3) ) - ( a_vec(1,3) * b_vec(1,2) ) ;
10
11 a_cross_b_delta_y = ( a_vec(1,3) * b_vec(1,1) ) - ( a_vec(1,1) * b_vec(1,3) ) ;
12
13 a_cross_b_delta_z = ( a_vec(1,1) * b_vec(1,2) ) - ( a_vec(1,2) * b_vec(1,1) ) ;
14
15 a_cross_b_vec = [a_cross_b_delta_x,a_cross_b_delta_y,a_cross_b_delta_z];
16
17 end
18

CA6.aa Dot Product Calculator

Filename: dot_product.m

1 function [a_dot_b] = dot_product(a_vec,b_vec)
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 % [a_dot_b] = dot_product(a_vec,b_vec)
5 %

7
8 a_dot_b = sum(vector_prod) ;

CA6.bb Find Where a Line Intersects a Plane

Filename: line_intersects_plane.m


1 function [does_line_intersect_plane, ...
2 does_line_coincide_with_plane, ...
3 intersection_point_vec, ...
4 line_intersects_triangle] = ...
5 line_intersects_plane(line_mat,plane_mat)
6 %
7 % Consider a line specified by two points, and a plane specified by 3
8 % points. Given this information, determine how and where the line
9 % intersects the plane.
10 %
11 % Input terms:
12 %
13 % line_mat = a 2-row by 3-column vector, where each row represents one
14 % of the two points that define the line in 3D Cartesian
15 % coordinates, and gives them in (x,y,z) format.
16 %
17 %
18 % plane_mat = a 3-row by 3-column vector, where each row represents one
19 % of the three points that define the plane in 3D Cartesian
20 % coordinates, and gives them in (x,y,z) format.
21 %
22 % Usage:
23 %
24 % [does_line_intersect_plane,...
25 % does_line_coincide_with_plane,...
26 % intersection_point_vec,...
27 % line_intersects_triangle] =...
28 % line_intersects_plane(line_mat,plane_mat);
29
30 % Find the normal to the surface of the plane.
31
32 plane_21_vec = diff(flipud(plane_mat(1:2,:)),1,1) ;
33

                                       759
34 plane_23_vec = diff(plane_mat(2:3,:),1,1) ;
35
36 cross_21_to_23_vec = cross_product(plane_21_vec,plane_23_vec) ;
37
38 norm_21_to_23_vec = cross_21_to_23_vec / magnitude(cross_21_to_23_vec) ;
39
40 % Find the angle between the normal and the line.
41
42 line_dir_vec = diff(line_mat,1,1) ;
43
44 norm_line_dir_vec = line_dir_vec / magnitude(line_dir_vec) ;
45
46 theta_from_normal_to_line_dir =
acos(dot_product(norm_21_to_23_vec,norm_line_dir_vec)) ;
47
48 tol = 1e-14 ;
49
50 % If this angle is pi/2....
51 %if theta_from_normal_to_line_dir == pi/2
52 if abs( theta_from_normal_to_line_dir - (pi/2) ) < tol
53 % ...the line is parallel to the plane, and must either lie entirely within
54 % the plane, or intersect it nowhere.
55
56 % disp(' ')
57 % disp('The line is parallel to the plane.')
58 % disp('Now determining if the line is coincident with the plane....')
59
60 % Find the vector difference between one point in the plane, and one
61 % point on the line.
62
63 p0_minus_l0_vec = plane_mat(1,:) - line_mat(1,:) ;
64
65 % Find the dot product of this vector and the normal vector.
66
67 dot_of_diff_and_normal = dot_product(p0_minus_l0_vec,norm_21_to_23_vec) ;
68
69 %if abs(dot_of_diff_and_normal) <= 1e-10
70 if dot_of_diff_and_normal == 0
71 %disp(' ')
72 %disp('The line is completely within the plane.')
73
74 does_line_intersect_plane = 1 ;
75 does_line_coincide_with_plane = 1 ;
76 intersection_point_vec = [] ;
77 line_intersects_triangle = 1 ;
78
79 else
80 % disp(' ')
81 % disp('The line is completely outside the plane.')
82
83 does_line_intersect_plane = 0 ;
84 does_line_coincide_with_plane = 0 ;
85 intersection_point_vec = [] ;
86 line_intersects_triangle = 0 ;
87
88 end
89
90 % Otherwise...
                                       760
91 else
92
93 % ...the line must intersect the plane at exactly one point. The problem
94 % then becomes one of determining if the line intersects the plane...
95 %
96 % a) within the triangle specified by the three points given;
97 %
98 % or
99 %
100 % b) outside the triangle specified by those points.
101
102 %disp(' ')
103 %disp('The line intersects the plane at exactly one point.')
104 %disp('Now checking if that point lies within the triangle defining the
plane....')
105
106 does_line_intersect_plane = 1 ;
107 does_line_coincide_with_plane = 0 ;
108
109 line_T_mat = line_mat.';
110
111 plane_T_mat = plane_mat.';
112
113 t_num_pre_mat = horzcat(plane_T_mat,line_T_mat(:,1)) ;
114
115 t_num_mat = vertcat(ones(1,4),t_num_pre_mat) ;
116
117 t_den_pre_mat = horzcat(plane_T_mat,diff(line_T_mat,1,2));
118
119 t_den_mat = vertcat([1,1,1,0],t_den_pre_mat);
120
121 t = -det(t_num_mat)/det(t_den_mat) ;
122
123 x_intersect = line_mat(1,1) + ( (line_mat(2,1)-line_mat(1,1)) * t ) ;
124 y_intersect = line_mat(1,2) + ( (line_mat(2,2)-line_mat(1,2)) * t ) ;
125 z_intersect = line_mat(1,3) + ( (line_mat(2,3)-line_mat(1,3)) * t ) ;
126
127 %line_mat = line_mat
128
129 %plane_mat = plane_mat
130
131 intersection_point_vec = [x_intersect,y_intersect,z_intersect] ;
132
133 triangle_x_range_vec = [min(plane_mat(:,1)),max(plane_mat(:,1))] ;
134
135 triangle_y_range_vec = [min(plane_mat(:,2)),max(plane_mat(:,2))] ;
136
137 triangle_z_range_vec = [min(plane_mat(:,3)),max(plane_mat(:,3))] ;
138
139 x_intersect_in_triangle_x_range = and( x_intersect >=
triangle_x_range_vec(1,1),
x_intersect <= triangle_x_range_vec(1,2) ) ;
140
141 y_intersect_in_triangle_y_range = and( y_intersect >=
triangle_y_range_vec(1,1),
y_intersect <= triangle_y_range_vec(1,2) ) ;
142

                                       761
143 z_intersect_in_triangle_z_range = and( z_intersect >=
triangle_z_range_vec(1,1),
z_intersect <= triangle_z_range_vec(1,2) ) ;
144
145 line_intersects_triangle = all([x_intersect_in_triangle_x_range,
y_intersect_in_triangle_y_range,z_intersect_in_triangle_z_range]) ;
146
147 end
148
149 end

                                       762
CA6.dd Right Triangle with Quasi Hyperbola

Filename: right_triangle_with_quasi_hyperbola.m


1 function [x_intersect_vec,y_intersect_vec] =
right_triangle_with_quasi_hyperbola(l_minor,
l_major,num_line_segments)
2 %
3 % Usage:
4 %
5 % [x_intersect_vec,y_intersect_vec] = ...
6 % right_triangle_with_quasi_hyperbola(l_minor,l_major,num_line_segments) ;
7
8 % Draw the right triangle.
9
10 x_major_vec = [0,l_major] ;
11 y_major_vec = [0,0] ;
12
13 plot(x_major_vec,y_major_vec, 'b');
14
15 grid
16 axis equal
17 hold on
18
19 x_minor_vec = [l_major,l_major] ;
20 y_minor_vec = [0,l_minor] ;
21
22 plot(x_minor_vec,y_minor_vec, 'b') ;
23
24 x_hypotenuse = [0,l_major] ;
25 y_hypotenuse = [0,l_minor] ;
26
27 plot(x_hypotenuse,y_hypotenuse, 'b') ;
28
29 x_bisect = [0, l_major] ;
30 y_bisect = [0, l_minor/2] ;
31
32 plot(x_bisect,y_bisect, 'c') ;
33
34 % Create a vector that describes the points along the major leg where the
35 % line segments will originate from.
36
37 A_x_vec = 0:(l_major-0)/(num_line_segments+1):l_major ;
38
39 A_y_vec = zeros(1,max(size(A_x_vec))) ;
40
41 % Create a vector that describes the points along the hypotenuse where the
42 % line segments will go to.
43 %
44 % As was the case with the A points, the C points will need to be evenly
45 % spaced along their part of the right triangle, i.e. the hypotenuse.
46
47 C_x_vec = A_x_vec ;
48
49 C_y_vec = ( l_minor / l_major ) .* C_x_vec ;
50
                                       763
51 % Plot the A and C points.
52
53 plot(A_x_vec,A_y_vec, 'k.')
54
55 plot(C_x_vec,C_y_vec, 'k.')
56
57 % Draw the line segments running between the A and C points.
58
59 C_x_new_vec = fliplr(C_x_vec) ;
60
61 C_y_new_vec = fliplr(C_y_vec) ;
62
63 for line_seg_itr = 1:max(size(A_x_vec))
64 AC_x_vec = [A_x_vec(1,line_seg_itr),C_x_new_vec(1,line_seg_itr)] ;
65 AC_y_vec = [A_y_vec(1,line_seg_itr),C_y_new_vec(1,line_seg_itr)] ;
66 plot(AC_x_vec,AC_y_vec, 'r-')
67 end
68
69 % Plot the midpoints of these line segments.
70
71 %AC_x_mat = [ A_x_vec; C_x_new_vec ] ;
72
73 %AC_y_mat = [ A_y_vec; C_y_new_vec ] ;
74
75 %midpoint_x_vec = mean(AC_x_mat,1) ;
76 %midpoint_y_vec = mean(AC_y_mat,1) ;
77
78 %plot(midpoint_x_vec,midpoint_y_vec,'g*') ;
79
80 % Plot the intersection points of adjacent line segments.
81
82 x_intersect_vec = [] ;
83
84 y_intersect_vec = [] ;
85
86 for intersect_itr = 2:max(size(A_x_vec))-2
87 m_1 = ( C_y_new_vec(1,intersect_itr) - A_y_vec(1,intersect_itr) ) / (
C_x_new_vec(1,
intersect_itr) - A_x_vec(1,intersect_itr) ) ;
88 m_2 = ( C_y_new_vec(1,intersect_itr+1) - A_y_vec(1,intersect_itr+1) ) / (
C_x_new_vec
(1,intersect_itr+1) - A_x_vec(1,intersect_itr+1) ) ;
89
90 y_term = A_y_vec(1,intersect_itr+1) - A_y_vec(1,intersect_itr) ;
91
92 mx_term = ( m_1 * A_x_vec(1,intersect_itr) ) - ( m_2 *
A_x_vec(1,intersect_itr+1) )
;
93
94 x_intersect = ( y_term + mx_term ) / ( m_1 - m_2 ) ;
95
96 x_intersect_vec = [x_intersect_vec,x_intersect] ;
97
98 y_intersect = ( m_1 * ( x_intersect - A_x_vec(1,intersect_itr) ) ) + A_y_vec
(1,intersect_itr) ;
99
100 y_intersect_vec = [y_intersect_vec,y_intersect] ;
101
                                       764
102 end
103
104 plot(x_intersect_vec, y_intersect_vec, 'g.') ;
105
106 end

CA6.ee Square Annular Toroid Symmetric Around the Z-axis

6 % The purpose of this function is to generate the Cartesian meshgrids
7 % that describe a square annular toroid, which is totally symmetric

outer_x ;

outer_x ;
28

+half_length_of_square_side ;
34

half_length_of_square_side ;

38

[x_outer_half_side_vec,x_upper_side_vec,x_inner_half_side_vec,
x_inner_half_side_vec,x_lower_side_vec,x_outer_half_side_vec ] ;
42

y_upper_side_vec,fliplr(y_upper_half_vec),

Filename: circular_toroid.m

CODING APPENDIX.7 Coding Appendix Chapter 7

This is a collection of all the MATLAB code used in Chapter 7.

CA7.a Calculate Torque on Frustrum

Filename: integrated_torque_on_frustum_as_fxn_of_z_offset.m


1 function [h_cone,integrated_torque_vec] = ...
2 integrated_torque_on_frustum_as_fxn_of_z_offset(z_offset_vec, ...
3 r_inlet,r_throat,l_inlet, ...
4 dynamic_pressure)
5 %
6 % Usage: Note that in this function, n_theta must be set manually inside
7 % the function itself.
8 %
9 % [h_cone,integrated_torque_vec] = ...
10 % integrated_torque_on_frustum_as_fxn_of_z_offset(z_offset_vec,...
11 % r_inlet,r_throat,l_inlet,...
12 % dynamic_pressure) ;
13
14 theta_cone_half_angle = atan( (r_inlet-r_throat) / l_inlet ) ;
15
16 h_cone = r_inlet * cot(theta_cone_half_angle) ;
17
18 theta_min_vec = atan(r_throat./(l_inlet+z_offset_vec)) ;
19
20 theta_max_vec = atan(r_inlet./(z_offset_vec)) ;
21
22 integral_1_vec = zeros(1,max(size(z_offset_vec))) ;
23
24 integral_2_vec = zeros(1,max(size(z_offset_vec))) ;
25
26 n_theta = 100 ;
27
28 for integral_itr = 1:1:max(size(z_offset_vec))
29
30 theta_vec = theta_min_vec(1,integral_itr) : ((theta_max_vec(1,integral_itr))-
theta_min_vec
(1,integral_itr))/(n_theta - 1) : theta_max_vec(1,integral_itr) ;
31
32
33 pre_integral_1_vec = ((sin(theta_vec).*cos(theta_vec))./((sin
(theta_vec+theta_cone_half_angle)).^3)) ;
34
35 integral_1_vec(1,integral_itr) = trapz(theta_vec,pre_integral_1_vec) ;
36
37
38 pre_integral_2_vec = ((sin(theta_vec).*sin(theta_vec))./((sin
(theta_vec+theta_cone_half_angle)).^3)) ;
39
40 integral_2_vec(1,integral_itr) = trapz(theta_vec,pre_integral_2_vec) ;
41

                                         775
42 end
43
44 integral_term_1_vec = cos(theta_cone_half_angle) .* integral_1_vec ;
45
46 integral_term_2_vec = -sin(theta_cone_half_angle) .* integral_2_vec ;
47
48 integrated_torque_vec = ( 4 * pi * dynamic_pressure *
((sin(theta_cone_half_angle))^5) ) *
( (z_offset_vec+h_cone) .^3 ) .* ( integral_term_1_vec + integral_term_2_vec ) ;
49
50 end
